1001 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gonzalez


No. 3-06-0654 consolidated with No. 3-06-0655


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


388 Ill. App. 3d 1003; 906 N.E.2d 34; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 146; 329 Ill. Dec. 189



March 27, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Henry County, Illinois. No. 06-CF-111. Honorable Larry S. Vandersnick, Judge, Presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Henry County, Illinois. No. 06-CF-81. Honorable Larry S. Vandersnick, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants in separate cases were charged with aggravated DUI under 625 ILCS 5/11-501(d)(1)(G) and (H) (2006). The Henry County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted their motions to dismiss on the ground that the subsections were not embodied in the statute at the time the offenses were alleged to have been committed. The People appealed, and the cases were consolidated for the purpose of appeal.


OVERVIEW: The subsections were added to the statute by 2005 Ill. Laws 329. The court stated that it appeared that the trial court had found that 2005 Ill. Laws 329 had been superseded by 2005 Ill. Laws 609, which also amended the statute. The court stated that it was convinced that the trial court had not found 2005 Ill. Laws 329 to be unconstitutional, but had found it inoperative based upon principles of statutory construction. The court stated that the law was well settled in favor of harmonizing enactments passed in the same legislative session. Here, the enactments could be harmonized, and the trial court erred in not giving effect to both. The legislature intended to make two distinct changes to the statute. The intent of 2005 Ill. Laws 329 was to add two new offenses to aggravated DUI, whereas 2005 Ill. Laws 609 amended the statute to provide that if a defendant was convicted of aggravated DUI because his DUI was the cause of the death of one or more persons, the defendant would be sentenced to a term of imprisonment, unless the trial court determined that extraordinary circumstances required probation. Thus, the legislative intent of each enactment was not inconsistent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order invalidating the statutory provisions at issue. It remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with this disposition.

 

1002 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Cwik v. Topinka


Nos. 1-07-2368 & 1-07-2786 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


389 Ill. App. 3d 21; 905 N.E.2d 300; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 116; 328 Ill. Dec. 766



March 9, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 1, 2009.
Appeal granted by Cwik v. Giannoulis, 232 Ill. 2d 578, 910 N.E.2d 1126, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 564, 331 Ill. Dec. 370 (2009)
Affirmed by Cwik v. Giannoulias, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 672 (Ill., May 20, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 05 CH 09872. Honorable Phillip L. Bronstein, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered, cause reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied appellant state officials' motion to dismiss a Uniform Disposition of Unclaimed Property Act (765 ILCS 1025 et seq. (2004)) complaint filed by appellee owners. Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 308 certified questions were: whether retention of interest earned on property held by the State was a taking for which compensation was due, and whether compensation was measured by the interest earned on the property.


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged that 765 ILCS 1025/15 was a taking without compensation in violation of Ill. Const. art. I, § 15; U.S. Const. amend. V and XIV; and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court found that interest was earned on the unclaimed property because the Treasurer had to deposit the money in an authorized bank, savings and loan association or credit union. Therefore, the payment would not be a money judgment against the State because the source of the interest monies would be the institution where the funds were invested. Property remitted to the State under the Act was "presumptively abandoned," not "abandoned," and the State acted as a property's custodian, not its owner. Therefore, the Treasurer's argument that abandonment entitled it to the interest generated after it was remitted to the State lacked merit. However, there was no evidence that the owner's property was producing any interest until the Treasurer took possession of it under the Act. The State's gain did not establish a loss on the part of the owners. As such, the owners had no claim for a taking for which compensation was due; having no claim, they could not represent the interests of a class.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified questions in the negative, reversed the order granting certification and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1003 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Hanna v. City of Chicago


No. 1-07-3548


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


388 Ill. App. 3d 909; 907 N.E.2d 390; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 98; 329 Ill. Dec. 799



March 6, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 13, 2009.
Appeal denied by Hanna v. City of Chicago, 232 Ill. 2d 580, 910 N.E.2d 1127, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 612, 331 Ill. Dec. 371 (May 28, 2009)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Mrowka v. City of Chicago, 2013 IL App (1st) 121701-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2168 (Sept. 26, 2013)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Hanna v. City of Chi., 2017 IL App (1st) 160493-U, 2017 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1070 (May 31, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 06 CH 19422. Honorable Sophia H. Hall, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners filed suit against defendants, a city, a commission on landmarks, and city officials, alleging that Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code §§ 2-120-580 to 2-120-920 was invalid on its face in violation of Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 and art. IV, § 1. The owners challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion to dismiss the city, commission, and officials filed under 735 ILCS 5/2-615 (2006).


OVERVIEW: The commission recommended certain areas as landmark districts, and the city council designated the areas as such. The owners' properties were in those areas. The appellate court held that the allegations in the owners' complaint that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous were sufficient to establish a cause of action. The terms "value," "important," "significant," and "unique" in Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 2-120-620 (2000) were vague, ambiguous, and overly broad. The city offered no criteria by which a person of common intelligence could determine from the face of the ordinance whether a building or district would be deemed to have value or importance or whether a person would be deemed to have a "special interest" in neighborhood preservation. The owners adequately stated a cause of action in the count of their complaint alleging that the ordinance permitted an improper delegation of authority. The commission performed a declaratory function. Under the ordinance, the commission could make a recommendation to the city council, and the city council was not required to review the commission's recommendations before they became final.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the owners' complaint and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1004 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Ill. Campaign for Political Reform v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections


No. 1-06-1694


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


388 Ill. App. 3d 517; 904 N.E.2d 996; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 93; 328 Ill. Dec. 486



March 4, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 13, 2009.
Appeal denied by Ill. Campaign for Political Reform v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections, 232 Ill. 2d 580, 910 N.E.2d 1127, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 521, 331 Ill. Dec. 371 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for Review from the Illinois State Board of Elections. No. 05 CD 003.
Ill. Campaign for Political Reform v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections, 382 Ill. App. 3d 51, 886 N.E.2d 1220, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 269, 320 Ill. Dec. 151 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant objectors filed a complaint against appellee coalition in the Illinois State Board of Elections, alleging violations of the campaign disclosure requirements of the Illinois Election Code, 10 ILCS 5/9-1 et seq. (2004). The Board dismissed the complaint. The objectors appealed pursuant to 10 ILCS 5/9-22 (2004).


OVERVIEW: The Board's dismissal order was not based on the merits of the complaint, but on the Board's deadlock vote and consequent inability to achieve the statutorily-mandated five-member vote to enable the Board to find the matter to have been filed on justifiable grounds and order a public hearing under 10 ILCS 5/1A-7 and 10 ILCS 5/9-21 (2004). On appeal, the court found that the members of the Board voting to dismiss the complaint did not clearly err in determining that the complaint was not filed on justifiable grounds. The court also rejected the objectors' constitutional arguments that the Board's deadlock vote violated the objectors' rights to meaningful judicial review and protection against arbitrary government actions. Accordingly, the Board failed to determine that the complaint was filed on justifiable grounds when it voted four-to-four on that question. The Board, therefore, complied with the clear directive of § 9-21 by dismissing the complaint after failing to determine that it was filed on justifiable grounds.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the complaint was affirmed.

People v. Davis


No. 1-07-0398


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


388 Ill. App. 3d 869; 904 N.E.2d 149; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 76; 328 Ill. Dec. 387



February 25, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended March 20, 2009. Released for Publication April 13, 2009.
Appeal denied by People v. Davis, 233 Ill. 2d 571, 919 N.E.2d 357, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1450, 335 Ill. Dec. 638 (2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Davis v. Illinois, 130 S. Ct. 1707, 176 L. Ed. 2d 195, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 2117 (U.S., 2010)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by People v. Davis, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 3233, 2012 IL App (1st) 112577U (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Marjorie C. Laws, Judge Presiding.
People v. Davis, 307 Ill. App. 3d 1067, 760 N.E.2d 1059, 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 4270, 260 Ill. Dec. 286 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which made a second-stage dismissal of his supplemental postconviction petition, filed under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 ILCS 5/122-1 (2002) et seq. Defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder, two counts of attempted first-degree murder, and home invasion. The case was transferred to the criminal courts.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment for the murder convictions and lesser concurrent terms on the others. On appeal of the underlying judgment, defendant, relying on specific case law, asserted that the mandatory sentence of natural life in prison, as applied to himself, a 14-year-old juvenile convicted based on an accountability theory, was unconstitutional. The court held that the case law relied upon by defendant did not prohibit the imposition of a natural life sentence for all juveniles or for all juveniles convicted based on a theory of accountability. The court held that the case was fact specific and did not create a new substantive rule warranting retroactive application. The court found no merit to defendant's contention that the indictment did not place him on notice that he faced the possibility of a mandatory natural life sentence as the State did not charge him with a higher classification of murder because of a prior conviction, therefore, the State was not required to notify him of the sentence he would receive upon conviction. The court further held that retained postconviction counsel satisfied the requirements of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1006 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Simmons


No. 1-06-3114


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


388 Ill. App. 3d 599; 903 N.E.2d 437; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 68; 328 Ill. Dec. 50



February 20, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Publication allowed February 17, 2009. Released for Publication March 25, 2009.
Appeal denied by People v. Simmons, 232 Ill. 2d 593, 910 N.E.2d 1131, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 617, 331 Ill. Dec. 375 (2009)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Simmons v. Yurkovich, 2012 U.S. App. LEXIS 25753 (7th Cir. Ill., Dec. 18, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 90 CR 24997. Honorable Nicholas Ford, Judge Presiding.
People v. Simmons, 294 Ill. App. 3d 1103, 721 N.E.2d 853, 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 1507, 242 Ill. Dec. 574 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pled guilty to and was sentenced for murder and armed robbery, he sought leave in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) to file a third successive petition for relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act (725 ILCS 5/122-1 et seq. (2004)). The trial court denied leave, holding defendant could not satisfy the cause-and-prejudice test. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said Rivera, holding partial summary dismissal of a postconviction petition was error, let him seek postconviction review, as his first postconviction petition was partially summarily dismissed. The appellate court disagreed. The partial summary dismissal of his first petition was affirmed over three years before Rivera was issued, which stated a new rule that did not apply retroactively to defendant's successive petition, since, before Rivera, Illinois' lower courts disagreed as to the propriety of partial summary dismissals of postconviction petitions. Rivera's reliance on prior appellate court decisions did not show it did not state a new rule, so it could not be retroactively applied to invalidate the partial summary dismissal of defendant's first petition, and he could not use it to meet the required "prejudice" prong of 725 ILCS 5/122-1(f) (2004) to obtain leave to file his successive petition. He could not base his petition on a freestanding actual innocence claim because he presented no supporting new evidence and made this claim in his first petition, merely contesting his plea's voluntariness without contesting whether he committed the underlying crimes.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1007 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Madigan v. Leavell


NO. 4-08-0019


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


388 Ill. App. 3d 283; 905 N.E.2d 849; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 106; 329 Ill. Dec. 11



February 18, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 07CH707. Honorable Leslie J. Graves, Judge Presiding.
People ex rel. Madigan v. Leavell, 228 Ill. 2d 552, 886 N.E.2d 1027, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 457, 319 Ill. Dec. 903 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Illinois filed a complaint against appellee supply company owner in the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), for violations of the Illinois Oil and Gas Act, 225 ILCS 725/1 through 28.1 (2006). The trial court granted the owner's motion for change of venue under 735 ILCS 5/2-101 (2006), or, in the alternative, to transfer on the basis of forum non conveniens. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State of Illinois alleged that the owner violated orders and a final administrative decision by the Illinois Department of Natural Resources regarding oil production and injection wells. The State also indicted that venue was appropriate in Sangamon County based on the Department's issuance of final administrative decisions to the owner in that county. The owner contended that venue was proper in White County. On appeal, the court found that the specific venue provision of § 11 of the Illinois Oil and Gas Act, 225 ILCS 725/1 through 28.1 (2006), was the applicable venue provision, and thus Sangamon County was a proper venue under 225 ILCS 725/11 (2006). However, because part of the subject land and some of the activity was in White County, that county was also a proper place of venue for the entire action under § 11. Accordingly, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by transferring the case to White County under the doctrine of forum non conveniens because, considering the totality of the circumstances and all of the relevant factors, the inconvenience of Sangamon County greatly outweighed the State's venue choice and a transfer to White County was strongly favored.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1008 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Madigan v. Excavating & Lowboy Servs.


1-07-3345


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


388 Ill. App. 3d 554; 902 N.E.2d 1218; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 49; 327 Ill. Dec. 832



February 13, 2009, Decided 
February 13, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 25, 2009.
Appeal denied by People ex rel. Madigan v. Excavating & Lowboy Servs., 232 Ill. 2d 595, 910 N.E.2d 1132, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 478, 331 Ill. Dec. 376 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 04 CH 0863, No. 04 CH 9347, No. 07 CH 11709 (Consolidated). The Honorable Stuart E. Palmer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed appellant City's third-party complaint against appellees, the Illinois Department of Transportation (IDOT) and its former secretary, finding that sovereign immunity barred relief and that the complaint did not state a claim. The City appealed, claiming in part, that the State consented to suit based on the Illinois Environmental Protection (EP) Act, 415 ILCS 5/1 et seq. (2004).


OVERVIEW: A matter of first impression was presented as to whether the EP Act contained an exception to sovereign immunity. The court found that the EP Act conferred a liberal grant of authority for suits against those alleged to have harmed or compromised the environment. There was nothing unclear, contradictory or in conflict between or among the EP Act, the State Lawsuit Immunity Act, 745 ILCS 5/1, and the Court of Claims Act, 705 ILCS 505/1 et seq. The EP Act's use of the phrase "may sue" as to third parties did not confer jurisdiction in any forum or evince legislative intent mandating that the EP Act contradict, override, or supercede the other Acts regarding jurisdiction. The State did not consent to be sued under the EP Act; nor did it waive sovereign immunity, vesting a circuit court with jurisdiction. The interplay of the EP Act with the other Acts guided the conclusion that dismissal was proper for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Dismissal as to IDOT applied equally to the secretary. There was no inequity in requiring the City to seek relief in the court of claims. A traditional reluctance of that court to grant injunctive relief was not tantamount to its unavailability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal.

 

1009 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Olsen


No. 2-07-0894


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


388 Ill. App. 3d 704; 903 N.E.2d 778; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 45; 328 Ill. Dec. 118



February 11, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 10, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 04-DT-5581. Honorable John J. Kinsella, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of DuPage County (Illinois) convicted defendant of driving with a blood alcohol level of 0.08 or more, a violation of 625 ILCS 5/11-501(a)(1) (2004). On appeal, defendant argued that: (1) the State did not lay a proper foundation for admitting the blood test results; (2) the trial court erred in taking judicial notice of Ill. Admin. Code tit. 20, § 1286.40; and (3) he was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: The court reviewed the interpretation of 625 ILCS 5/11-501.4 de novo and found that the trial court's ruling that the State satisfied the foundational requirements to admit defendant's blood test was not an abuse of discretion. Defendant received emergency medical treatment, and the blood test was ordered in the ordinary course of providing the medical treatment, rather than at the request of law enforcement; and in the normal course of business, the hospital's lab tested all blood, defendant's blood test results looked like they came from that lab, and the results were entered in his chart shortly after he arrived at the hospital. The Department of State Police was authorized to pass Ill. Admin. Code tit. 20, § 1286.40, subjecting blood serum test results to a particular conversion factor. Because the Department intended to prescribe a valid regulation, the court construed the phrase "will be" as permissive rather than mandatory, rendering the regulation constitutional and permitting the trial court to take judicial notice of the regulation. Based on the foregoing, defendant's sufficiency of the evidence argument failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

1010 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cowart


No. 1-07-0053


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


389 Ill. App. 3d 1046; 907 N.E.2d 1; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 47; 329 Ill. Dec. 682



February 11, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 3, 2009.
Substituted opinion at, Modified by, Rehearing denied by People v. Cowart, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1724 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., May 13, 2009)
Appeal denied by People v. Cowart, 233 Ill. 2d 571, 919 N.E.2d 357, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1746, 335 Ill. Dec. 638 (2009)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Cowart, 2015 Ill. App. LEXIS 95 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Feb. 17, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 94 CR 29080, 94 CR 25257, 94 CR 25258, 94 CR 25259, 94 CR 25260, 94 CR 25261, 94 CR 28843, 94 CR 28844. Honorable Lon William Shultz Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded; sentences modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate pled guilty to eight acts of home invasion, one residential burglary, four aggravated criminal sexual assaults, and five attempted aggravated criminal sexual assaults, and was sentenced. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) then denied the inmate's motion to withdraw his plea, and summarily dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief against appellee State pursuant to 725 ILCS 5/122-1 (2004). The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate first argued that four of his sentences exceeded the statutory maximum for his offenses, and that the sentence terms in excess of the statutory maximum were void. The State conceded the merit of the inmate's arguments regarding these sentences. The inmate also asserted that two home invasion convictions for a single break-in was an unconstitutional violation of the one-act, one-crime rule. The appellate court found that the inmate's petition was sufficiently specific to communicate the legal principles supporting his constitutional claim, and rejected the State's claim that its lack of detail was a proper basis for its dismissal. Since the inmate's prior summary proceeding in the appellate court addressing Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d) compliance was the equivalent of filing no appeal, he did not forfeit post-conviction review of his allegations of violation of the one-act, one-crime principle. The petition made a sufficient allegation of a deprivation of constitutional rights to survive first-stage review under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 ILCS 5/122-1 (2004). Accordingly, the petition was neither frivolous nor patently without merit.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the petition was reversed and the entire petition was remanded for further proceedings under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act. The sentences imposed in three of the cases were reduced to 30 years, and the sentence in a fourth case was reduced to 60 years.

 

1011 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Morgan


NO. 4-07-0653


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


388 Ill. App. 3d 252; 901 N.E.2d 1049; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 46; 327 Ill. Dec. 316



February 9, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County. No. 07CF55. Honorable Harold J. Frobish, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with offenses including unlawful possession of a controlled substance (a substance containing cocaine) (720 ILCS 570/402(c) (2006)) arising out of an incident and the trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress, finding police officers entered defendant's home on the basis of an invalid warrant and without consent. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State conceded that defendant's arrest on an inactive warrant violated the Fourth Amendment, but argued that the good-faith exception to the exclusionary rule should apply. The appeals court found that the State failed to meet its burden of proof that the good-faith exception of 725 ILCS 5/114-12(b)(1) (2006) should apply, and that exclusion was the proper remedy. The case involved a situation where the officers knowingly obtained an up-to-three-day-old list and did not verify the continued validity of defendant's warrant, even though their standard police procedure was to obtain a current list. The officers provided no explanation during their testimony why they accepted an old list, failed to request a newer list, and failed to verify the continued validity of the warrants on the list. The State also argued that exigent circumstances justified officers' warrantless entry into defendant's residence. However, the record was devoid of any facts supporting an officer's concern for safety, and the record was devoid of any indication that the officers had probable cause to believe defendant committed or was committing an offense. The motion to suppress was properly granted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1012 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Managers of Wespark Condo. Ass'n v. Neumann Homes, Inc.


No. 1-07-1307


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


388 Ill. App. 3d 129; 903 N.E.2d 39; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 25; 327 Ill. Dec. 942



January 29, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 25, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Brigid M. McGrath, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered; order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Construction problems led plaintiff condominium association to sue defendant builder. The builder filed a third-party complaint against third-party defendant subcontractor. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied the subcontractor's motion to dismiss the third-party complaint as untimely, but later granted the subcontractor's motion to certify for immediate appeal two questions concerning the interpretation of 735 ILCS 5/13-204 (2006).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that a failure to comply with 735 ILCS 5/13-217 (1994) was not fatal, because 735 ILCS 5/13-204 provided another opportunity to file an action. However, in order to do so, the party seeking to proceed with a claim under 735 ILCS 5/13-204 had to comply with the limitations periods under both 735 ILCS 5/13-204(b) and (c). In addition, a defendant could not file a timely action for contribution or indemnity under 735 ILCS 5/13-204 unless the plaintiff in the underlying action could have, at the time it sued the defendant, filed a timely action against the parties from whom the defendant sought contribution or indemnity. In the instant case, the third-party complaint was untimely, under 735 ILCS 5/13-204(c), because when the association sued the builder, the time had expired for the association to file a timely complaint against the subcontractor. Thus, the builder was barred from suing the subcontractor for contribution or indemnity because the builder did not satisfy both limitations of 735 ILCS 5/13-204(b), (c). Also, a standstill agreement in which the subcontractor did not participate could not affect its rights as protected by 735 ILCS 5/13-204(c).


OUTCOME: The certified questions were answered, the order of the trial court denying the subcontractor's motion to dismiss was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions to dismiss as untimely the builder's third-party complaint against the subcontractor.

 

1013 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Vill. of Bensenville v. City of Chicago


No. 2-08-0769


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


389 Ill. App. 3d 446; 906 N.E.2d 556; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 7; 329 Ill. Dec. 358



January 7, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 3, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Vill. of Bensenville v. City of Chi., 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1741 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., May 27, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. Nos. 07-CH-1620, 07-CH-2995. Honorable Kenneth L. Popejoy, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a village and its residents, sued defendant city in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) for declaratory and injunctive relief regarding the city's acquisition of village property, for common-law fraud and unjust enrichment, for a claim that a village ordinance governed certain demolitions, and for public nuisance. After temporarily granting an injunction, the trial court dismissed the complaint. The plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city acquired village land to expand its airport. The appellate court held it was no abuse of discretion to dismiss, under 735 ILCS 5/2-619(a)(3) (2006), a claim that the city did not show acquiring the land was necessary because this was pending before another judge, as to plaintiffs' property, and they did not show they could intervene as to other land, nor could they attack condemnation judgments as to those properties. A request to declare a village ordinance governed any demolition was dismissed under § 2-619 because state law preempted the ordinance. A fraud claim was dismissed under 735 ILCS 5/2-615 (2006) because no influence of plaintiffs by misrepresentations to third parties or physical harm were alleged. An unjust enrichment claim was dismissed because it did not say how acquiring other owners' property denied plaintiffs a benefit. The trial court erred in dissolving a preliminary injunction because it was not shown that agency oversight was an adequate alternative to an injunction. The trial court also erred in relying on administrative authority because no agency involvement was shown, and an administrative remedy did not relieve a court of its judicial function.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal, with prejudice, of plaintiffs' complaint was affirmed, but the trial court's termination of a preliminary injunction was reversed, and the matter was remanded to reanalyze the propriety of injunctive relief.

 

1014 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Angarola


Nos. 2-07-0396 & 2-07-1062 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


387 Ill. App. 3d 732; 900 N.E.2d 1281; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 2; 326 Ill. Dec. 1034



January 6, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 3, 2009.
Rehearing denied by People v. Angarola, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1726 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Feb. 3, 2009)
Appeal denied by People v. Angarola, 235 Ill. 2d 590, 924 N.E.2d 456, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 134, 338 Ill. Dec. 250 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 06-CF-1499. Honorable George J. Bakalis, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 2--07--0396, Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions. No. 2--07--1062, Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) of two counts of forgery, under 720 ILCS 5/17-3(a)(1) and (2) (2006), and one count of deceptive practices, under 720 ILCS 5/17-1(B)(d) (2006), and his postconviction petition, under 725 ILCS 5/122-1 et seq. (2006), was dismissed. He appealed his convictions and the dismissal of his petition, and the appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said counsel ineffectively conceded his guilt of forgery. The appellate court disagreed because he could have been convicted of theft and forgery, as forgery required proof of (1) making a fake check or (2) issuing the check knowing it was fake, while theft required proof he knowingly obtained control over property by deception, 720 ILCS 5/16-1(a)(2) (2006), so conceding guilt of forgery did not fail to subject the State's theft case to adversarial testing. The one-act, one-crime rule required vacating his deceptive practices conviction because it was based on the same act as his forgery convictions, but separate forgery convictions for creating and delivering a fake check were not barred. One charge required proof of making the check purportedly by another or with the authority of one who gave no such authority, while the other charge required proof of issuing the check knowing it was fake. Defendant did each act, supporting separate convictions. It was no error to dismiss his postconviction petition for mootness, since he could raise his claims in the appeal he was allowed to file, as mootness and res judicata were closely related.


OUTCOME: Defendant's forgery convictions were affirmed, but his deceptive practices conviction was vacated, and the matter was remanded for resentencing based on the proper convictions. The first-stage dismissal of defendant's postconviction petition was affirmed. Because he was convicted of two forgery counts, but sentenced for one forgery count and one theft count, the discrepancy was to be reconciled and defendant resentenced accordingly.

People v. Pace


NOS. 4-08-0026, 4-08-0260 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


386 Ill. App. 3d 1056; 899 N.E.2d 610; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1299; 326 Ill. Dec. 393



December 19, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at, Motion granted by People v. Pace, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1851, 2012 IL App (4th) 100161-U, 2012 IL App (4th) 100161U (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Jersey County. No. 96CF35. Honorable Tim P. Olson, Judge Presiding.
People v. Pace, 182 Ill. 2d 565, 707 N.E.2d 1243, 1999 Ill. LEXIS 288, 236 Ill. Dec. 673 (1999)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order entered by the Circuit Court of Jersey County (Illinois), which denied reinstatement of defendant's pro se petition filed pursuant to the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 ILCS 5/122-1 through 122-8 (1998), after it had been previously dismissed on a voluntary basis without prejudice. Defendant had been convicted of first-degree murder under 720 ILCS 5/9-1(a)(1) (1995).


OVERVIEW: After the trial court determined three allegations in the original petition were of concern, it appointed counsel to represent defendant. However, counsel sought a voluntary dismissal without prejudice after finding no colorable arguments but sought leave to refile if appropriate evidence became available. The trial court denied defendant's request for reinstatement of his petition nine months later. On appeal, the court reversed. While the court did not decide whether defendant's right to reinstatement was absolute, under 725 ILCS 5/122-5 (2006), the trial court had the authority to permit pleading over or the filing of further pleadings, including a post-conviction petition. Whether reinstatement was mandatory or an act of discretion, defendant was entitled to reinstatement under the circumstances because if appointed counsel felt that the arguments lacked merit, he could have sought to withdraw as opposed to dismissing the petition; counsel apparently did not give defendant the option of proceeding pro se. Additionally, the request for reinstatement was within the one-year time period that applied under 735 ILCS 5/13-217 (2006) to the refiling of complaints in civil cases.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Gonzalez

December 12, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 18, 2008. Released for Publication January 29, 2009.
Appeal denied by People v. Gonzalez, 231 Ill. 2d 675, 904 N.E.2d 982, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 668, 328 Ill. Dec. 472 (Mar. 25, 2009)
Post-conviction proceeding at People v. Gonzalez, 2012 IL App (1st) 103498-U, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 221 (Feb. 3, 2012)
Habeas corpus proceeding at United States ex rel. Gonzalez v. Atchison, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 23892 (N.D. Ill., Feb. 20, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 03 CR 135. Honorable James B. Linn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of first-degree murder and personally discharging a firearm which proximately caused the death of the victim. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: As a result of defendant allegedly shooting the victim to death from a vehicle and shooting near two other individuals, defendant was charged with multiple crimes, including first-degree murder and personally discharging a firearm causing the death of a victim. Defendant was convicted by a jury of those two offenses. Defendant alleged on appeal that the trial court failed to take any remedial action when it knew a juror may have fallen asleep, the trial court improperly instructed the jury on felony murder, and that the prosecution made improper closing arguments. The appellate court found that he had not preserved any of the alleged errors for review and that (1) the trial court's instruction to the parties about its observation that a juror may have fallen asleep and that it would consider any motion in that regard was sufficient remedial action, (2) the jury was properly instructed on the felony murder charge because the predicate felony of aggravated discharge of a firearm involved individuals other than the victim, and (3) the prosecution's closing arguments were not shown to be improper, especially since many of comments merely responded to comments made by defense counsel.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Jackson v. Victory Mem. Hosp.


No. 2-07-0525


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


387 Ill. App. 3d 342; 900 N.E.2d 309; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1198; 326 Ill. Dec. 673



December 2, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 06-L-958. Honorable David M. Hall, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that dismissed plaintiff patient's medical malpractice complaint against defendants, a hospital and two doctors. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient filed a medical malpractice action against the two doctors and the hospital. Eventually, the patient moved to voluntarily dismiss her complaint, which the trial court granted. One year later, she refiled her complaint against the two doctors and the hospital. In an attached affidavit, the patient's attorney asserted that he was unable to obtain the medical consultation required by 735 ILCS 5/2-622(a)(1) (2006), because the statute of limitations would hinder the action and, thus, he needed a 90-day extension. Thereafter, the patient requested another extension of time to obtain certain medical record. Instead, the trial court granted the two doctors' motion to dismiss based on the patient not declaring pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-622(a)(2) that she had not previously voluntarily dismissed the action and granted the hospital's motion to dismiss based on res judicata because the patient had voluntarily dismissed her action and had not replead it. The appellate court found that under the version of 735 ILCS 5/2-622(a)(2) in effect, the patient was not required to make that declaration and res judicata did not apply to an action voluntarily dismissed without prejudice.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Shaw


NO. 4-06-0734


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


386 Ill. App. 3d 704; 898 N.E.2d 755; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1188; 325 Ill. Dec. 708



November 26, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Shaw, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 413 (Ill., May 28, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 04CF821. Honorable Theodore E. Paine, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After petitioner inmate's armed robbery convictions were affirmed on direct appeal, the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) dismissed the inmate's Post-Conviction Hearing Act (725 ILCS 5/122-1 through 122-8 (2006)) petition and the warden conducted a 730 ILCS 5/3-6-3(d) (2006) hearing and revoked the inmate's good time credit for having filed a frivolous petition, a violation of Ill. Admin. Code tit. 20, § 504. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the postconviction relief petition failed to state the gist of a constitutional violation and was properly dismissed as frivolous and without merit. There was no violation of confrontation rights under U.S. Const., amend. VI and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, nor ineffective assistance of appellate counsel because 1) a witness's statements about a conversation with a nontestifying witness did not include testimony as to the armed robber's identity, 2) the statements were not inadmissible hearsay or violative of the Confrontation Clause, and 3) counsel could not have been ineffective for failing to raise a nonexistent Confrontation Clause issue. Because armed robbery was not included in 740 ILCS 45/2(c) (2004), the proper amount of a fine assessed was $ 20 pursuant to 725 ILCS 240/10(c)(2) (2004); but, because the imposition of the fine was a judicial function beyond the authority of the circuit clerk, the fine imposed by a clerk had to be vacated. 730 ILCS 5/3-6-3(d) furthered a valid State interest in ensuring that its courts were not overburdened with frivolous suits. The inmate did not exhaust administrative remedies before seeking relief from the warden's action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with directions that the trial court impose the proper Violent Crime Act fine.

Druck v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections


No. 1-08-2440


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


387 Ill. App. 3d 144; 899 N.E.2d 437; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1309; 326 Ill. Dec. 220



November 26, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 16, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 08 CO EL 000008. Honorable Alfred J. Paul, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant candidate sought review of a decision entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which effectively affirmed a decision by appellee, the Illinois State Board of Elections (SBOE), sitting as the State Officers Electoral Board (SOEB), to invalidate the candidate's nominating papers after appellee objector had made objections based on the number of signatures obtained.


OVERVIEW: The candidate, who was a member of the Libertarian party, claimed, inter alia, that the requirements of 10 ILCS 5/10-2, 10-8 (2006) violated his First and Fourteenth Amendment rights and rights under Ill. Const. art. I, §§ 2, 4, 5. On appeal, the court affirmed. While the rights to vote and to associate were fundamental, the State was permitted to impose reasonable restrictions on access to the ballot and had a duty to ensure the electoral process was orderly. The minimum signature requirements in 10 ILCS 5/10-2 for a new party formed in a district were not unconstitutional as the State had a legitimate interest in only putting candidates on the ballot who demonstrated a measurable quantum of support or a level of political viability. The signature requirements were not illusory based on the candidate's claim that they could only be enforced when objections were filed under 10 ILCS 5/10-8 because that provision's plain language indicated that two conditions precedent had to be met before the nominating papers would be deemed valid: the papers had to be filed with the proper election authority under 10 ILCS 5/10-6 and in apparent conformity with the Election Code.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

People v. Williams


No. 1-05-0810


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1135



November 19, 2008, Decided 
November 19, 2008, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by People v. Williams, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 582 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., June 24, 2009)
Substituted opinion at People v. Williams, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 593 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., June 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 98 CR 26083 (04). Honorable Daniel P. Darcy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a joint bench trial, the trial court granted defendant's motion for a directed verdict on a criminal drug conspiracy charge and found defendant guilty of official misconduct. The Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, sentenced defendant to 24 months' probation and 250 hours of community service. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in finding that the State proved that she violated a law, as required for a conviction for official misconduct under 720 ILCS 5/33-3(b) (1998). Defendant, who worked as police dispatcher, argued that the nature of the law she allegedly violated when she communicated information about police activity to a codefendant was simply a rule from an employee manual and not a law as envisioned by the legislature in its enactment of § 33-3(b). The appellate court disagreed. The subject rule was more than a mere rule of employment, but was a village ordinance by a home rule community. The trial court found incredible defendant's claims that she made up the information imparted to a codefendant rather than disseminated confidential information. The appellate court also concluded that § 33-3(b) was not unconstitutional, but clearly prohibited public officers from knowingly performing, in their official capacity, an action known to be forbidden by law. Nor was the law vague, as a person of ordinary intelligence would not have to guess that calling a drug dealer to inform him where police were gathering and conducting surveillance was unlawful.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Stroud


No. 1-05-0683


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1134



November 19, 2008, Decided


NOTICE:

THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Stroud, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 775 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Jan. 27, 2009)
Substituted opinion at People v. Stroud, 392 Ill. App. 3d 776, 911 N.E.2d 1152, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 594, 331 Ill. Dec. 922 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., June 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98 CR 26083. Honorable Daniel P. Darcy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was tried with three co-defendants and found guilty of criminal drug conspiracy, five counts of delivery of more than 100 but less than 400 grams of cocaine, one count of possession of more than 900 grams of cocaine with intent to deliver, and one count of possession of 1 to 15 grams of cocaine with intent to deliver. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced him to concurrent 20 year terms in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court first concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in issuing a wiretap order because the affidavits appended in support of the application showed that other normal investigative procedures, such as use of a confidential informant and garbage seizures, had been tried and failed, appeared unlikely to succeed if tried, or were too dangerous. The appellate court also found no abuse of discretion in the extension orders, as the evidence showed that the calls initially intercepted were insufficient to support the conspiracy charge. The State's violation of 725 ILCS 5/108B-9 (1998) did not necessitate a new trial, as the investigator's voice identification did not rest solely on defendant's admission that it was his voice on the tape but was also based on having listened to the tapes and recognizing defendant's voice. The appellate court also found that evidence that defendant and another agreed to deliver controlled substances, had been transacting business in a standardized manner, and had numerous conversations with the other about the availability and price of drugs was sufficient to support defendant's criminal drug conspiracy conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) adjudicated respondent juvenile a delinquent minor, finding him guilty of criminal sexual assault and attempted robbery, and sentencing him to an indeterminate term to automatically terminate upon the passage of 15 years or respondent attaining the age of 21. Caro ex rel. Taxpayers v. Whitaker


1-06-1243


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


386 Ill. App. 3d 485; 898 N.E.2d 1110; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1071; 325 Ill. Dec. 831



November 4, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 16, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Caro v. Whitaker, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1702 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Jan. 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 06 CH 6527. Honorable James F. Henry, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer filed a lawsuit in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) against defendant Director of the Illinois Department of Public Health, to enjoin disbursement of funds for stem cell research mandated by two executive orders of the Governor of Illinois. The trial court dismissed the lawsuit and ruled that the lawsuit was a nonjusticiable political question, inappropriate for judicial determination. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Governor issued Executive Order 2005-06 creating the Illinois Regenerative Institute for Stem Cell Research which directed the Director of the Illinois Department of Public Health to create an entity to be known as the Illinois Regenerative Medical Institute (IRMI). IRMI was to develop a program which would award grants and loans to medical research facilities for the development of cures based on stem cell research. The taxpayer sought leave to file a taxpayer complaint against the Director only. The taxpayer alleged that Executive Orders 2005-06 and 2006-03 were unconstitutional. The appellate court held it was not possible to grant the taxpayer the relief requested as the court could not prevent what has already been done. The taxpayer had not properly alleged a declaratory judgment action challenging the Governor's authority and the court would have no power to make that declaration. The Director was not the appropriate defendant. As neither the Comptroller, the Treasurer, or the recipients of the grants were named as defendants, the trial court could not grant the taxpayer the relief sought. As the appellate court could not grant the relief sought, the appeal was moot.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his request for summary reversal of his conviction for a probation violation. The State made a request that defendant's probation be voided as an illegal sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been convicted in 2000 on drug charges under 720 ILCS 570/401(d) (2000), 720 ILCS 570/407. Based on defendant's six prior felony convictions, the State argued that defendant should be sentenced to a mandatory Class X prison sentence under 730 ILCS 5/5-5-3(c)(8) (2000); however, the trial court did not address that argument and sentenced defendant to 24 months' probation. In 2001, the State filed a petition for violation of probation based on defendant's arrest for attempted armed robbery and attempted murder; defendant was found guilty in 2005, but the convictions were reversed in 2007 after a violation of probation was found. Defendant's probation period was tolled by the filing of the State's petition under 730 ILCS 5/5-6-4(a) (2000). The remand for resentencing did not constituted double jeopardy as probation was not punishment in the same sense as imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's probation conviction and sentence and remanded the action for resentencing on defendant's original drug conviction.

Chicago Bar Ass'n v. White


No. 1-08-2741


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


386 Ill. App. 3d 955; 898 N.E.2d 1101; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1050; 325 Ill. Dec. 822



October 28, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 19, 2008. Released for Publication December 11, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 08 COEL 11 & 08 COEL 12, Consolidated. Honorable Nathaniel R. Howse, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) disposed of a multicount declaratory judgment action challenging the format and language on an upcoming election ballot for the calling of a constitutional convention by ordering that a "corrective notice" to the ballot be issued. Plaintiff bar association, as well as other plaintiffs who had filed the declaratory judgment action, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Illinois Constitution required that Illinois ask its voters at specified intervals about whether a state constitutional convention should be held. That question was slated to be on the ballot at the upcoming general election. However, the question was worded inaccurately. The bar association, as well as other plaintiffs, filed a multicount declaratory judgment action challenging the question. The trial court, rather than order corrections to the ballot itself, directed defendant state officials to issue a "corrective notice" to be distributed to voters along with the ballot. The appellate court found that the "corrective notice" guaranteed that each voter had a clear opportunity to express his choice either for or against holding a state constitutional convention, and, thus, fulfilled the requirement of Ill. Const. art. III, § 3 that elections be "free and equal." It also found that the bar association and other plaintiffs had not shown that the requirement that the "corrective notice" be on a "separate ballot" meant a ballot physically distinct from the general ballot instead of the trial court's remedy of that notice being on a separate part of the general ballot.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Maldonado


Nos. 2-07-0015, 2-07-0016, 2-07-0017 & 2-07-0058 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


386 Ill. App. 3d 964; 897 N.E.2d 854; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1056; 325 Ill. Dec. 315



October 28, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 12, 2008.
Appeal denied by People v. Maldonado, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1066 (Ill., Jan. 28, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County. No. 06-CF-61. Honorable R. Craig Sahlstrom, Judge, Presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County. No. 06-CF-113. Honorable John R. Truitt, Judge, Presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County. No. 06-CF-111. Honorable John R. Truitt, Judge, Presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County. No. 06-CF-433. Honorable John R. Truitt, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Boone County (Illinois), in four separate cases, entered final judgments of conviction against four defendants for aggravated driving under the influence, in violation of 625 ILCS 5/11-501(d)(1)(G) (2006), for driving while intoxicated and while not licensed by Illinois to drive. It then sentenced each defendant to probation and ordered each to pay certain fines. Defendants appealed; their appeals were then consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The four defendants in separate cases were convicted of aggravated driving under the influence (DUI), in violation of 625 ILCS 5/11-501(d)(1)(G) (2006), for driving while intoxicated and while not licensed by Illinois to drive. The four defendants received probation and were ordered to pay certain fines. On appeal, the four defendants argued that 625 ILCS 5/11-501(d)(1)(G) (2006) was not in effect at the time of their offenses. Accordingly, they requested that their convictions be reduced to DUI. Alternatively, they claimed they were entitled to monetary credit against their fines for time in pre-sentencing custody, pursuant to 725 ILCS 5/110-14 (2004). The appellate court found that two amendatory acts passed after 625 ILCS 5/11-501(d)(1)(G) (2006) went into effect did not involve material inconsistent with that statute and, thus, did not repeal it; rather, the appellate court found, the statute and the two amendatory acts could all be read together. However, it agreed with the four defendants that they were entitled to $ 5 per day sentence credits pursuant to 725 ILCS 5/110-14 (2004) and remanded the cases for a determination of the monetary credit owed in each case.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgments of conviction as to each defendant. It then ordered that the cases be remanded to the trial court to determine the amount of time each of the four defendants spent in custody and to grant the appropriate amount of credit against each defendant's fine.

People v. Lampton


No. 4-07-0208


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


385 Ill. App. 3d 507; 898 N.E.2d 680; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1074; 325 Ill. Dec. 633



October 24, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Lampton, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 975 (Ill., Jan. 28, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 04CF814. Honorable Heidi Ladd, Judge Presiding.
People v. Lampton, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 981 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., Sept. 26, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted by the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) of armed robbery under 720 ILCS 5/18-2(a)(1) (2002), and was sentenced. The convictions and sentences were affirmed. The inmate's postconviction petition was dismissed as patently without merit. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that to survive a first-stage dismissal of a postconviction petition the inmate had to allege the gist of a constitutional claim. The inmate's sole claim was that he did not receive the effective assistance of appellate counsel because counsel failed to argue the State failed to prove that he possessed a dangerous weapon. The inmate's possession of a weapon could be inferred from circumstantial evidence. A detective stated the inmate told him he took the pepper spray with him into the bank in case he needed to use the spray on the tellers. The inmate denied saying this and maintained he did not take the pepper spray into the bank, but the jury believed the detective. The can of pepper spray was found on the inmate when he was apprehended shortly after the robbery. The inmate possessed the pepper spray during the robbery. It could be inferred the inmate knew the can of pepper spray actually contained pepper spray from the fact the inmate confessed the he intended to use it to spray in the tellers' faces to debilitate them, if necessary. The pepper spray was a dangerous weapon under the armed-robbery statute. Appellate counsel was not ineffective.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The State was awarded a $ 50 statutory assessment as costs of the appeal.

People v. Jessica M. (In re Jessica M.)


No. 1-06-2007


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


385 Ill. App. 3d 894; 897 N.E.2d 810; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1009; 325 Ill. Dec. 271



October 17, 2008, Decided 
October 17, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 11, 2008.
Vacated by, Appeal denied by State v. Jessica M. (In re Jessica M.), 234 Ill. 2d 522, 917 N.E.2d 526, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 2065, 334 Ill. Dec. 700 (2009)
Vacated by, On remand at, Remanded by People v. Jessica M. (In re Jessica M.), 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 157 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Feb. 26, 2010)
Vacated by, Remanded by People v. Jessica M. (In re Jessica M.), 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 217 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Mar. 19, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Noreen M. Daly, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which adjudicated her delinquent for the offense of aggravated battery, 720 ILCS 5/12-4(a) and (b)(8) (2004), sentenced her to five years probation, and ordered her to submit a saliva sample for DNA indexing under 730 ILCS 5/5-4-3(f) (2004).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with beating a victim. The appellate court held that the trial court did not err in rejecting defendant's claim of self-defense. The severity of the victim's injuries, contrasted with the few abrasions defendant sustained, manifestly supported the trial court's finding that defendant's use of force was unreasonable and excessive. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in excluding testimony concerning defendant's reputation because no evidence was offered to show that the testimony was based on contact with individuals who were defendant's neighbors and associates. Because there was one adjudication of delinquency, and the dispositional order did not reflect that the probation was based on multiple offenses, the one-act, one-crime principle had no application. Defendant did not show that 730 ILCS 5/5-4-3(f) was invalid. One database was used to identify or exclude potential suspects or offenders and for random statistical probability calculations. The science of DNA "fingerprinting" to obtain the profiles transmitted and included within the single database did not use those portions of a subject's DNA that coded for genetic characteristics.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court but modified the term of defendant's probation and supervision to terminate on her twenty-first birthday, June 20, 2010.

 

1029 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Paige


No. 3-07-0869


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


385 Ill. App. 3d 486; 896 N.E.2d 879; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 995; 324 Ill. Dec. 803


May 9, 2008, Submitted 
October 6, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 18, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. No. 07-DT-1626. Honorable Bennett J. Braun, Judge, Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pro se defendant was charged with driving under the influence of drugs, in violation of 625 ILCS 5/11-501(a)(4) (2006), and his license was summarily suspended for refusing or failing to submit to drug testing, pursuant to 625 ILCS 5/11-501.1 (2006). The Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois granted his motion to rescind the summary suspension of his driver's license. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court granted the petition to rescind the summary suspension because the police did not have reasonable grounds to stop defendant's vehicle. On appeal, the State contended that the trial court erred by denying its motion for directed finding. The State argued that defendant failed to establish a prima facie case for recision by failing to put forward any evidence that the roadside safety check was invalid. Defendant had not filed an appellee brief. Defendant was stopped pursuant to a roadside safety check. While the roadblock was considered a seizure, it was not a per se violation of the Fourth Amendment. In order to successfully establish a prima facie case for recision, defendant needed to show some evidence that the roadblock was not reasonable. Defendant did not produce any such evidence. Thus, the county circuit court's decision denying the State's motion for a directed finding was against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the county circuit court was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1030 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Morgan


No. 3-06-0605


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


385 Ill. App. 3d 771; 896 N.E.2d 417; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 982; 324 Ill. Dec. 631



September 30, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 5, 2008. Released for Publication November 18, 2008.
Appeal denied by People v. Morgan, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 901 (Ill., Mar. 25, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Tazewell County, Illinois, No. 06-CF-47. Honorable J. Peter Ault, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a fully negotiated plea agreement, the trial court found defendant guilty of, among other things, four counts of home invasion under 720 ILCS 5/12-11(a) (2004). The Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Tazewell County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to four concurrent 30-year prison terms for these offenses. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that three of his home invasion convictions and sentences should be vacated under the one-act, one-crime principles. The State argued that defendant forfeited or waived that argument by failing to raise the issue in the trial court. Although defendant failed to raise the issue before the trial court, the appellate court concluded that plain error review was warranted because the one-act, one-crime rule was used to enforce the double jeopardy prohibition against multiple punishments. The State also argued that defendant waived or forfeited his one-act, one-crime argument by entering a guilty plea. The appellate court disagreed, declining to assume that defendant voluntarily and knowingly pled guilty to improper excess convictions, without something in the record suggesting that he voluntarily relinquished a known right by agreeing to those impermissible excess convictions.


OUTCOME: Three of defendant's convictions and sentences for home invasion were vacated.

 

1031 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lampton


NO. 4-07-0208


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 981



September 26, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Lampton, 385 Ill. App. 3d 507, 898 N.E.2d 680, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1074, 325 Ill. Dec. 633 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., Oct. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 04CF814. Honorable Heidi Ladd, Judge Presiding.
People v. Lampton, 222 Ill. 2d 589, 861 N.E.2d 660, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1936, 308 Ill. Dec. 329 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) denied defendant's pro se postconviction petition that alleged ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel and challenged the constitutionality of mandatory supervised release provisions. Defendant appealed, claiming that his petition stated the gist of a constitutional claim of ineffective assistance in failing to challenge the sufficiency of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction and sentence for 3 counts of armed robbery (720 ILCS 5/18-2(a)(1) (2002)) were affirmed on direct appeal. Because defendant admitted he robbed a bank, the court only had to determine whether he did so with a "dangerous weapon." Viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the State, the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant possessed pepper spray during the robbery. The fact that he did not use it was immaterial. The statute required only that he was armed with a dangerous weapon. It could have been inferred that defendant knew the can actually contained pepper spray from the fact he confessed to a detective that he intended to use it to spray in the tellers' faces to debilitate them if necessary. Accordingly, the court concluded that the pepper spray was a dangerous weapon under the armed-robbery statute. Because defendant's underlying claim that the State did not prove he committed the robbery while possessing a "dangerous weapon" was without merit, appellate counsel was not ineffective on that basis and the trial court properly dismissed defendant's postconviction petition at the first stage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Herrin


No. 3-06-0924


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


385 Ill. App. 3d 187; 895 N.E.2d 1075; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 940; 324 Ill. Dec. 360


January 10, 2008, Assigned; March 11, 2008, Submitted 
September 25, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 5, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit Tazewell County, Illinois. No. 05-CM-870. Honorable Richard D. McCoy, Judge, Presiding. JUSTICE SCHMIDT, specially concurring.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of two counts of simple battery and sentenced to 12 months of probation. The Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit Tazewell County (Illinois) revoked defendant's probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to revoke her probation. Since defendant's revocation hearing did not occur until after the original 12-month probation term expired, the appellate court noted that the trial court lacked jurisdiction unless the term was tolled. The appellate court further concluded that the pleading filed by the probation officer was valid ab initio because the probation officer lacked authority to file the pleading. The pleading amounted to law practice and the probation officer lacked a law license; thus, the probation officer's actions not only constituted the unauthorized practice of law but also usurped the statutory prerogative of the state's attorney.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

 

1033 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Uphold v. Ill. Workers' Comp. Comm'n


No. 5-07-0669WC


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT, ILLINOIS WORKERS' COMPENSATION COMMISSION DIVISION


385 Ill. App. 3d 567; 896 N.E.2d 828; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 936; 324 Ill. Dec. 752



September 24, 2008, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 07-MR-230. Honorable Thomas W. Chapman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought workers' compensation benefits under the Illinois Workers' Compensation Act (ILWCA), 820 ILCS 305/1 et seq. Appellee Illinois Workers' Compensation Commission affirmed an arbitrator's decision that the employee could proceed under the ILWCA or the Longshore and Harbor Workers' Compensation Act (LHWCA), 33 U.S.C.S. § 901 et seq. The Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) set aside the decision. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the claim under the ILWCA was preempted by the LHWCA. The claimant argued that his case fell within the twilight zone and was, therefore, subject to concurrent jurisdiction. The appellate court reviewed whether there was jurisdiction under the LHWCA and the ILWCA de novo as the facts essential to the inquiry were undisputed. The claimant was eligible for coverage under the pre-1972 version of the LHWCA where, by exclusion, he qualified as an employee under 33 U.S.C.S. § 902(3), his injury arose out of and in the course of his employment, his employer had at least one worker engaged in maritime employment, and his injury occurred upon navigable waters of the United States. However, there was no jurisdiction under the ILWCA because this was not a doubtful case. At the time of his injury, the claimant was removing hazardous material from the bottom of the ship before it was placed in dry dock for repair; he was engaged in an activity that was an integral part of and essential to ship repair, a traditional maritime activity. The claimant also did not fall within the maritime but local doctrine. Thus, the Commission lacked jurisdiction to hear the claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment setting aside the Commission's decision was affirmed.

 

1034 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Siegel v. Lake County Officers Electoral Bd.


No. 2-08-0626


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


385 Ill. App. 3d 452; 895 N.E.2d 69; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 925; 324 Ill. Dec. 69



September 9, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 24, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 08-MR-563. Honorable Raymond J. McKoski, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents appealed an order entered by the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) reversing a decision of the Lake County Officers Electoral Board (Board) to exclude petitioner candidate from the November 2008 general election ballot for member of the Lake County Board.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that respondents crafted a more precise argument when they alleged that a resolution did not reflect the true date of a District Committee meeting. Respondents' objection to the occurrence of the meeting included the objection pertaining to the true date of the meeting. Respondents did not waive under 10 ILCS 5/10-8 (2006) their ability to challenge the sufficiency of the papers for the candidate's failure to include the true date of her nomination. 10 ILCS 5/7-61 (2006) was a mandatory provision, and the date requirement was not reclassified from mandatory to directory. The notary incorrectly wrote the date of April 6, 2008, in the jurats on the resolution and the statement of candidacy. There was no evidence of bad-faith noncompliance. The candidate's resolution was facially valid, and both the true date of selection and the incorrect date fell within all statutory time constraints. The notary affixed a date to the resolution, albeit the incorrect date. But for the scrivener's error, the resolution complied in every mandatory aspect of § 7-61. The error did not impair the integrity of the electoral process, and § 7-61 was substantially followed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

J.S.A. v. M.H.


No. 3-04-0678 Consolidated with 3-04-0908 Consolidated with 3-05-0556 Consolidated with 3-05-0561


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


384 Ill. App. 3d 998; 893 N.E.2d 682; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 931; 323 Ill. Dec. 410



September 8, 2008, Filed and Modified


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by J.S.A. v. M.H., 229 Ill. 2d 668, 900 N.E.2d 1118, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1427, 326 Ill. Dec. 871 (2008)
Decision reached on appeal by J.S.A v. M.H., 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 3192 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. Nos. 99-F-420, 99-AD-115. Nos. 99-F-420. Nos. 99-AD-115. Honorable William McMenamin, Judge, Presiding.
