Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. Nos. 99-F-420, 99-AD-115. Nos. 99-F-420. Nos. 99-AD-115. Honorable William McMenamin, Judge, Presiding.
J.S.A. v. M.H., 224 Ill. 2d 182, 863 N.E.2d 236, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 426, 309 Ill. Dec. 6 (2007)
J.S.A. v. M.H., 361 Ill. App. 3d 1102, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 4888 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2005)
J.S.A. v. M.H., 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 697 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., July 11, 2008)



DISPOSITION: No. 3-04-0678, Reversed in part and affirmed in part. No. 3-04-0908, Affirmed. No. 3-05-0556, Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded. No. 3-05-0561, Reversed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A child resulted from an affair between cross-appellant father and cross-appellant wife of cross-appellant husband, the father brought a parentage action, and the husband and wife brought an adoption action. In consolidated appeals, including a case remanded from the Illinois Supreme Court, the father and the husband and wife cross-appealed various orders of the Circuit Court for the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois.


OVERVIEW: DNA testing established that the father was the biological father of the child, and the parties disputed whether the parentage and adoption cases were properly consolidated, whether a stay of adoption case pending appeal was properly denied, whether the husband was properly ordered to undergo DNA testing, and whether the father's petition to establish a parent-child relationship and visitation rights was properly denied. The appellate court first held that the parentage and adoption actions were properly consolidated since they both concerned the parentage of the child and shared common parties and facts, and a stay of the adoption proceedings was warranted since the consequences of the adoption action could potentially deprive the father of his rights as the child's biological father. Further, by filing a declaration of parentage in the paternity action, the husband put his physical condition at issue and was properly found in contempt for refusing to submit to DNA testing. Also, the determination of the father's parentage necessarily established a parent-child relationship, and denial of the relationship and visitation based on the best interests of the child was impermissible.


OUTCOME: The trial court's orders were affirmed in part with regard to consolidation and compelling DNA testing, but the orders were reversed in part with regard to denial of the father's petition to establish a parent-child relationship and denial of a stay pending appeal, and proceedings in the adoption action were vacated and the cases were remanded for a hearing on the father's visitation request and to reinstate the father in the adoption action.

 

1036 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Traven C. (In re T.C.)


No. 1-07-0393


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


384 Ill. App. 3d 870; 894 N.E.2d 876; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 851; 323 Ill. Dec. 850



August 22, 2008, Decided 
August 22, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 7, 2008.
Appeal denied by People v. Traven C. (In re T.C.), 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1735 (Ill., Nov. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 JD 3603. Honorable Rodney Hughes Brooks, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review following a proceeding in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), where he was adjudicated delinquent of aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced to five years of probation. As a result of the adjudication, appellant was classified as a "sexual predator" pursuant to the Sex Offender Registration Act (SORA), 730 ILCS 150/1 et seq. (2004).


OVERVIEW: The sexual predator classification meant that appellant would be required to register as a sex offender for the rest of his life. The evidence was sufficient to establish that appellant committed an act of sexual penetration beyond a reasonable doubt under 720 ILCS 5/12-12(f) (2004) as even slight contact was sufficient to establish penetration. Testimony from the victim as well as admissions made by appellant in a handwritten statement provided the necessary evidence. Appellant argued that 705 ILCS 405/5-101(3) (2004), which denied minors the right to a jury trial except in certain circumstances, deprived him of due process due to the consequences imposed on appellant under SORA. The appellate court disagreed. The registration requirements under SORA did not deprive appellant of a liberty interest. Thus, there was no due process violation. Further, even if appellant had established a liberty interest, he received all of the process that he was due. Juvenile proceedings were not criminal prosecutions within the meaning and reach of the Sixth Amendment, so due process did not require a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed.

 

1037 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Millineum Maint. Mgmt. v. County of Lake


No. 2-07-0728


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


384 Ill. App. 3d 638; 894 N.E.2d 845; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 830; 323 Ill. Dec. 819



August 15, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 26, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 06-MR-752. Honorable Mary S. Schostok, Judge, Presiding.
Millineum Maint. Mgmt. v. County of Lake, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 598 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., June 12, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs developers sought administrative review in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) of defendant Lake County Board's denial of their conditional use permit application. After the trial court granted the developers' motion for a de novo hearing, the court certified two questions of law on the standard of review, interlocutory review was allowed under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 308, and a defendant's petition for leave to appeal was granted.


OVERVIEW: A certified question asked if the permit's denial was subject to de novo review under 55 ILCS 5/5-12012.1 (2006) as a legislative decision rather than review under the Administrative Review Law, 735 ILCS 5/3-101 et seq. (2006) as an administrative or quasi-judicial decision. The appellate court held 55 ILCS 5/5-12012.1 (2006) did not apply to the denial because it plainly applied only to judicial review of the granting of a permit. It did not violate separation of powers because its removal of certain zoning decisions from the purview of the Administrative Review Law, 735 ILCS 5/3-101 et seq. (2006), did not exceed the legislature's authority, nor did language invoking de novo judicial review as a legislative decision, so courts were given neither too much nor too little power. The statute's prescribed review for arbitrariness as a matter of substantive due process deferred to agency decision making because a court intervened only when there was no rational basis for a contested decision, and any new evidence presented had to bear on review for arbitrariness as a matter of substantive due process. Since the statute did not apply, the second certified question was not answered.


OUTCOME: The first certified question was answered in the negative, and the second question was not answered. The matter was remanded to the trial court.

Kirkpatrick v. Strosberg


Nos. 2-06-0724 & 2-06-0731 Cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


385 Ill. App. 3d 119; 894 N.E.2d 781; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 772; 323 Ill. Dec. 755



August 8, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 19, 2008.
Appeal denied by Kirkpatrick v. Strosberg, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1662 (Ill., Nov. 26, 2008)
Appeal denied by Kirkpatrick v. Strosberg, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1685 (Ill., Nov. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 00-L-473. Honorable Stephen J. Culliton, Judge, Presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 00-L-473. Honorable Stephen J. Culliton, Judge, Presiding.
Kirkpatrick v. Strosberg, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 358 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Apr. 16, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff condominium buyers brought suit against defendant builders, alleging violation of the Illinois Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act, 815 ILCS 505/1 et seq. (1996), and other claims. After a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), plaintiffs were awarded nominal damages on their breach of contract and consumer fraud claims, attorney fees, and punitive damages. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants indicated that plaintiffs' units would have nine-foot ceilings, but the ceilings were 8 feet 6 inches. Plaintiffs' units closed in 1997, but plaintiffs' expert testified as to comparable values in 2004. Because of the seven-year difference, the court held that the trial court did not err in finding that the expert's figures did not represent fair market value. Because plaintiffs failed to provide a proper basis to compute their damages, the trial court did not err in awarding only nominal damages. The trial court properly awarded punitive damages under 815 ILCS 505/10a(a) (1996) based on intentional conduct. The evidence showed that defendants knew at least one year before closing that the ceilings would not be the promised height, but never told plaintiffs this. The $300,000 in punitive damages was not grossly excessive under the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, given defendants' intentional conduct, the fact that $83,000 in attorney fees were awarded, and the fact that 815 ILCS 505/7 (1996) authorized civil penalties of up to $50,000 per violation; here, defendants had committed numerous violations of the Act. The amount of attorney fees was not error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1039 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Cullerton v. Du Page County Officers Electoral Bd.


No. 2-08-0605


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


384 Ill. App. 3d 989; 894 N.E.2d 774; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 771; 323 Ill. Dec. 748



August 7, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 19, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 08-MR-802. Honorable Paul M. Fullerton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, a county electoral board and its members, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which reversed the board's decision to exclude petitioner candidate from the November 2008 ballot as the Democratic candidate for senator for an Illinois legislative district.


OVERVIEW: Because the candidate voted as a Republican in the 2008 primary, under the statement of candidacy portion of he 10 ILCS 5/7-10 (2006), he could not run as a Democrat in the general election. Under § 7-10, only a "qualified primary voter" of the party to which a nominating petition related could be a candidate in the general election. Thus, to run as a Democrat, the candidate was required to have voted as a Democrat in the preceding primary. Because the candidate voted as a Republican in the primary, he was "locked" as a Republican primary voter until the next primary. While he could then switch parties, and become a Democrat primary voter, the next primary would not occur until 2010. The Sperling decision did not require a contrary ruling. Although portions of § 7-10 had been found unconstitutional in Sperling, a post-Sperling amendment to § 7-10 in 1990, while removing the offending party switching language, left intact the restriction on party-changing found in the statement of candidacy portion of § 7-10. That specific language had never itself been deemed unconstitutional and was viable even in light of Sperling.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the decision of the circuit court.

Hernandez v. Alexian Bros. Health Sys.


No. 1-06-1196


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


384 Ill. App. 3d 510; 893 N.E.2d 934; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 759; 323 Ill. Dec. 460



July 31, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 23, 2008.
Petition denied by Hernandez v. Alexian Bros. Health Sys., 229 Ill. 2d 622, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1259 (Ill., Sept. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 L 4613. Honorable Diane J. Larsen, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered summary judgment for appellees, a doctor and his employer, in appellant decedent's estate administrator's claim that appellees' negligence caused the death. The administrator claimed that § 25 of the Good Samaritan Act (745 ILCS 49/25 (2002)) was unconstitutional and defeated the purpose of the Illinois Hospital Licensing Act (210 ILCS 85/1 et seq. (2002)). The administrator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent had been undergoing a biopsy in the radiation department when she suffered cardiac arrest. She was transferred to the emergency room where the doctor responded to an "any available cardiologist" page over the intercom. Because the doctor rendered emergency care, and did not bill the decedent, appellees claimed that his actions were immunized from civil liability by the provisions of § 25. The court found that there were no facts in dispute as to the doctor's good faith in providing emergency medical care. However, the doctor's answer to a supplemental good-faith interrogatory that he did not bill in cases like the decedent's conflicted with his billing service's testimony that, other than the decedent's case, there were no other cases where doctor had not billed patients for such services. The court found that the doctor's decision not to bill the decedent raised a question of material fact as to whether he acted in good faith and had an honest, lawful intent to provide medical services without fee, or whether the doctor was acting in bad faith and deviated from his routine billing practices to invoke the protection of § 25.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment and remanded the case for proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

1041 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Curry


NO. 4-06-0355


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


384 Ill. App. 3d 315; 893 N.E.2d 295; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 751; 323 Ill. Dec. 281



July 28, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Curry, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1646 (Ill., Nov. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 05CF800. Honorable Scott B. Diamond, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of armed robbery. The trial court adjudged defendant an habitual criminal and sentenced him to life in prison under the Habitual Criminal Act, 720 ILCS 5/33B-1 through 33B-3 (2006). On appeal, defendant argued that the sentence of natural-life under the Act violated his rights to due process and to a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: At trial, defendant exercised his U.S. Const. amend. V right not to testify and filed a motion to bar application of § 33B-1 on constitutional grounds. The trial court denied that motion and a post trial motion. On appeal, defendant relied on Ngo, arguing that § 33B-1(c) unconstitutionally increased his Class X felony sentence to one of mandatory life imprisonment based on facts that were, as in Shepard, too far removed from the fact of a prior conviction, i.e., that his two prior convictions did not result from and were not connected with the same transaction. The court distinguished Ngo on the facts: (1) defendant's first two armed-robbery convictions were not connected with the same transaction was clear from the record; (2) he was first convicted of armed robbery in 1990, and he was sentenced to nine years in prison; (3) his second conviction for armed robbery occurred in 1995; (4) his intervening stay as a guest of the government showed his convictions met the requirements of § 33B-1; and (5) that the qualifying offenses were not part of the same transaction was inherent in the convictions themselves such that a determination by a jury of defendant's peers was not required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence.

People v. Johnson


NO. 4-07-0820


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


384 Ill. App. 3d 409; 893 N.E.2d 275; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 705; 323 Ill. Dec. 261



July 16, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 07CM383. Honorable Holly F. Clemons, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed after the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained during a traffic stop. Defendant had been charged with unlawful possession of cannabis.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for violating 625 ILCS 5/12-503(c) (2006) by having his view obstructed by a cherry air freshener hanging from his rear view mirror. The validity of the stop turned on the Fourth Amendment question of whether it was reasonable for the officer who stopped defendant to believe that he had observed defendant driving with a "material obstruction" of defendant's view. The trial court found defendant's testimony that the officer stated that defendant could not have anything hanging from his rear view mirror persuasive. Section 12-503 only prohibited items that materially obstructed a driver's view. The officer did not have a clear understanding of what a material obstruction was. Further, photographs taken of defendant's vehicle showed that the officer's belief that the air freshener was a material obstruction was not justifiable.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed.

J.S.A. v. M.H.


No. 3-04-0678 Consolidated with 3-04-0908 Consolidated with 3-05-0556 Consolidated with 3-05-0561


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 697



July 11, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by J.S.A. v. M.H., 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 907 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., Sept. 8, 2008)
Modified by J.S.A. v. M.H., 384 Ill. App. 3d 998, 893 N.E.2d 682, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 931, 323 Ill. Dec. 410 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. Nos. 99-F-420, 99-AD-115. Honorable William McMenamin, Judge, Presiding.
J.S.A. v. M.H., 361 Ill. App. 3d 745, 841 N.E.2d 983, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1063, 299 Ill. Dec. 251 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: No. 3-04-0678, Reversed in part and affirmed in part. No. 3-04-0908, Affirmed. No. 3-05-0556, Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded. No. 3-05-0561, Reversed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In parentage and adoption cases combined for appeal, the trial court, inter alia, ordered appellee husband to submit to DNA testing, denied appellant father's petition for visitation, dismissed the father from the adoption, and found that the father had abandoned the child. All parties appealed, but the appeals were dismissed. The Supreme Court of Illinois reversed as to one appeal and remanded. The remaining dismissals were vacated.


OVERVIEW: The father was dismissed from the adoption based on his failure to register with the Putative Father Registry. The appellate court found that this was error. The failure to register was irrelevant to the parentage action and did not affect the father's participation in the adoption. The order staying the adoption was appropriate until the parentage action concluded. The parentage and adoption proceedings were properly consolidated and should have remained so until the termination of all the litigation. Both actions concerned parentage and shared a common nucleus of parties and facts. Removal of the stay would have prejudiced the father's rights as the child's biological father. The trial court was authorized by Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 215 to compel the husband to submit to DNA testing. The husband placed his physical condition in issue by his declaration of parentage in the paternity action. The Parentage Act, 750 ILCS 45/1, did not authorize the trial court to deny the father's petition for parentage on the basis of best interest. The determination of parentage necessarily resulted in the determination of a parent-child relationship.


OUTCOME: The father was reinstated as a party to the adoption proceedings. The order compelling the husband to submit to DNA testing and the contempt finding against the husband were affirmed. The denial of the father's petition to establish a parent-child relationship was reversed and the case was remanded for a hearing on visitation. All rulings in the adoption subsequent to the trial court's denial of the father's request for a stay were vacated.

 

1044 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


McHenry County Defenders, Inc. v. City of Harvard


No. 2-07-0386


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


384 Ill. App. 3d 265; 891 N.E.2d 1017; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 680; 322 Ill. Dec. 726



July 2, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 15, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 05-MR-109. Honorable Maureen P. McIntyre, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an advocacy group and a city resident, sued defendants, a city and its officials, in the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) under 525 ILCS 30/17 (2004) and 520 ILCS 10/11(b) (2004) to require defendants to engage in environmental consultations. The trial court granted plaintiffs summary judgment, but dismissed their request to declare ordinances void and to amend a complaint. Plaintiffs appealed and defendants cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city said it did not "authorize" a gravel pit, as the term was used in 525 ILCS 30/17 (2004) and 520 ILCS 10/11(b) (2004), so the statutes' requirements to consult with the Illinois Department of Natural Resources (IDNR) did not apply. The appellate court held the city's acts met the definition of "authorized" because it was actively involved in initial planning stages, affecting its original plan for the land. It reviewed an owner's plans, negotiated an annexation agreement subjecting the owner to restrictions, and rezoned the land. The statutes' requirement that public agencies engage in environmental consultations was unambiguous, so private parties' prior consultations with IDNR did not meet the city's duties. It had to engage in the consultation because it "authorized" the project. It was no error to dismiss plaintiffs' request to declare ordinances the city passed as part of the process void. The statutes did not let a trial court, in a suit by private citizens, invalidate an ordinance, as plaintiffs could only seek mandamus relief, nor, was it error not to let them amend their complaint to ask that the city be ordered to pass ordinances voiding the ordinances at issue.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1045 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Chapa v. Cook (In re Estate of Hale)


No. 1-07-2536


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


383 Ill. App. 3d 559; 890 N.E.2d 1244; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 652; 322 Ill. Dec. 325



June 30, 2008, Decided 
June 30, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released For Publication August 1, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Jeffrey A. Malak, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimants, a daughter and her husband, filed a 755 ILCS 5/18-1.1 (2004) custodial claim in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) against a decedent's estate. The claimants appealed the circuit court's award of $100,000, set off by the $50,000 the daughter had already received as the decedent's guardian.


OVERVIEW: The claimants cared for the decedent for 9 1/2 years prior to her death. During that time, the decedent suffered from severe Alzheimer's and could not care for herself. The circuit court limited the claimants recovery to the last three years of the decedent's life. The claimants argued that the circuit court erred in applying a five-year statute of limitations to the custodial claim and in applying the set off. The appellate court agreed. Nothing in § 18-1.1 limited the claimants' recovery to only five years prior to the date of a disabled person's death. Rather, the statute clearly set forth the requirement that the claimants have cared for the decedent for at least 3 years. Further, as § 18-1.1 provided that the claimants were entitled to a claim against the estate when the decedent died, any statute of limitations that might apply begin to run until the date of death. In determining the amount of the claim, the circuit court should have considered the entire 9 1/2 years that the claimants cared for the decedent. The circuit court also erred in setting off the custodial award against the guardian fee as the custodial claim was to be in addition to any other reasonable claim.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the circuit court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the appellate court's opinion.

 

1046 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Winnebago County Citizens for Controlled Growth v. County of Winnebago


No. 2-07-0362


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


383 Ill. App. 3d 735; 891 N.E.2d 448; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 607; 322 Ill. Dec. 433



June 18, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 1, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 06-MR-239. Honorable Janet R. Holmgren, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nonprofit corporation sued defendant county and developer, challenging a special use permit to construct a planned community development. The Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) dismissed the claims that sought review under the Administrative Review Law, 735 ILCS 5/3-101 et seq., and alleged that the grant of the permit violated substantive due process (the LaSalle claim). The corporation appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court erred in dismissing the LaSalle claim on the ground that the corporation lacked standing under the associational standing doctrine where there was nothing inherently implausible about the corporation's arguments that only limited participation by its members would be necessary in the trial; establishing the corporation's right to relief on its claim did not necessarily require significant participation by the individual members of the corporation. 805 ILCS 105/103.10(b) did not impose more stringent requirements than that imposed by case law as the intent of the legislature in enacting the statute was to codify the common law. The fact that the corporation was not a party to the administrative proceeding did not prevent it from appealing the decision under 735 ILCS 5/3-101 as its standing was derivative of its members' standing. Since the members had participated in the initial hearing before the zoning board and the corporation met all of the other requirements of associational standing, the corporation was entitled to step into the shoes of its members in bringing the claim under the Administrative Review Law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1047 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Millineum Maint. Mgmt. v. County of Lake


No. 2-07-0728


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 598



June 12, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Rehearing granted by Millineum Maint. Mgmt. v. County of Lake, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 856 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Aug. 15, 2008)
Substituted opinion at Millineum Maint. Mgmt. v. County of Lake, 894 N.E.2d 845, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 830, 323 Ill. Dec. 819 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Aug. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 06-MR-752. Honorable Mary S. Schostok, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant citizen filed an interlocutory appeal in plaintiffs' action seeking review of a county board's denial of a conditional use permit application. The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) certified: (1) Whether the denial of a special use was subject to de novo review as a legislative decision under 55 ILCS 5/5-12012.1 (2006), and (2) if not, did § 5-12012.1 preclude review under the Administrative Review Law. 55 ILCS 5/1-6007 (2006)


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that a denial of a special use permit by a county board was not subject to de novo judicial review as a legislative decision under § 5-12012.1. Therefore, § 5-12012.1 did not apply to the denial of plaintiffs' application for a conditional use permit. Although § 5-12012.1 could be ambiguous, it plainly applied only to the adoption of a special use. Section 5-12012.1 was intended to reach not all county and municipal decisions on relevant zoning matters, but rather only decisions to grant the listed zoning actions. It applied only when a board adopted a special use, not when it denied one. To the extent § 5-12012.1 was intended to remove the listed zoning decisions from the purview of the Administrative Review Law, it did not offend separation of powers principles, Ill. Const. art. II, § 1. The legislature had the authority to remove certain administrative determinations from, or add certain determinations to, the ambit of judicial review. The type of review imposed by § 5-12012.1 could be nominally "de novo" and could allow for the presentation of new evidence but was actually much less searching than the administrative review the statute curtails.


OUTCOME: The appellate court answered the first certified question in the negative and did not reach the second certified question.

People v. Mobley


1-06-2486


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


383 Ill. App. 3d 89; 890 N.E.2d 673; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 554; 321 Ill. Dec. 951



June 11, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Released for Publication July 21, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 1-06-2486. Honorable Thomas M. Davy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of one count of residential burglary. The trial court then found for sentencing purposes that she was statutorily ineligible for Treatment Alternatives for Safe Communities services and sentenced her to four years in prison with recommended alcohol and drug treatment. Defendant appealed her sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in a bench trial of residential burglary. Prior to her sentencing, the trial court ordered a Treatment Alternatives for Safe Communities (TASC) evaluation. Despite being clinically acceptable for TASC, the trial court found that she was ineligible pursuant to the Alcoholism and Other Drug Abuse and Dependancy Act (Act), 20 ILCS 301/40-5(7) (2004), for TASC services because of the conviction and a prior felony conviction. She was then sentenced to four years in prison. She claimed on appeal that her sentence violated her equal protection and due process rights. The appellate court disagreed. It first noted that her argument had to be reviewed under the plain-error doctrine because she had not raised it in the trial court but claimed a substantial right was involved. It then found that plain error was not committed in finding she was not eligible for TASC, as the Act rationally distinguished between similarly-situated convicted felons based on deterring home invaders and was reasonably designed to remedy the evils the legislature determined to be a threat to the public safety, health, and well being, namely, people breaking into the homes of others.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Godfrey


No. 3-06-0819


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


382 Ill. App. 3d 511; 888 N.E.2d 1230; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 468; 321 Ill. Dec. 297


November 28, 2007, Assigned; March 11, 2008, Submitted 
May 23, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 25, 2008


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit Peoria County, Illinois. No. 05-CF-437. Honorable Scott A. Shore Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County (Illinois) of home invasion, under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(a)(2) (2004), criminal trespass and domestic battery. He sought a reduction of his conviction under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615, and a remand for additional proceedings on his ineffective assistance of counsel claim.


OVERVIEW: After defendant did not arrive at the victim's house, at her invitation, for a significant time, she locked her door and did not answer her phone. He kicked her door down. The appellate court held he was not entitled to a reduction in the degree of his conviction, under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615, because there was no evidentiary weakness in the State's case, as (1) there was no fact question as to whether his presence in the victim's home was authorized, (2) the limited authority doctrine did not allow him to enter the home out of a concern for the victim's safety because he entered by force, and (3) sufficient evidence showed he physically injured the victim. The decision to believe the testimony of the victim and the officer over defendant showed no evidentiary weakness. Defendant did not show he received ineffective assistance of counsel when counsel did not tell him about a mandatory six-year home invasion sentence because the trial court told him of this sentence, and he said he understood. The trial court correctly concluded that defendant's ineffective assistance claim had no merit and refused to appoint independent counsel to pursue the claim at the trial level.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

McCready v. Ill. Secy. of State


NO. 3-06-0521


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


382 Ill. App. 3d 789; 888 N.E.2d 702; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 428; 321 Ill. Dec. 183


January 18, 2008, Submitted 
May 15, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 16, 2008.
Appeal denied by McCready v. White, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1483 (Ill., Nov. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Iroquois County, Illinois, No. 04-CH-29. Honorable Scott-Swaim, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Iroquois County (Illinois), granted motions to dismiss filed by defendants, Secretary of State and vehicle sellers, in plaintiff buyer's suit that alleged violations of the Freedom of Information Act (FOIA), 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 140/1 et seq. (2004), the Uniform Deceptive Trade Practices Act, and the Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act.


OVERVIEW: The buyer sought title information from the Secretary for cars he purchased from the sellers through tax lien sales. The buyer's claim for declaratory judgment was premised on his alleged ownership of a security interest in a car when the sellers sought and the Secretary issued a new title for the car. He attached a note to the complaint, as required by 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-606 (2004), but the note showed that he did not obtain an interest in the car until years after defendants allegedly acted illegally by seeking and issuing a new title to the car. Thus, the trial court properly dismissed the declaratory judgment action. As to the FOIA claim for an immediate turnover of ownership records, the court found that the 10-day period of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-123(f) (2004) directly regulated vehicle title searches, and that § 2-123, not the FOIA, controlled the requests. The mandamus and quo warranto actions were properly dismissed because the buyer offered no proof that 92 Ill. Admin. Code § 1002.20 was constitutionally invalid for not including sole proprietorships in its definition of a business entity for purposes consistent with the Illinois Vehicle Code.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decisions.

People v. Hernandez


No. 2-06-0548


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


382 Ill. App. 3d 726; 888 N.E.2d 1200; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 433; 321 Ill. Dec. 267



May 13, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 27, 2008
Appeal denied by People v. Hernandez, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1216 (Ill., Sept. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 02-CF-2046. Honorable Kathryn E. Creswell, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which, upon his convictions for predatory criminal sexual assault of a child and aggravated criminal sexual abuse, imposed two concurrent life sentences for the former conviction under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14.1(b)(1.2) (2002) and three concurrent five-year sentences for the latter conviction, to be served consecutively to the life sentences.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that defendant placed his penis into the mouth and buttocks of two six-year-old boys. After he was convicted, the trial court imposed two concurrent life sentences on defendant and also imposed three concurrent five-year sentences, to be served consecutively to the life sentences. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's contention that the mandatory life sentence provision in 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14.1(b)(1.2) (2002) was unconstitutional as applied to him. The court deferred to the legislature's judgment and determined that sentencing defendant to the two concurrent life sentences for his two convictions was not cruel, degrading, or shocking to the moral sense of the community; therefore, it did not violate the proportional penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution. Further, the trial court did not err by imposing two concurrent life sentences for defendant's two convictions for predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. The plain and ordinary meaning of the statute authorized one life sentence for each conviction. However, the trial court erred by ordering the five-year sentences to be served consecutively to the life sentences.


OUTCOME: The court modified defendant's three concurrent five-year sentences to be served concurrently with his two life sentences. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court as modified.

People v. Allen


No. 1-06-1928


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


382 Ill. App. 3d 594; 888 N.E.2d 686; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 419; 321 Ill. Dec. 167



May 12, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 24, 2008.
Appeal denied by People v. Allen, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1011 (Ill., Sept. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 05 CR 23128. Honorable James R. Epstein, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of violating 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.1(a) (2004), granted his motion for a new trial, and vacated that order. He appealed, claiming that § 5/24-1.1(a) unconstitutionally required the State to prove his felon status as an element of the offense, thus depriving him of procedural due process and violating the Equal Protection Clause of the federal and state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The court found that defendant was not denied procedural due process when the trial court accepted a stipulation as to defendant's prior felony convictions for purposes of establishing an element of the offense because the name or nature of the prior conviction was not offered and a stipulation was the least prejudicial way to offer the evidence. A bifurcated trial under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 451(g) was not required because (1) the rule was not effective when defendant was convicted; (2) it only applied where an enhanced sentence was imposed under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/111-3(c-5) (2004); and (3) it did not apply where, as here, the legislature had made a prior felony conviction an element of the offense of unlawful use of a weapon by a felon. The court found that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.1(a) did not violate the equal protection clause of the state or federal constitutions because (1) felons were not a suspect class; (2) all similarly situated felons were treated equally under the statute; and (3) the statute bore a rational relationship to the State's legitimate goal of deterring possession of firearms by felons.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

In re Denetra P.


NO. 4-07-0372


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


382 Ill. App. 3d 538; 904 N.E.2d 44; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 423; 328 Ill. Dec. 282



May 7, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 07MH228. Honorable George H. Ray, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent patient appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which granted petitioner State of Illinois, through a psychiatrist at a state facility, authority to administer psychotropic medications to the patient pursuant to 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-107.1 (2006).


OVERVIEW: The petition lacked the required 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-107.1(a-5)(1) (2006) allegation that the State had made a good faith attempt to determine whether a power of attorney for health care existed. The failure to include the allegation was not, in the instant case, harmless error. Further, § 2-107.1(a-5)(4) had been interpreted to require trial courts to apply the substituted-judgment test before ruling on a petition under the best-interests of the patient test. A power of attorney for health care or a declaration for mental-health treatment was essential to the application of the substituted-judgment test as the test, through a surrogate, attempted to determine what the patient wishes would have been if she had been competent to make decisions. Both the record and the patient's brief indicated that a power of attorney for health care existed. Attempts should have been made to obtain that document before any ruling on the petition was made.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment.

In re Marriage of Gulla


No. 2-07-0387


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


382 Ill. App. 3d 498; 888 N.E.2d 585; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 404; 321 Ill. Dec. 66



May 1, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 20, 2008.
Appeal granted by Gulla v. Knobias, Inc., 229 Ill. 2d 621, 879 N.E.2d 251, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1158, 325 Ill. Dec. 3 (2008)
Affirmed by, Modified by, Remanded by In re Marriage of Gulla, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 920 (Ill., June 4, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 94-D-8. Honorable Joseph R. Waldeck, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Mississippi employer of respondent ex-husband, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which ordered the employer to pay $369,000 to appellee ex-wife as a penalty for knowingly failing to pay child support from the ex-husband's wages as required under the Income Withholding of Support Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 28/35(a) (2006).


OVERVIEW: The employer did not begin withholding income until seven months after it received notice that it should withhold $3,000 per month from the ex-husband's salary. The appellate court affirmed. The notice was properly served under 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 28/20(g) (2006). It informed the employer of its obligation to withhold the income and where to send the income. It also explained that if the amount ordered withheld exceeded the amount allowed by the law of its state, the employer should withhold only the amount allowed by law. The notice also advised the employer to contact the ex-wife's attorney if it had questions regarding the notice. Based on the clarity of the notice, the employer could not rebut the presumption that it knowingly failed to pay over the amounts it was obligated to pay. Contrary to the employer's assertion, under Miss. Code Ann. §§ 93-25-67, -69 (2006) and 42 U.S.C.S. § 666, the trial court properly determined that it had jurisdiction over the employer. Finally, the argument that the Withholding Act was unconstitutional because the penalty was totally disproportionate to the violation being punished had been previously rejected by the state supreme court.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1055 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Hanna v. City of Chicago


No. 1-06-3348


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


382 Ill. App. 3d 672; 887 N.E.2d 856; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 383; 320 Ill. Dec. 712



April 25, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 6, 2008.
Related proceeding at Hanna v. City of Chicago, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 3428 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Mar. 31, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 03 CH 05933. Honorable David R. Donnersberger, Judge Presiding.
Hanna v. City of Chicago, 331 Ill. App. 3d 295, 771 N.E.2d 13, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 369, 264 Ill. Dec. 609 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sued defendant city complaining that his property had been unconstitutionally downzoned. The Circuit Court of Cook County granted the city's motion to dismiss his complaint for failure to state a claim and, on remand, dismissed the complaint as moot. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner's several amended complaints challenged zoning changes that occurred in 1998, 2004 and 2006, and sought declarations that one or all of the rezonings violated his constitutional rights to substantive or procedural due process. On appeal, he invoked the public interest exception to the mootness doctrine. The court declined to accept the invocation, finding that (1) the allegations as to the 1998 and 2004 rezonings were moot because the zoning ordinances were no longer in force; (2) the voluntary cessation doctrine did not apply because there was no showing that the city ceased enforcement until the coast was clear; (3) perpetuating the lawsuit so that the owner could attempt to elevate his personal zoning policy preferences over the city's citizens and their elected officials was not an appropriate use of the judicial system; (4) there was no longer an actual case or controversy between the parties once the city's council amended the municipal zoning ordinance; and (5) the owner had secured the substantive relief he sought, which was to negate the effects of the rezonings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

 

1056 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ehley


NO. 4-07-0150


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


381 Ill. App. 3d 937; 887 N.E.2d 772; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 392; 320 Ill. Dec. 628



April 21, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 06DT707. Honorable Richard P. Klaus, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition in the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) to rescind the Secretary of State's summary suspension of his driver's license based on an alleged refusal to submit to chemical testing of defendant's blood alcohol concentration. The trial court found defendant failed to make a prima facie case for rescission and granted the State's motion for a directed finding. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After medical personnel tested defendant's blood alcohol concentration (BAC), he refused an officer's request to submit to such testing. The appellate court held he raised a proper ground for seeking to rescind the suspension when he said statutes could be interpreted to state that, once medical personnel tested his blood, the arresting officer could not ask him for further tests. The matter was reviewed de novo because it involved statutory construction of whether testing under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501.4(a) (2006) barred the officer from seeking further testing under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501.1(a) (2006). The two statutes' plain language showed each applied to a distinct situation, as results of medical-personnel-directed testing were admissible only in driving under the influence (DUI) or reckless homicide cases and not license suspension proceedings, while results of law-enforcement-directed testing were admissible in such proceedings. Thus, it was not improper for the officer to ask defendant to submit to a test even though he knew hospital staff had already determined defendant's BAC, so it was proper to suspend his driver's license when he refused the request.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1057 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kitch


NO. 4-05-0982


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1353



April 7, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by, Vacated by, Remanded by People v. Kitch, 231 Ill. 2d 643, 899 N.E.2d 1077, 902 N.E.2d 1087, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 164, 326 Ill. Dec. 426 (2009)
Substituted opinion at, On reconsideration by People v. Kitch, 392 Ill. App. 3d 108, 915 N.E.2d 29, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 558, 333 Ill. Dec. 508 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., June 25, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from Circuit of Schuyler County. No. 05CF5. Honorable Alesia A. McMillen, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Circuit of Schuyler County (Illinois) of predatory sexual assault of a child and aggravated sexual abuse, and was sentenced to nine consecutive life terms for the predatory sexual assault of a child and a 14-year extended-term sentence for the aggravated sexual abuse. An appeal on defendant's behalf was dismissed under the fugitive dismissal rule. A petition for rehearing was granted.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the state's highest court had not directly addressed the constitutionality of 725 ILCS 5/115-10(a)(1) (2002) since the Crawford decision. Even if § 115-10 was unconstitutional, the admission of child one's and child two's out-of-court statements was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Child one and the mother testified as to defendant's actions, relating the information they gave in statements to the sheriff and an employee. The employee and child one testified that defendant grabbed child one's breasts and buttocks, showered with her, and rubbed lotion on her breasts. A doctor concluded after a physical exam that child one had been sexually abused. A semen stain on child one's comforter matched defendant's deoxyribonucleic acid profile. While 730 ILCS 5/5-8-4(a)(ii) (2004) and 720 ILCS 5/12-14.1(a)(1), (b)(1.2) (2004) appeared to provide for consecutive sentences, a defendant could only serve multiple life sentences concurrently, and the consecutive life sentences were modified. Finally, even if the fugitive-dismissal rule was a rule of forfeiture, it was appropriate to decide the case on its merits.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified to provide for concurrent life imprisonment terms for the predatory sexual assault convictions. As modified, the convictions were affirmed. The case was remanded for the issuance of an amended sentencing judgment.

Murphy v. Mancari's Chrysler Plymouth, Inc.


No. 1-07-1642


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


381 Ill. App. 3d 768; 887 N.E.2d 569; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 281; 320 Ill. Dec. 425; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P17,976



March 31, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 27, 2008.
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Murphy v. Mancari's Chrysler Plymouth, Inc., 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 297 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Mar. 31, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 06 L 9445. Honorable Jeffrey Lawrence, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff buyers filed a personal injury action asserting strict product liability claims against defendant seller and manufacturer of a vehicle which they purchased. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the seller's motion to dismiss. The buyers appealed. The issue was whether a nonmanufacturer only had to have actual knowledge of the defect for a strict liability claim under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-621(a) (2006).


OVERVIEW: The buyers bought a convertible from the seller. One of the buyers sustained permanent spinal cord injuries when the car rolled over while he was driving it. The buyers alleged that the design of the car proximately caused the injuries and that the car was in an unreasonably dangerous condition when it left the seller's control because the windshield and roof of the car improperly designed and the car was not equipped with sufficient devices to protect the buyer from traumatic injury in a reasonably foreseeable rollover. The buyers alleged the seller knew that the car was not equipped with a sufficient roll bar or other devices to protect the buyer but did not warn the buyers. The appellate court held that in a strict liability action, a "defect" was a product in an unreasonably dangerous condition. 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-621 required the buyers to show that a presumptively dismissed nonmanufacturer had actual knowledge of the unreasonably dangerous nature of the physical characteristics/design of the product, not just actual knowledge that the physical characteristics/design existed, in order to avoid dismissal.


OUTCOME: The appellate court held that the buyers reliance upon the "actual knowledge of the defect" exception to avoid dismissal against the nonmanufacturer had to allege that the nonmanufacturer had actual knowledge of the physical characteristics of the product that the buyers claimed were unreasonably dangerous and that said characteristics made the product unreasonably dangerous. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

Ill. Campaign for Political Reform v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections


No. 1-06-1694


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


382 Ill. App. 3d 51; 886 N.E.2d 1220; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 269; 320 Ill. Dec. 151



March 31, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 27, 2008.
Supplemental opinion at Ill. Campaign for Political Reform v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections, 388 Ill. App. 3d 517, 904 N.E.2d 996, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 93, 328 Ill. Dec. 486 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2009)
Appeal denied by Ill. Campaign for Political Reform v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections, 232 Ill. 2d 580, 910 N.E.2d 1127, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 521, 331 Ill. Dec. 371 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for Review from the Illinois State Board of Elections. No. 05 CD 003.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a political organization and an individual, filed an action against respondents, a political coalition and an individual, in which petitioners alleged that respondents had violated campaign disclosure requirements of the Election Code, 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1 et seq. (2004). The Illinois State Board of Elections dismissed the complaint under 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-21 and 5/1A-7 (2004). Petitioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: A motion was made to find that the complaint was filed on justifiable grounds and to order a public hearing. Because four members voted in favor of the motion and four against, the Board did not achieve a five-vote majority, and the complaint was dismissed based on the deadlock. The court stated that in dismissing the complaint, the Board had acted consistent with 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-21, which had been amended to specifically require a majority vote. The dismissal of the complaint based on the deadlock did not violate petitioners' due process right to judicial review because 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-22 provided for judicial review to any party filing a complaint, whether or not the Board had taken any action. Nothing precluded judicial review in the event of a deadlock vote. Furthermore, the dismissal was not arbitrary and capricious. Nothing in the Code required the deadlock to be broken. The court could not review the dismissal on the merits, however, as there were no findings regarding whether justifiable grounds existed for the filing of the complaint. Remand was required for a statement of findings by the four members who had voted against the motion.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the Board for a statement of findings by the four members who had voted against ordering a public hearing on the complaint.

Ryan v. Commonwealth Edison Co.


No. 1-06-3309


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


381 Ill. App. 3d 877; 885 N.E.2d 544; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 280; 319 Ill. Dec. 273



March 28, 2008, Decided 
March 28, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 7, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 01 L 004073. No. 01 L 004073. Honorable Bill Taylor Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant electrician was injured in an on-the-job circuit breaker explosion. His complaint included a count against his employer and a count against appellee utility. He challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of the utility finding that the action was barred by the construction statute of repose, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-214(b) (2006).


OVERVIEW: The electrician claimed that the statute did not apply because he had not alleged negligent design but negligent failure to perform ongoing maintenance duties on a building's 20-year old electrical system. Whether the utility could invoke the statute's protection to shield itself was in dispute among the state's appellate districts. The appellate court found that there was no question that the utility had a specific duty to maintain its equipment. The duty derived from its capacity as the power supplier and not from its status as installer of the system. The theory of recovery predicated on the utility's alleged failure to discover and repair defects in its power system setup was an activity that was not protected by the statute of repose, notwithstanding the utility's status as an installer of equipment. The court concurred with the holding of the Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District, in MBA Enterprises v. Northern Illinois Gas Company, in finding that the maintenance-related claims did not fall within the scope of the construction statute of repose as defined by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

People v. Baltimore


Nos. 2-06-0689 & 2-06-0690 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


381 Ill. App. 3d 115; 885 N.E.2d 1096; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 208; 319 Ill. Dec. 416



March 17, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 2, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 05--CF--2916. Honorable Grant S. Wegner, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeals dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed an appeal under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(a)(1) after the Circuit Court of Kane County, Illinois, entered an adverse ruling regarding the State's use of a surveillance videotape at defendant's burglary trial. Defendant then appealed an order that, as part of defendant's release under Rule 604(a)(3), required him to report to court services weekly until the State's appeal was resolved.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the State's appeal. The appellate court granted the motion. The surveillance footage was obtained from the store defendant was alleged to have burglarized. Due to technical issues with the surveillance footage, the State wanted to use a second videotape created from the original material. However, the State was unable to create a second videotape that was an accurate reflection of the original surveillance tape. The trial court's order did not prohibit the State from presenting the surveillance footage to the jury. The trial court's order merely required the State to present the original surveillance tape to the jury. The order did not suppress the subject evidence, it merely impacted the manner in which the information was to be presented to the jury. As a result, a Rule 604(a)(1) appeal was not available to the State. As to defendant's appeal, assuming arguendo that the State's appeal provided the appellate court jurisdiction to consider defndant's appeal, it lost that jurisdiction when it dismissed the State's appeal. Further, the appellate court's decision rendered defendant's appeal moot.


OUTCOME: The appellate court dismissed both the appeal filed by the State and the appeal filed by defendant.

Rosenbaum-Golden v. Golden


No. 1-07-2940


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


381 Ill. App. 3d 65; 884 N.E.2d 1272; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 185; 319 Ill. Dec. 27



March 6, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Rosenbaum-Golden v. Golden, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 5618 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Apr. 1, 2008)
Appeal denied by Rosenbaum-Golden v. Golden, 229 Ill. 2d 659, 897 N.E.2d 263, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1019, 325 Ill. Dec. 15 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Domestic Relations Division. No. 04 D 1240. Honorable Charles Winkler, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; contempt order vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a dissolution of marriage action between petitioner wife and respondent husband, the Circuit Court of Cook County, Domestic Relations Division (Illinois), awarded the wife interim attorney fees pursuant to 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/501(c-1) (2004), and later found the husband in contempt for failure to pay that award. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband argued that the petition was barred by a provision of their premarital agreement that provided that the wife and the husband waived their rights to attorney fees. The appellate court found, however, that there was not a violation of the premarital agreement, as the interim fees that the trial court awarded constituted an advance against the marital estate. 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/501(c-1)(2) (2004) created a presumption that interim attorney fee awards were deemed advances from the marital estate. Contrary to the husband's argument, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/501(c-1) (2004) did not substantially impair any contractual obligation that the parties had regarding attorney fees, and did not violate the Contract Clauses of the United States Constitution, U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, or the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 16. Documentary evidence attached to the wife's petition supported the conclusion that she lacked sufficient access to assets or income to pay attorney fees, and the award was reasonable. Because the husband represented that the issue was not to have been contemptuous, but to test the order's validity, it was proper to vacate the citation.


OUTCOME: The contempt order was vacated. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

Yoder v. Ferguson


Nos. 1-04-3214 & 1-04-3230 Consolidated


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


381 Ill. App. 3d 353; 885 N.E.2d 1060; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 186; 319 Ill. Dec. 380



March 6, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Yoder v. Ferguson, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 5621 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Apr. 3, 2008)
Appeal withdrawn by Yoder v. Ferguson, 232 Ill. 2d 598, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 2345, 331 Ill. Dec. 377 (2009)
Appeal withdrawn by Yoder v. Alexander, 232 Ill. 2d 597, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 2344, 331 Ill. Dec. 377 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 02 L 3002, 02 L 3003, 02 L 3004, 02 L 3005. Honorable Daniel M. Locallo, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, multiple vehicle drivers and others, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which was entered in favor of plaintiff, a mother individually and on behalf of her disabled child and her deceased child, in her negligence action that arose from a multi-vehicle accident. Post-trial motions by some of the drivers were denied.


OVERVIEW: Due to the multi-vehicle accident that left one member of the mother's family dead and the others severely injured, she filed suit against multiple parties, including her husband who was driving the family vehicle at the time. She entered into settlement agreements with various defendants, and thereafter, a large jury verdict was entered in her favor. The trial court properly determined that the settlements were reached in good faith.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court with respect to the contribution judgments, which were vacated, and as to the failure to grant defendants a full setoff for the judgment against one of the settling defendants. The remainder of the trial court judgment was affirmed.

People v. Larson


No. 2-06-0096


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


379 Ill. App. 3d 642; 885 N.E.2d 363; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 189; 319 Ill. Dec. 92



March 5, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 18, 2008.
Appeal denied by People v. Larson, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 601 (Ill., May 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County. No. 04--CF--260. Honorable Gerald F. Grubb, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Boone County (Illinois), which after a jury verdict found him guilty of committing the offenses of aggravated cruelty to an animal (510 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 70/3.02 (2004)) and possession of a firearm without a firearm owner's identification (FOID) card (430 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 65/2(a)(1) (2004)). The trial court imposed a sentence of 12 months' probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his conviction had to be reversed because the aggravated-cruelty-to-an-animal statute was unconstitutionally vague. The appeals court disagreed, as its review of the statute did not reveal inconsistent terminology or terms without definition or meaning that could not be discerned from their context. Defendant argued that the statute failed to define "euthanasia," but it appeared that euthanasia would refer to the painless or humane killing of a companion animal. The appeals court believed that anyone who earnestly attempted to understand the statute could fully comprehend its terms and phrases and understand what was prohibited. A rational trier of fact could have concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was criminally culpable for aggravated cruelty to an animal for shooting a family dog. Defendant admitted that he took the dog outside and away from home and shot the dog three times using a.45-caliber handgun, causing the dog's death. There was sufficient evidence to conclude that defendant knowingly possessed a firearm on October 10, 2004, without a FOID card, as the card submitted into evidence reflected that it had expired January 1, 2002.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Cardamone


No. 2-06-0117


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


379 Ill. App. 3d 656; 883 N.E.2d 628; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 105; 318 Ill. Dec. 397



February 14, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 4, 2008.
Related proceeding at People v. Cardamone, 381 Ill. App. 3d 462, 885 N.E.2d 1159, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 286, 319 Ill. Dec. 479 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2008)
Appeal granted by People v. Cardamone, 228 Ill. 2d 538, 889 N.E.2d 1117, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 390, 321 Ill. Dec. 557 (2008)
Affirmed by People v. Cardamone, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 304 (Ill., Mar. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 04--CF--2254. Honorable George J. Bakalis, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of harassment of a witness (720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/32-4a(a) (2000)). The trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial and sentenced him to three years' imprisonment. The court subsequently denied his motion to reconsider his sentence. Defendant appealed, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence for his conviction.


OVERVIEW: The State alleged that defendant, with the intent to harass or annoy a potential witness in a pending legal proceeding against him, communicated indirectly with the potential witness, in that he placed a 911 call and falsely reported that she committed or was committing traffic offenses. The call resulted in a police officer effecting a traffic stop in such a manner as to produce mental anguish and emotional distress. The appeals court found that the evidence was sufficient to establish that the potential witness suffered mental anguish or emotional distress as a result of defendant's false report. She testified that the incident was "nerve wracking" and defendant conceded that the potential witness was upset as a result of being pulled over by the police. The evidence was also sufficient to establish that defendant communicated with the potential witness. He indirectly communicated with her by calling the police and effecting the stop. The potential witness was aware of the indirect communication from defendant. She testified that, upon being stopped by an officer, she told the officer that she knew that defendant had made the 911 call.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Harvey


No. 1-06-1930


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


379 Ill. App. 3d 518; 884 N.E.2d 724; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 95; 318 Ill. Dec. 756



February 13, 2008, Decided 
February 13, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 3, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 92 CR 6652(01). Honorable Evelyn B. Clay, Judge Presiding.
People v. Harvey, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 328 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Feb. 7, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted appellee State of Illinois' motion to dismiss the inmate's 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2004) petition for relief from judgment.


OVERVIEW: In his §2-1401 petition, the inmate asserted that the dismissal of his prior postconviction petition was a void judgment because the trial court did not properly dispose of a contemporaneous motion for substitution of judge, in contravention of 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/114-5(d) (1994). The appellate court affirmed. The inmate filed his substitution motion under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-8 (2004). Thus, the requirement in 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/114-5(d) that the motion be considered before any other action was taken did not apply. Further, while 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-8 provided that a judge other than the one who presided over a trial should consider a postconviction petition, that statute had been ruled unconstitutional a full 10 years prior to the inmate's motion. Even if the motion had been under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/114-5(d), the statute did not apply to postconviction proceedings. The inmate had no right to a substitution of counsel in such proceedings. Finally, the inmate failed to present any evidence of prejudice or arbitrariness by the trial court that would have required its recusal.


OUTCOME: The order denying the 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2004) petition was affirmed.

People v. Mescall


No. 2-06-0287


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


379 Ill. App. 3d 670; 883 N.E.2d 612; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 104; 318 Ill. Dec. 381



February 11, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 4, 2008.
Appeal denied by People v. Mescall, 228 Ill. 2d 545, 889 N.E.2d 1120, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 391, 321 Ill. Dec. 560 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County. No. 96--CF--170. Honorable Gerald F. Grubb, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Mescall, 347 Ill. App. 3d 995, 808 N.E.2d 1101, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 401, 283 Ill. Dec. 813 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Boone County (Illinois), which dismissed with prejudice the inmate's 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2006) petition in which the inmate sought relief from an allegedly void judgment. The petition was filed outside the two-year time period for filing stated in the statute.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had been convicted on an amended information that charged, inter alia, four counts of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child (PCSA) under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14.1(a)(1) (1996). The petition alleged that the information was defective because some of the conduct complained of was alleged to have occurred before the effective date of the statute. As a result, the inmate argued that the trial court had lacked jurisdiction to enter a judgment of conviction on the PCSA counts. The appellate court affirmed. A defective information or indictment did not deprive a trial court of jurisdiction. While the inmate was correct that the amended information was defective, the trial court still had jurisdiction to enter a judgment of conviction. Because the trial court had jurisdiction, the judgment rendered was voidable, and the inmate's 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 petition was subject to the limitations period under § 2-1401(c). Thus, the inmate's failure to timely file his § 2-1401 petition or prove any grounds to excuse his untimeliness barred his petition.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the inmate's § 2-1401 petition with prejudice was affirmed.
