People v. Singleton


No. 1-06-1115


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1352



February 5, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Singleton, 231 Ill. 2d 650, 902 N.E.2d 1089, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 157, 327 Ill. Dec. 703 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98 CR 13718. Honorable Lon William Shultz, Judge Presiding.
People v. Singleton, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1945 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Feb. 5, 2008)
People v. Singleton, 203 Ill. 2d 566, 788 N.E.2d 734, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 763, 273 Ill. Dec. 143 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sua sponte dismissing his pro se petition pursuant to the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 ILCS 5/122-1 et seq. (2006), and 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 (2006), and assessed the inmate $ 105 in costs and fees. The inmate had been convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault and armed robbery, and sentenced to consecutive terms of 58 and 30 years respectively.


OVERVIEW: The inmate contended that the trial court erred by recharacterizing his 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 (2006) petition as a post-conviction petition without admonishing him that it was doing so. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the inmate expressly invoked the Act in his petition and that the postconviction court clearly considered the inmate's petition under both the Act and § 2-1401, denying leave to file a successive petition under the former and dismissing it sua sponte under the latter. The inmate also contends that the trial court erred in assessing costs and fees under 735 ILCS 5/22-105 (2006) for filing a frivolous petition when he was denied leave to file a successive post-conviction petition. The appellate court disagreed, finding that § 22-105 applied to the inmate's petition, a § 2-1401 filed against the State and commencing a new, collateral action attacking a judgment in the State's favor. Lastly, the appellate court found no merit in the inmate's contention that the costs and fees pursuant to § 22-105 violated his constitutional right to equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the postconviction court was affirmed.

 

1069 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Irvine


No. 1-06-0005


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


379 Ill. App. 3d 116; 882 N.E.2d 1124; 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 53; 318 Ill. Dec. 1



January 31, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 18, 2008.
Appeal denied by People v. Irvine, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 441 (Ill., May 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 05 MC1 439010. The Hon. Kay Marie Hanlon, Judge Presiding.
People v. Irvine, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1302 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 20, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) finding him guilty of domestic battery in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-3.2 (2004) and sentencing him to 12 months of conditional discharge, to mandatory domestic violence classes, and to fees and fines of $ 379.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court found that the relationship between the complainant and defendant qualified as a serious courtship in the context of 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/112A-3(3) (2004), because they dated for six weeks and continued to have sexual intercourse up to and including the date of their altercation. Six weeks of dating coupled with sexual intercourse was not a casual acquaintanceship. Accordingly, defendant and the complainant were "family members" within the purview of the domestic violence statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-3.2(a)(1) (2004). The language in § 12-3.2(a)(1) and the definition for "family members" in 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/112A-3(3) (2004) were explicit enough to serve as a guide for those who had to comply with and interpret the domestic violence statute, and defendant's vagueness challenge to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-3.2(a)(1) (2004) failed. Defendant failed to establish the deficiency prong of the Strickland test for ineffective assistance of counsel. In light of the fact that defendant personally spoke with a witness on the day of the altercation, he could have informed his attorney to conduct an investigation.


OUTCOME: Defendant was entitled to a credit of $ 10 for two days he was incarcerated prior to sentencing. A $ 30 minor traffic ordinance violation fee imposed by the trial court pursuant to 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 105/27.2a (2004) of the Clerks of Courts Act was vacated. Defendant's conviction and sentences were affirmed as modified.

1071 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Ploense v. Electrolux Home Prods.


NO. 4-06-0894


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


377 Ill. App. 3d 1091; 882 N.E.2d 653; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1401; 317 Ill. Dec. 773



December 28, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 05L202. Honorable James E. Souk, Judge Presiding.
Ploense v. Chrome Coalition, 223 Ill. 2d 684, 862 N.E.2d 1001, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 710, 308 Ill. Dec. 798 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff widow sued defendants, including a nonresident coalition and manufacturers, alleging wrongful death and a civil conspiracy to suppress knowledge of the harmful health effects of chrome. The coalition specially appeared and moved to dismiss the action against it for lack of personal jurisdiction. The Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) denied the motion. The coalition petitioned for leave to appeal, which was granted on review.


OVERVIEW: The widow alleged that the decedent contracted lung cancer due to his exposure to chrome while working. The widow alleged that defendants conspired to spread false information that chrome posed no hazard to human health. The coalition disseminated information relating to chrome, but had no financial investment in any of the manufacturers and did not share in their profits. The appellate court determined that dismissal of the coalition was warranted because personal jurisdiction did not exist over the coalition. Personal jurisdiction was unavailable under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-209(a)(2) (2006) because it was not the coalition but a manufacturer or distributor that actually committed the tortious or injury-causing act in Illinois by selling chrome products without hazardous warnings. Personal jurisdiction was unavailable under § 2-209(c) because (1) despite coconspirators' activities, there was a total absence of affiliating circumstances between the coalition and Illinois, (2) the widow did not allege any activity that the coalition purposefully directed at Illinois, and (3) there was no evidence that the coalition had any agreement with coconspirators regarding Illinois.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the circuit court's judgment.

People v. Keith C. (In re Keith C.)


No. 1-06-1807


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


378 Ill. App. 3d 252; 880 N.E.2d 1157; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1366; 317 Ill. Dec. 165



December 27, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 13, 2008.
Appeal denied by People v. Keith C. (In re Keith C.), 2008 Ill. LEXIS 831 (Ill., Mar. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 04 JD 5661. Honorable Arthur Hill, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile was found guilty of aggravated battery and armed robbery. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to serve the minimum disposition, five years' probation, and ordered him to complete 20 hours of community service. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Despite the fact that the victim did not have an opportunity to view her assailants at the time of the crime, the appellate court concluded that her identification was sufficient as, inter alia, she had two opportunities to view them just before the robbery. Any inconsistencies in the victim's testimony was for the trier of fact to resolve. The appellate court also found it "practically certain" that throwing a brick at the windshield of an occupied car would result in great bodily harm to the driver, thereby supporting the battery conviction. Next, the appellate court found no error in the trial court's refusal to permit expert identification testimony, as the testimony would have been based on speculation given that there was no evidence on whether the victim was admonished at the lineup. The appellate court found that the admission of hearsay evidence as to the victim's identification of her cell phone was not reversible error, as the victim testified and was available for cross-examination. Finally, the appellate court concluded that defendant failed to show that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2004), providing for testing of DNA, was unconstitutional as applied to him.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Beaty


NO. 5-05-0511


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


377 Ill. App. 3d 861; 880 N.E.2d 237; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1417; 316 Ill. Dec. 759



December 27, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Beaty, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 5632 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., Jan. 10, 2008)
Appeal denied by People v. Beaty, 228 Ill. 2d 537, 889 N.E.2d 1117, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 534, 321 Ill. Dec. 557 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Beaty v. Illinois, 555 U.S. 914, 129 S. Ct. 264, 172 L. Ed. 2d 197, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 6129 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Christian County. No. 03-CF-20. Honorable Ronald D. Spears, Judge, presiding.
People v. Beaty, 351 Ill. App. 3d 717, 814 N.E.2d 590, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 857, 286 Ill. Dec. 602 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Christian County (Illinois), which convicted him of four counts each of aggravated criminal sexual assault and criminal sexual assault, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14(a)(2) and 12-13(a)(1) (2002). The trial court imposed a mandatory natural-life sentence on each conviction.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant arose from his sexual assault on his ex-wife. The trial court granted the State's motion to admit defendant's prior criminal record as substantive evidence pursuant to § 115-7.3(b) of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-7.3(b) (2004). After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of all charges and he was sentenced. On appeal, the court found that admission of the prior convictions was proper, as the State used it to show that the ex-wife understood defendant's threats and to show defendant's propensity to commit the acts. Section 115-7.3 did not violate the federal or Illinois due process or equal protection clauses. Defendant was not denied a fair trial under a plain error standard of review where no Boose hearing was held prior to the trial court requiring him to wear a "leg device" that prevented him from bending his knee enough to run. The device was hidden from the jury's view and no prejudice was shown. Defendant failed to show his counsel was ineffective on a number of issues, and he also failed to show errors in evidentiary rulings under the plain error standard pursuant to 134 Ill. 2d R. 615(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

People v. Rogelio S. (In re Rogelio S.)


No. 1-06-1603


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


378 Ill. App. 3d 211; 882 N.E.2d 612; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1357; 317 Ill. Dec. 732



December 26, 2007, Decided 
December 26, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 13, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Stuart F. Lubin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent juvenile appealed after the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) adjudicated him delinquent for committing aggravated criminal sexual abuse. At sentencing, respondent was told that when he turned 17 he would need to register under the Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/1 et seq. (2006). He was also ordered to submit buccal swab saliva specimens pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2006).


OVERVIEW: Respondent originally argued that requiring him to register as a sex offender under the Registration Act and the Sex Offender Community Notification Law, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 152/121 (2006), was unconstitutional. However, the parties agreed that the argument was rendered moot by 2007 Ill. Laws 658, which eliminated the provision in the Registration Act that required juveniles to register as adult sex offenders upon turning 17 years of age. Respondent's second argument was that the compulsory extraction of his saliva and perpetual storing of his DNA profile violated his constitutional right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures. The appellate court rejected that argument based on the state supreme court's decision in Garvin and the appellate court's own prior rulings. 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 did not violate a juvenile's right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures, despite the argument that juveniles had a greater right to privacy than adult offenders.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Vill. of Oak Lawn v. Faber


No. 1-06-2622


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


378 Ill. App. 3d 458; 880 N.E.2d 659; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1356; 316 Ill. Dec. 923



December 21, 2007, Decided 
December 21, 2007, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 05 CH 19575. Honorable Sophia Hall Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff village sued defendant former employee, alleging that the employee's severance constituted unjust enrichment and violated Ill. Const. art. 8, § 1, the village's code of ethics, and 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-3-7 and 8-1-7(b) (2004). The Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, granted summary judgment in favor of the employee. The village appealed.


OVERVIEW: The village alleged that prior to the date a newly elected village board of trustees was to take office, the outgoing village board voted to terminate the employee's employment as village manager so that he could claim a severance package totaling nine months of his salary. The appellate court determined that the outgoing board's renewal of the employee's employment did not provide the employee with any right to severance that he did not already enjoy. The severance did not constitute an unconstitutional gift of public funds in violation of Ill. Const. art. 8, § 1, because the employee's past performance constituted adequate consideration for the severance and his severance pay had a public benefit. The village's code of ethics did not prohibit the village from offering severance pay as part of an employment contract. Regarding the village's argument that the employee's term could not exceed the term of the village president, there was no violation of 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/8-1-7(b), because the employee was terminable at will. The employee's term of employment satisfied the indefiniteness requirement of 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-3-7 because he was terminable at will.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Pooh-Bah Enters. v. County of Cook


No. 1-05-2924


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


378 Ill. App. 3d 268; 881 N.E.2d 552; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1354; 317 Ill. Dec. 384



December 21, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Pooh-Bah Enters. v. County of Cook, 227 Ill. 2d 596, 888 N.E.2d 1188, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 829, 321 Ill. Dec. 255 (2008)
Appeal granted by Pooh-Bah Enters. v. County of Cook, 227 Ill. 2d 596, 888 N.E.2d 1188, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 851, 321 Ill. Dec. 255 (2008)
Later proceeding at Pooh-Bah Enters. v. County of Cook, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 36 (Ill., Jan. 20, 2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by Pooh-Bah Enters. v. County of Cook, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 308 (Ill., Mar. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Alexander P. White, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff adult cabaret operator sued defendants, a county, a city, and a county official, alleging that defendants' amusement tax exemptions for small, fine arts venues that excluded adult entertainment cabarets violated the First Amendment and the free speech clause of the Illinois Constitution. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted defendants' motions to dismiss. The operator appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants imposed on patrons of any amusement a tax on the admission price to enter, witness, view, or participate in any amusement within their boundaries. With the intent to foster the production of live performances that offered theatrical, musical, or cultural enrichment, defendants amended their amusement tax ordinances to include a small-venue exemption, but the exemption excluded performances conducted at adult entertainment cabarets. The appellate court determined that the adult entertainment cabaret exclusions from the amusement tax small-venue exemptions violated the First Amendment because they were content-based regulations on speech that did not serve a compelling state interest. The exclusions, on their face, discriminated based on content because they defined an adult entertainment cabaret by the content of the expression featured at the establishment. Defendants' interests did not rise to the level of a compelling state interest that would justify a content-based restriction on protected expression. The appellate court rejected defendants' contention that affirmative government policies encouraging selective private speech did not implicate the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the circuit court's judgment.

People v. Christopherson


No. 2-06-0839


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


377 Ill. App. 3d 752; 879 N.E.2d 1035; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1308; 316 Ill. Dec. 647



December 19, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 1, 2008.
Appeal granted by People v. Christopherson, 227 Ill. 2d 587, 888 N.E.2d 1185, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 797, 321 Ill. Dec. 252 (2008)
Affirmed by People v. Christopherson, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1435 (Ill., Nov. 20, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 06--CM--871. Honorable Charles P. Weech, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with unlawful delivery of alcoholic liquor to a person under the age of 21 (a minor) in violation of § 6-16(a)(iii) of the Illinois Liquor Control Act of 1934, 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-16(a)(iii) (2004). The Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) granted defendant's motion to dismiss. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant were dismissed after the trial court agreed with defendant that 6-16(a)(iii) (2004) did not apply to minors who sold, gave, or delivered alcohol to other minors. On appeal, the State argued that the trial court erred in dismissing the charge against defendant because 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-16(a)(iii) (2004) did prohibit minors from distributing alcohol to other minors. The appellate court agreed with the State. The appellate court found that the references to people within certain age ranges in § 6-16 demonstrated that the legislature, if it intended to do so, clearly had the ability and knowledge to limit the term "person" to those over the age of 21. The appellate court's interpretation of the statute was not inconsistent with the public policy of Illinois and did not defeat the purpose of the statute: to protect the health, safety, and welfare of the public and to promote temperance in the consumption of alcohol, 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1-2 (2004). Finally, the appellate court concluded that the fact that minors were treated differently in other statutes did not warrant the same determination in this instance.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Cook County Republican Party v. State Bd. of Elections


Nos. 1-05-3407, 1-05-3408, 1-05-3409, 1-05-3410, 1-05-3411, 1-05-3412, 1-05-3413, 1-05-3414, 1-05-3415 and 1-05-3416, Consolidated

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for Review from the Illinois State Board of Elections. No. 05 CD 44. Petition for Review from the Illinois State Board of Elections. No. 05 CD 45. Petition for Review from the Illinois State Board of Elections. No. 05 CD 46. Petition for Review from the Illinois State Board of Elections. No. 05 CD 47. Petition for Review from the Illinois State Board of Elections. No. 05 CD 50. Petition for Review from the Illinois State Board of Elections. No. 05 CD 55. Petition for Review from the Illinois State Board of Elections. No. 05 CD 56. Petition for Review from the Illinois State Board of Elections. No. 05 CD 57. Petition for Review from the Illinois State Board of Elections. No. 05 CD 58. Petition for Review from the Illinois State Board of Elections. No. 05 CD 59.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent state elections board (Illinois) entered a decision that dismissed, without a public hearing, 10 complaints alleging Election Code, 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1-1 et seq. (2004), violations involving respondent politicians. Petitioner county political party chairman appealed, and requested that the appellate court reverse the board's dismissal in each case and remand the causes for a public hearing on the merits.

The board by a majority vote in two cases dismissed two complaints for lack of justifiable grounds. The board reached a tie vote on the remaining eight complaints and dismissed those complaints in compliance with 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-21 (2004). The board issued a final, written order in each case dismissing the complaint. The appellate court found that no clear error occurred in the majority vote cases because justifiable grounds did not support the chairman's filing of the complaints. Regarding the tie-vote cases, the appellate court found that the trial court properly dismissed those cases because the board did not give the 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-21 (2004) majority vote necessary for the complaints to survive.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the board's decision regarding dismissal of all 10 complaints.

People v. Morgan


No. 3-06-0362


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


377 Ill. App. 3d 821; 881 N.E.2d 507; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1310; 317 Ill. Dec. 339



December 14, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 5, 2008.
Appeal denied by People v. Morgan, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 755 (Ill., Mar. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 14th Judicial Circuit, Rock Island County, Illinois. No. 05-CF-260. Honorable Charles H. Stengel, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, the 14th Judicial Circuit Court, Rock Island County (Illinois), convicted defendant of knowingly residing within 500 feet of a school building that persons under the age of 18 attended, a violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-9.3(b-5) (2006). It then sentenced him to probation, fined him $ 1,000, and imposed an additional $ 40 fine for the Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in 1997 of a sex offense involving a child. The legislature enacted § 11-9.3 in 1998, prohibiting the presence of sex offenders in school zones. The statute was amended in July 2000 to include § 11-9.3(b-5). Defendant was released from prison in 1999. He was arrested on the instant charge in April 2005. The appellate court found that § 11-9.3(b-5) was not an impermissible ex post facto law because it protected the public rather than punishing defendant. The appellate court also found that pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/110-14 (2006), defendant was entitled to a $ 5 per day credit on the eight days he had served. Finally, the fine imposed by the trial court for the victims' fund was improper because under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 240/10(c) (2006) that fine could only be imposed if no other fine had been imposed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction. The appellate court also vacated the Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund fine and directed the trial court to grant defendant a $ 40 credit against defendant's $ 1,000 fine.

Chicagoland Chamber of Commerce v. Pappas


No. 1-05-1488


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


378 Ill. App. 3d 334; 880 N.E.2d 1105; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1285; 317 Ill. Dec. 113



December 14, 2007, Decided 
December 14, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 29, 2008.
Appeal denied by Chicagoland Chamber of Commerce v. Pappas, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 855 (Ill., Mar. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, County Department, Chancery Division. No. 04 CH 16874. Honorable Sophia Hall, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the nonprofit organizations and the taxpayers, sued appellee county officials in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for declaratory and injunctive relief regarding the enactment by the Illinois General Assembly of an alternative homestead exemption. Appellee, the Illinois Department of Revenue, intervened. The court dismissed the complaint for failure to state a claim. The organizations and the taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The organizations and the taxpayers claimed that the alternative homestead exemption in the amendment to 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/15-176 (2004) was unconstitutional. They further claimed that their due process rights were violated by a retroactive increase of their property taxes. On appeal, the court found that (1) 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/15-176 did not unconstitutionally delegate to the counties the exclusive power of the Illinois General Assembly under Ill Const. art. IX, § 6 to create an alternative homestead exemption; (2) the exemption contained in 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/15-176 did not create a constitutionally infirm nonuniform real property taxation under Ill. Const. art. IX, § 4(a); (3) the amendment was not an ultra vires act by the General Assembly but the enactment of a constitutionally permissible homestead exemption under Ill. Const. art. IX, § 6; (4) 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/15-176 did not violate the taxpayers' right to equal protection under Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, nor their right under Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 to not be disadvantaged by special legislation; and (5) 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/15-176 was not improperly retroactively applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

People v. Holley


No. 3-05-0382


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


377 Ill. App. 3d 809; 879 N.E.2d 530; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1274; 316 Ill. Dec. 463



December 7, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 28, 2008.
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Holley, 2016 IL App (3d) 140287-U, 2016 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1253 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois, No. 04--CF--1020. Honorable James E. Shadid, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County (Illinois), denied defendant's pro se motion for a new trial and entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of aggravated criminal sexual assault. It then sentenced defendant to 24 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State charged defendant with committing aggravated criminal sexual assault by the use of force or threat of force while displaying a dangerous weapon, a handgun, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14(a)(1) (2004). At trial, the victim testified that defendant sexually penetrated her while threatening her with a handgun. The jury found defendant guilty. The trial court did not rule on defendant's post-trial motion claim that he discussed with his attorney having a bench trial. It denied the motion and sentenced defendant. The appellate court found that upon remand, the trial court had to consider whether defendant should have a new attorney argue his ineffective assistance of counsel claim because it was not clear whether defendant's trial counsel neglected the bench trial request. It also found that defendant should not have been sentenced under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14(a)(1), as that provision required that the crime be committed with something other than a firearm. Finally, it found that he lacked standing to claim that the statute he should have been sentenced under violated the Illinois Constitution because he was not sentenced under it.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment of conviction was affirmed, the sentence imposed by the trial court was vacated, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings as directed.

Adames v. Sheahan


No. 1-05-3911


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


378 Ill. App. 3d 502; 880 N.E.2d 559; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1263; 316 Ill. Dec. 823



November 29, 2007, Decided 
November 29, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 22, 2008.
Appeal granted by Adames v. Sheahan, 227 Ill. 2d 577, 888 N.E.2d 1182, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 775, 321 Ill. Dec. 249 (2008)
Appeal granted by Adames v. Sheahan, 227 Ill. 2d 577, 888 N.E.2d 1182, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 710, 321 Ill. Dec. 249 (2008)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Adames v. Sheahan, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 310 (Ill., Mar. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 L 05894. Honorable Carol Pearce McCarthy, Judge Presiding.
Adames v. Sheahan, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1084 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Oct. 11, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part, remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the co-special administrators of the estate of a deceased child sued defendants, a sheriff, a gun manufacturer, and others, seeking to recover for the death of the child, who died after he was shot by a friend who was playing with the service weapon of his father, who was a deputy sheriff. The administrators appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendants' motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The friend found the deputy's service weapon in the deputy's bedroom closet. While playing, the friend accidentally shot the decedent. The administrators sued the sheriff based on a respondeat superior theory and sued the manufacturer based on a strict products liability theory. Reversing the grant of summary judgment to the sheriff, the court found that (1) the deputy stored his weapon at home in the course of his employment; (2) although the friend was adjudicated a delinquent in juvenile court for violating § 24-9 of the Criminal Code, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-9, the juvenile adjudication was not tantamount to a criminal conviction, which would have absolved the sheriff of respondeat superior liability; and (3) the incident was reasonably foreseeable. With regard to the manufacturer, summary judgment was proper as to the defective design claim because, inter alia, the gun performed as expected and was not unreasonably dangerous for its intended use as a law enforcement service weapon. The manufacturer was not entitled to summary judgment on the failure to warn claim as there was no warning that a gun could fire a chambered bullet when the magazine was removed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to the sheriff on the issue of respondeat superior. The court also reversed the grant of summary judgment to the manufacturer with regard to the duty to warn claim. The court affirmed the remainder of the trial court's order.

People v. Moore

Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/116-3(b)(1) (2004).

People v. Gildart


No. 1-06-1484


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


377 Ill. App. 3d 39; 879 N.E.2d 410; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1167; 316 Ill. Dec. 343



November 7, 2007, Decided 
November 7, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 20, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 05 CR 5361. Honorable Victoria Stewart, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) imposed a sentence of probation and $ 1,235 in fines, fees, and costs, including a $ 10 mental health court charge and a $ 5 youth diversion/peer court charge pursuant to 55 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-1101(e), (e)(2) (2006). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the youth diversion/peer court charges, and argued that the charges violated his due process rights. Defendant argued that because there was no rational relationship between a conviction for possession of a controlled substance and the public interests that induced the legislature to create the charge, it was unconstitutional. The appellate court found that the youth diversion/peer court charge was not deemed to compensate the State for any costs incurred as a result of prosecuting defendant, and thus, these charges were fines notwithstanding the language of the statute. The charge was mandatory for any offender convicted of, inter alia, a felony. Clearly then the charge was not intended to reimburse the State for any of the costs of prosecution. As a fine, it was to have been upheld, under a due process analysis, unless the amount was wildly disproportionate to the underlying offense. There was certainly not such disproportionality under circumstances in which the fine was $ 5. The State conceded that the total of the fines, fees, and costs was overstated by $ 20.


OUTCOME: The appellate court ordered that the total amount assessed against defendant be reduced by $ 20 to reflect the correct total of $ 1,215. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

People v. Johnson


NOS. 5-05-0461 & 5-05-0620 (cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


377 Ill. App. 3d 854; 879 N.E.2d 977; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1163; 316 Ill. Dec. 589



November 5, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied, January 22, 2008.
Rehearing denied by, 01/22/2008
Appeal denied by People v. Johnson, 228 Ill. 2d 542, 889 N.E.2d 1119, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 539, 321 Ill. Dec. 559 (2008)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by People v. Johnson, 2013 IL App (5th) 110112, 2013 Ill. App. LEXIS 713 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 99-CF-995. Honorable Annette A. Eckert, Judge, presiding.
People v. Johnson, 213 Ill. 2d 568, 829 N.E.2d 791, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 136, 293 Ill. Dec. 866 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of two courts of first degree murder. The convictions were affirmed on direct appeal. The inmate filed a petition for relief from judgment which the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) dismissed. The inmate then filed a petition for post conviction relief against appellee State, which the trial court also dismissed. The inmate appealed both rulings, and the appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's first-stage dismissal was on the ground that all the issues raised were barred by either res judicata or waiver. The appellate court found, however, that the petition presented the gist of a constitutional claim. Four claims of error in the petition did not include allegations of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel, but because some of the claims were not subject to a dismissal at the first stage, the entire postconviction petition was required to be docketed for second-stage proceedings. Based on exhibits attached to the petition and citations to the record, the appellate court rejected the State's contention that the petition could have been properly dismissed on the basis of a failure to attach affidavits or other supporting evidence. Consideration of the State's arguments related to the merits of the petition was not needed because the arguments required the appellate court to go beyond a "quick look" at the record. These were the types of arguments that should have been argued to the trial court at the second stage of the procedure.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

In re Marriage of Rife


No. 2-06-1048


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


376 Ill. App. 3d 1050; 878 N.E.2d 775; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1143; 316 Ill. Dec. 53



October 24, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 03--DV--669. Honorable Michael W. Feetterer, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent former husband sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), which denied his petition under § 2-701 of the Code of Civil Procedure, the Declaratory Judgment Act (DJA), 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-701 (2004), wherein he sought a determination that petitioner former wife's response to his postdissolution petitions invoked a modification clause (MC) of the parties' marital settlement agreement (MSA).


OVERVIEW: The MSA, which was incorporated into the parties' dissolution judgment, provided joint custody over their two children. The husband was required to use funds to establish an individual retirement account (IRA) in the wife's name for her use monthly as child support (CS). The MC of the MSA provided that if the wife sought to modify the custody, visitation, or CS, her right to withdraw same from the IRA would cease and those funds would transfer to an IRA in the husband's name. The husband thereafter filed postdissolution petitions, and in response, the wife sought a change in the children's day to day care. The husband sought relief under the DJA based on the MC. The trial court held that the wife's response to the postdissolution petitions was not itself a "petition" as defined by the MC of the parties' MSA. Accordingly, there was no transfer of the IRA funds required. On appeal, the court initially clarified the appropriate standard of review. It then held that the MC was not enforceable under 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/502(f) (2004) because it violated public policy, in that it penalized the wife upon seeking a change that might have been in the children's best interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

1088 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Bigelow Group v. Rickert


No. 2-06-0879


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


377 Ill. App. 3d 165; 877 N.E.2d 1171; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1144; 315 Ill. Dec. 842



October 24, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Bigelow Group, Inc. v. Rickert, 226 Ill. 2d 611, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 217 (Ill., Jan. 30, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 04--MR--488. Honorable Michael J. Colwell, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a developer and homeowners, sued defendant tax collector in the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) for an injunction against the collector's refusal to allow property tax payment by specification and a declaration that this refusal violated 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/1-1 et seq. (2004), and U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. Plaintiffs sought to recover interest and penalty damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs said the tax collector had no policy on paying property taxes by specification. The appellate court held he had a policy because he did not allow it. His policy was not illegal because 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/20-210 (2004) said a collector "may" accept payment of property taxes by specification. His policy of refusing to accept payment by specification was not arbitrary and capricious or an abuse of discretion because he had the discretion to accept or decline payment by specification as long as he did not violate the law. It was not alleged that he violated the law, and without such a claim, and proof thereof, a challenge to his exercise of discretion failed. Any purported fact question as to the viability of his reasons was irrelevant. Given such limits on judicial inquiry into executive discretion, the rational-basis test associated with substantive due process review of a legislative action did not apply, and plaintiffs' substantive due process argument failed because they claimed no fundamental right to pay taxes by specification. The equal protection argument failed because the collector treated all taxpayers similarly by not allowing payment by specification.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

In re Marriage of Duggan


No. 2-06-0061


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


376 Ill. App. 3d 725; 877 N.E.2d 1140; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1131; 315 Ill. Dec. 811



October 16, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Carroll County. No. 01-D-67. Honorable Val Gunnarsson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Carroll County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted in part and denied in part appellant husband's motion to vacate a ruling on appellee wife's petition to increase child support that set a termination date for child support and did not state a specific dollar amount; the judgment corrected the termination date but did not set a dollar amount. The husband appealed while his petition to set specific times for visitation remained pending.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dissolved the husband and wife's marriage. The dissolution judgment directed him to pay child support. The wife later petitioned to increase the child support. An agreed order stated, inter alia, that the husband would pay a certain percent of income. He timely filed a motion to vacate alleging that a specific dollar amount should have been stated. He also filed a petition to establish specific visitation times. The trial court, ruling on the motion to vacate, refused to set a specific dollar amount. It did not make an Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 304(a) appealability finding. He filed a notice of appeal. The appellate court found that it had jurisdiction because Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 303(a) provided that a prematurely filed notice of appeal did not become effective until the judgment regarding the separate claim, the petition to establish specific visitation times, was entered. It also found that since that rule was procedural, it could be applied retroactively to allow for the husband's appeal. On the merits, the appellate court found that the husband had a right under 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/505(a)(5) (2004) to have the support judgment state the dollar amount to be paid.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Adames v. Sheahan


No. 1-05-3911


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1084



October 11, 2007, Decided 
October 11, 2007, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Adames v. Sheahan, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1409 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Nov. 21, 2007)
Modified and rehearing denied by, Remanded by Adames v. Sheahan, 880 N.E.2d 559, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1263 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Nov. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 L 05894. Honorable Carol Pearce McCarthy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) on plaintiff representatives' wrongful death claims against defendants, a sheriff and a gun manufacturer, granted the sheriff's summary judgment motion upon finding no duty existed to protect a shooting victim from a third party act and granted the gun manufacturer's summary judgment motion on its "not unreasonably dangerous," no duty to warn, and intervening cause defenses. The representatives appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father was a policeman. His son, who was 13-years-old, found the father's service weapon at home. The son pointed it at a friend and pulled the trigger. The gun fired, and a bullet in the gun's chamber struck the friend and fatally wounded him. The representatives sued, inter alia, the sheriff and the gun manufacturer. The claims against the sheriff were based on negligence under a respondeat superior theory that the sheriff was liable for the father's negligence in storing the gun so that nobody else could access it. The claims against the gun manufacturer were based on a products liability theory. The sheriff responded by stating that he did not have a duty to protect the shooting victim. The gun manufacturer primarily claimed that the son's conduct was an intervening cause of the death and that it was thus not liable. After the trial court ruled for the sheriff and gun manufacturer on summary judgment motions, the appellate court found that the sheriff could be liable for the father's negligence if that negligence occurred in the scope of the father's employment and that it was up to the jury to determine whether the son's conduct was criminal and foreseeable.


OUTCOME: The trial court's summary judgment grant in favor of the sheriff, based on the "no duty to protect" finding, was reversed. Its summary judgment grant in favor of the gun manufacturer on the "not unreasonably dangerous" defense was affirmed, but its summary judgment grant for the gun manufacturer on the no duty to warn and intervening cause defenses was reversed.

Ellison v. Ill. Racing Bd.


No. 1-05-3835


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


377 Ill. App. 3d 433; 878 N.E.2d 740; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1083; 316 Ill. Dec. 18



October 11, 2007, Decided 
October 11, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 7, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 99 CH 18598. Honorable Anthony Young, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Illinois Racing Board suspended and excluded appellant horse trainer from all racetracks under the supervision of the Board and revoked his licenses. The trainer filed an action against the Board and appellee officials and stewards in administrative review under the Illinois Administrative Review Law, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-101 et seq. (2004). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) affirmed the ruling. The trainer appealed.


OVERVIEW: Investigators at a racetrack found that the trainer possessed and attempted to hide contraband consisting of needles, syringes, injectables, and prescription items. When the investigators confronted the trainer, he fled through a barn, ignored calls to stop, discarded items, told inconsistent stories, and attempted to cover up the issue. The Board found that the trainer violated Ill. Admin. Code tit. 11, §§ 603.50, 603.80, and 603.90 (1998) and 230 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9(e) (2004) of the Illinois Horse Racing Act of 1975. On appeal, the court found that the trainer's contraband violations, combined with his behavior toward the investigators, supported the Board's finding that he violated § 9(e) as his actions undermined public confidence and the reputation of horse racing. Moreover, the Board was authorized to determine a proper punishment and its actions in imposing an exclusion and suspension were not arbitrary, unreasonable, or contrary to its goal of protecting the honesty and integrity of horse racing. Finally, the trainer's due process rights were not violated as the Board provided sufficient notice of the charges against him and § 9(e) was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Appeal denied by, Vacated by Crull v. Sriratana, 229 Ill. 2d 619, 903 N.E.2d 726, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 938, 328 Ill. Dec. 66 (2008)

State ex rel. Beeler, Schad & Diamond, P.C. v. Ritz Camera Ctrs., Inc.


No. 1-05-1059


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


377 Ill. App. 3d 990; 878 N.E.2d 1152; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1075; 316 Ill. Dec. 128



October 5, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 10, 2007. Released for Publication December 7, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 02 L 869, 02 L 1435, 02 L 4462, 02 L 4464, 02 L 4466, 02 L 5023, 02 L 5025, 02 L 5824, 02 L 5827, 02 L 6312, 02 L 6702, 02 L 7528, 02 L 7529, 02 L 7530, 02 L 8234, 02 L 8235, 02 L 10462, 02 L 10913, 02 L 12900, 03 L 185, 03 L 1163, 03 L 2506, 03 L 2931, 03 L 3071. Honorable Ronald F. Bartkowicz, Judge Presiding.
State ex rel. Beeler Schad & Diamond, P.C. v. Ritz Camera Ctrs., 216 Ill. 2d 735, 834 N.E.2d 912, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1532, 296 Ill. Dec. 107 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator law firm, acting on behalf of the State of Illinois, filed a complaint alleging that defendant retailers had violated the Illinois Whistleblower Reward and Protection Act, 740 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 175/1 et seq. (2002) as to use tax. The Attorney General intervened. On an interlocutory appeal from the denial of defendants' joint motion to dismiss, the Illinois Supreme Court directed the present court to answer six certified questions.


OVERVIEW: The court held that a remote retailer could not make a knowingly false record or statement to create liability under the Act if it disclosed that no use tax was due or collected based on its reasonable interpretation of the law. Next, the Act required the existence of an actual record or statement. Documents memorializing a purchase that disclosed that no use tax was being collected could not be considered false so as to create liability under the Act. Under the Act, a false record or statement did not have to be submitted to or directly relied upon by the State. Claims brought under the Act did not deprive defendants of rights and privileges so that the Act could not be used to enforce the collection of taxes, as litigants were afforded all the protections provided in civil proceedings. The Illinois Department of Revenue was not the sole entity authorized to assess and collect use tax when fraudulent records and statements were created. The Act applied to alleged tax liabilities under the Use Tax Act when fraudulent records and statements existed. Finally, the Act did not violate Ill. Const. art. V, §§ 15 and 21, relating to the attorney general and to executive compensation.


OUTCOME: The court answered the six certified questions, and the cause was remanded.

 

1094 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Thompkins


No. 1-05-0563


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


376 Ill. App. 3d 629; 876 N.E.2d 1088; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1049; 315 Ill. Dec. 498



September 28, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 9, 2007.
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Thompkins v. Pfister, 2012 U.S. App. LEXIS 22005 (7th Cir. Ill., Oct. 23, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John A. Wasilewski, Judge Presiding.
People v. Thompkins, 2000 Ill. LEXIS 938 (Ill., June 15, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of a double homicide. After his and other offenders' death sentences were commuted by the Governor of Illinois, the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, resentenced defendant to two concurrent natural life sentences. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the commutation order which removed his death sentence also removed the requirement of a mandatory natural life sentence under § 5-8-1(a)(1)(c) of the Illinois Unified Code of Corrections. The appellate court disagreed. While the Governor had the authority to commute defendant's sentence to an undetermined term, he chose not to do so, but instead mitigated defendant's sentence to natural life imprisonment, the only other sentence available for a double homicide. The trial court had no discretion and was required by law to impose a life sentence without parole. As the trial court properly considered both statutory and nonstatutory mitigation evidence, defendant's rights under the Due Process Clause and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, were not violated. The trial court's characterization of the instant crimes and defendant's prior conviction as similar was not erroneous, and even if it were, such error was an insignificant element of defendant's sentence and was harmless in the context of defendant's fundamental right to liberty. Defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally disparate with that of his co-defendant, as defendant had a more serious criminal history.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Campuzano v. Peritz


No. 1-06-0119


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


376 Ill. App. 3d 485; 875 N.E.2d 1234; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1050; 314 Ill. Dec. 947

September 28, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 9, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 04 M 1301797. Honorable Moira S. Johnson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that barred defendant alleged tortfeasors, pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 91(b), from rejecting an arbitration award entered in favor of plaintiff claimant. The alleged tortfeasors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant and the alleged tortfeasors were involved in a car accident. The claimant filed a negligence action. The case was assigned to mandatory arbitration. A discovery deadline was set. The claimant filed written discovery requests and notices to take the alleged tortfeasors' depositions. The alleged tortfeasors did not respond to the discovery requests, prompting the claimant to file a motion to compel. The trial court then had to order them to appear for depositions and to answer the claimant's interrogatories, all by a certain date. The trial court wrote that failure to comply with discovery would result in an order barring the alleged tortfeasors from testifying or presenting evidence at the arbitration and at trial. An arbitration hearing was held. The alleged tortfeasors admitted negligence. An award was entered for the claimant and against the one alleged tortfeasor who had been driving. The trial court granted the claimant's motion to bar rejection of the arbitration award, pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 91(b). On appeal, the appellate court found that imposition of such a sanction was proper and that Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 91(b) was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1096 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Melchor


No. 1-03-3036


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


376 Ill. App. 3d 444; 875 N.E.2d 1261; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1051; 314 Ill. Dec. 974



September 28, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 9, 2007.
Rehearing denied by People v. Melcher, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 5758 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Oct. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 90 CR 12896. Honorable Fred G. Suria, Judge Presiding.
People v. Melchor, 226 Ill. 2d 24, 871 N.E.2d 32, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 861, 312 Ill. Dec. 632 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder. The intermediate appellate court reversed on grounds that his right to confrontation was violated by admission of the former testimony of the sole eyewitness to the crime. The Illinois Supreme Court vacated that judgment and ordered the intermediate appellate court to determine whether the testimony was admissible under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-10.4, and if not, whether the error was harmless.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a codefendant were arrested for murder; defendant fled and was a fugitive for 10 years. A witness testified at the codefendant's trial and named defendant as the shooter, but he died before defendant's trial. The codefendant had been acquitted and was unavailable to testify. The trial court admitted a transcript of the dead witness' testimony under § 5/115-10.4; the instant court reversed on Confrontation Clause grounds. On remand, the instant court held that the witness' testimony was more probative as to the shooter's identity than any other evidence that could reasonably be procured. However, his testimony was untrustworthy because of (1) his felony convictions; (2) the lack of thorough cross-examination of his testimony, the only link between defendant and the crime; (3) his use of alcohol at the time of the crime; and (4) his possible hopes of making a deal on his pending robbery charge. As defendant's fleeing and failing to appear at trial was not aimed at intentionally procuring the witness's absence at a future trial, the doctrine of forfeiture of wrongdoing did not apply. As the error was very likely to have contributed to the conviction, it was not harmless.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed, his sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

United City of Yorkville v. Vill. of Sugar Grove


No. 2-06-0649


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


376 Ill. App. 3d 9; 875 N.E.2d 1183; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1031; 314 Ill. Dec. 896



September 24, 2007, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 05--MR--447. Honorable Michael J. Colwell, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted summary judgment to defendant village on plaintiff united city's declaratory judgment claim, under 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-12-9 (2006), that a later independent jurisdictional boundary line agreement invalidated an earlier one. It also dismissed the united city's claims for rescission and reformation of the earlier agreement and dismissed plaintiff bank as a party. The united city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The village negotiated two independent jurisdictional boundary line agreements, one with the united city and one with another village. The boundary line agreement with the united city was entered into first, making the older agreement; the boundary line agreement with the other village was entered into nearly 11 months thereafter, making it the newer agreement. The differences in the agreements caused some conflicts, which were discovered when the bank and another property owner attempted to develop a parcel that straddled the united city and the village. The united city and the bank sought a declaratory judgment action that creation of the later agreement invalidated the earlier agreement; it also sought relief for reformation or rescission earlier agreement. The trial court granted summary judgment to the village, dismissed the claims for reformation and rescission of the earlier agreement, and dismissed the bank from the action. On appeal, the appellate court found that statutory law that would invalidate the conflicting agreements applied prospectively only and that law was enacted after the agreements were entered into, and the dismissals were proper.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Brown


NO. 4-06-0694


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


375 Ill. App. 3d 1116; 874 N.E.2d 607; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1055; 314 Ill. Dec. 511



September 24, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Brown, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 5741 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., Oct. 16, 2007)
Appeal denied by People v. Brown, 226 Ill. 2d 619, 882 N.E.2d 79, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 95, 317 Ill. Dec. 505 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 06CF18. Honorably Scott Drazewski, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The McLean County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of unlawful possession of a methamphetamine precursor with the intent to manufacture methamphetamine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Following a bench trial, the trial court convicted defendant of unlawful possession of a methamphetamine precursor, pseudoephedrine, with the intent to manufacture methamphetamine, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 646/20(a)(1) (2005). The trial court later sentenced him to an extended term of eight years in prison. Defendant appealed, and argued only that the statute under which he was sentenced violated the proportionate-penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. The appellate court disagreed. It found that defendant was arguing that the state constitution was violated because the same punishment was imposed for possessing a precursor and violation of another statute imposing punishment for possession of actual methamphetamine, which would be shocking to the moral sense of the community. The appellate court found that in making that argument, defendant was relying on a cross-comparison analysis that the state supreme court had abolished and, instead, should have been comparing whether the sentence was wholly disproportionate to the offense committed, which was the proper test.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Martin v. Dep't of Empl. Sec.


NO. 5-06-0478


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


376 Ill. App. 3d 853; 877 N.E.2d 1119; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1015; 315 Ill. Dec. 790; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P8512



September 17, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Motion to publish granted, September 17, 2007.
Appeal denied by Martin v. Ill. Dep't of Empl. Sec., 226 Ill. 2d 616, 882 N.E.2d 78, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 26, 317 Ill. Dec. 504 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Martin v. Il Dep't of Empl. Sec., 2008 U.S. LEXIS 4690 (U.S., June 2, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Effingham County. No. 06-MR-8. Honorable James J. Eder, Judge, presiding.
Summary Rule 23 order filed August 8, 2007.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a decision of defendant board which denied unemployment insurance benefits to the employee. The Circuit Court of Effingham County (Illinois) affirmed the board's decision. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: A claims adjudicator found the employee ineligible because she was receiving disqualifying income, in the form of a portion of her social security retirement benefits, that exceeded her potential unemployment benefit. A hearing referee affirmed this decision and the hearing referee was in turn affirmed by the board. Because the employee neither raised nor briefed the issue of constitutionality, the appellate court found that she waived that argument on appeal. The employee argued that the chargeable employer was not her base-period employer because the chargeable employer did not contribute to the retirement benefits she was receiving, which were based on employment with other employers before her earlier retirement from the work force and because her retirement benefits did not change when she began employment with chargeable employer. The "base-period employer" was the employer who paid wages to the claimant during the eligibility period. The chargeable employer was the employer who paid wages to the employee during the time period immediately before her unemployment claim. Thus, the board properly found that the chargeable employer was the base-period employer.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that found defendant guilty of two counts of unlawful use of recorded sounds or images in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction on count three, unlawful use of unidentified sound or audio visual recordings. Ann. 5/22-105 did not violate any constitutional due process or equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Bailey


No. 2-05-1260


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


375 Ill. App. 3d 1055; 874 N.E.2d 940; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1008; 314 Ill. Dec. 575



September 6, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 19, 2007.
Appeal granted by People v. Bailey, 226 Ill. 2d 589, 879 N.E.2d 933, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1783, 316 Ill. Dec. 545 (2007)
Affirmed by People v. Bailey, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 183 (Ill., Feb. 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 05--CF--2094. Honorable J. Edward Prochaska, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Winnebago County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in connection with an incident in which police, who arrested him after learning during a vehicle stop that he had an outstanding arrest warrant, searched the car in which he had been riding and discovered a substance alleged to have contained cocaine. He requested that defense counsel not file motions to suppress statements he made to police since he did not want to cause delay to his speedy trial demand. As a result, defense counsel also did not file a motion to quash the arrest and to suppress evidence. Defendant was tried before a jury and was convicted. On appeal, the appellate court found that a statute which prohibited a police officer from inspecting a motor vehicle solely because of a seatbelt violation, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-603.1(f) (2004), did not prohibit a police officer from making an expeditious warrant check and arresting defendant once it was learned that he had an outstanding arrest warrant. As a result, the appellate court found that had defense counsel filed a motion to quash the arrest and to suppress evidence, it would have been denied, which defendant did not have a viable ineffective assistance of counsel claim.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1103 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Gore v. Ind. Ins. Co.


No. 1-06-3325


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


376 Ill. App. 3d 282; 876 N.E.2d 156; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 978; 315 Ill. Dec. 156



September 5, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 9, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from and the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 05 CH 3204. Honorable Martin S. Agran, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured sued defendants foreign insurers in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for alleged violations of the duty of good faith and fair dealing and for a declaratory judgment requiring the insurers to refund part of the premiums the insured paid. The trial court dismissed the insured's complaint, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: A tax on the insurers' premium income was held unconstitutional. The insured said they breached the implied covenant of good faith and fair dealing by including the tax in his premiums. The appellate court held this claim failed because (1) the duty of good faith and fair dealing limited a party's discretion in performing contractual obligations and, when the insured paid a premium, the insurers had no discretion to decide whether to insure him, (2) any decisions the insurers made to include the tax in premiums was made before a duty of good faith and fair dealing arose under subsequent contracts with the insured, and (3) including the tax in premiums was not bad faith because the insurers could increase premiums to recover the tax. The insured did not show an insurer collected the tax after it was found unconstitutional. He had no standing to seek to a declaratory judgment because, if the insurers violated the unearned premium statute, 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/379.1 (2004), this did not give him a private right of action, nor was any violation redressed by refunding premiums, so he had no "legal tangible interest," nor did he show the insurers' contracts violated public policy.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1104 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lee


No. 1-04-2258


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


376 Ill. App. 3d 951; 876 N.E.2d 671; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 963; 315 Ill. Dec. 359



August 30, 2007, Decided 
August 30, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 9, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Kenneth J. Wadas, Judge Presiding.
People v. Lee, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 339 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Apr. 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of armed robbery under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-1 (2000) and 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-2(a)(2) (2000), and three counts of aggravated unlawful restraint under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/10-3.1 (2000). He was sentenced to concurrent prison terms of 19 years for armed robbery and 10 years for each conviction of aggravated unlawful restraint. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: While a husband, his wife, and their child were crossing a street, defendant walked up behind them and demanded the husband's money. The wife testified that (1) she saw that defendant had a gun; and (2) he said he would shoot them. Defendant fled after the husband gave his money to him. On appeal, the court found that the direct and circumstantial evidence was sufficient to show that defendant committed robbery with a gun. While defendant's conviction for aggravated unlawful restraint as to the husband violated the one-act, one-crime doctrine, his convictions for aggravated unlawful restraint as to the wife and child were proper because there were multiple victims of defendant's conduct. Moreover, under the totality of the circumstances, the child was restrained even though he ran back across the street when defendant approached his family. Finally, the trial judge had no authority under the case law at the time to apply enhancement provisions to defendant's sentence for armed robbery. The decision which overturned the case law was issued while the case was pending on direct review. Therefore, the proper remedy was to remand for resentencing as permitted at the time.


OUTCOME: The armed robbery and aggravated unlawful restraint of the wife and child convictions were affirmed, the aggravated unlawful restraint of the husband conviction was vacated, and the concurrent sentences for the aggravated unlawful restraint convictions were affirmed. The armed robbery sentence was vacated, and the matter was remanded to the trial court to impose a sentence within the range for armed robbery as it existed prior to its amendment.

People v. Bobo


No. 1-05-2510


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


375 Ill. App. 3d 966; 874 N.E.2d 297; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 943; 314 Ill. Dec. 387



August 24, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 3, 2007.
Rehearing denied by People v. Bobo, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1182 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 24, 2007)
Appeal denied by Ill. v. Bobo, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1830 (Ill., Nov. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Garritt Howard, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of aggravated kidnapping and aggravated criminal sexual abuse. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to consecutive 20- and five-year terms in the Illinois Department of Corrections. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was not deprived of a fair trial by the admission of 30 photographs of women's feet, the State's use of defendant's statements, or the use of a prior statement by defendant that was not disclosed in discovery. The photographs were relevant to defendant's identity and intent to sexually gratify himself. Defendant's statements were not used until the defense strategy was found to be based on the issue of identity. And, the late disclosed statement was not known to the prosecutor until the morning of trial and a continuance was offered to defense counsel, who refused it. Next, the appellate court concluded that trial counsel's strategic decision to challenge the prosecution's case by attacking the evidence as to great bodily harm, while unsuccessful, subjected the State's case to meaningful adversarial testing. Defendant's Batson claim failed because the record did not reflect purposeful racial discrimination and the two excluded venirepersons shared more than racial characteristics in that they both had a history of involvement with the legal process. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the 20-year sentence was not disproportionate to the nature of offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Cummings


No. 1-05-2058


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


375 Ill. App. 3d 513; 873 N.E.2d 996; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 849; 314 Ill. Dec. 66



August 6, 2007, Decided 
August 6, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 18, 2007.
Appeal denied by People v. Cummings, 226 Ill. 2d 592, 879 N.E.2d 934, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1818, 316 Ill. Dec. 546 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 00 CR 26997-03. Honorable Joseph G. Kazmierski, Jr., Judge Presiding.
People v. Cummings, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 677 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., June 25, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's armed robbery conviction and sentence of life imprisonment as an habitual offender was affirmed, he petitioned the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. (2004). The trial court summarily dismissed the petition and denied his motion for reconsideration. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said his sentence was disproportionate because armed violence predicated on robbery with a category III weapon was identical to armed robbery but had a lesser sentence. The appellate court held his claim could not be considered because his post-conviction petition did not raise it. Res judicata barred the grounds on which he said his sentence was disproportionate because they were decided on direct appeal. The fundamental fairness exception to this rule did not apply because no decision since the affirmance of his conviction and sentence recognized the validity of his argument or said his direct appeal was wrongly decided, nor did the appellate court concede that its decision in his appeal was wrong. The life sentence was constitutionally proportionate when considered in the context of his violent offender history. The life sentence was not disproportionate under the identical elements test because it was based on three violent felony convictions and was not imposed solely for the armed robbery conviction. Once defendant was convicted of his third violent felony, the trial court had to find him an habitual criminal and give him a mandatory life sentence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Smart Growth Sugar Grove, LLC v. Vill. of Sugar Grove


No. 2-06-0656


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


375 Ill. App. 3d 780; 873 N.E.2d 20; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 855; 313 Ill. Dec. 725

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois) dismissed plaintiff limited liability company's six-count complaint against defendant village that had challenged the village's refusal to rezone the limited liability company's property, which the village had annexed, and a provision in the village's comprehensive plan recommending that the village acquire a right-of-way across the limited liability company's property. The village appealed.


OVERVIEW: The limited liability company filed a six-count complaint against the village challenging: (1) the village's refusal to rezone the limited liability company's property, which the village had annexed under an agreement with limited liability company's predecessor, and (2) a provision in the village's comprehensive plan recommending that the village acquire a right-of-way across limited liability company's property for a possible highway interchange.
