People v. Butler


No. 1-05-3288


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


375 Ill. App. 3d 269; 873 N.E.2d 480; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 836; 313 Ill. Dec. 856



August 1, 2007, Decided 
August 1, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 18, 2007.
Appeal denied by People v. Butler, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1764 (Ill., Nov. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 04 CR 25402. The Honorable Bertina E. Lampkin, Judge Presiding.
People v. Butler, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 637 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., June 13, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of harassment of a witness under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/32-4a(a) (2004) and sentenced him, as a Class X offender, to eight years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed, contending that the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague on its face and that the State failed to prove him guilty of witness harassment beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: The day after defendant was arrested on a business owner's complaint of attempted misdemeanor theft, defendant yelled at the owner and another witness from about 25 feet away, calling the owner by name and threatening to kill both men. The appellate court affirmed. Section 32-4a(a) did not overbroadly sweep protected speech within its purview. Although communication was an element of the statute, that did not draw otherwise validly proscribed activities within First Amendment protection. The punishable behavior was narrowed by the elements of the statute, which required a specific intent to harass. Defendant's vagueness argument failed, in part due to the failure of the overbreadth argument. Additionally, defendant could not demonstrate that the statute failed to provide citizens with adequate notice or led to arbitrary enforcement. The punishable conduct was limited to a specific group of people and was further limited by the specific intent to harass so as to, inter alia, convey a threat. Finally, defendant's actions presented the exact type of conduct § 32-4a(a) was meant to proscribe, and the State's evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1109 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Keys


NO. 4-06-0378


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


375 Ill. App. 3d 459; 874 N.E.2d 577; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 840; 314 Ill. Dec. 481



July 31, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County. No. 05CF219. Honorable Harold J. Frobish, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress, defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of a controlled substance (heroin) under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/402(c) (2004), and obstructing a peace officer under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/31-1(a) (2004). The Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to a six-year prison term on the unlawful possession count. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another were stopped by police. An officer told defendant to raise his hands and interlace his fingers, which defendant did. While the officer was attempting to pat-down defendant, defendant broke free and ran. During the officer's chase of defendant, the officer lost sight of defendant for a few seconds. After defendant was apprehended, the officer found three bags of heroin in the area where he lost sight of defendant. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the evidence recovered as the result of defendant's unconstitutional temporary seizure and pat-down search. The State argued that the temporary seizure and pat-down search were constitutionally valid; and, even if defendant's initial seizure was unconstitutional, defendant's actions of running from the police and abandoning the illegal drugs made them admissible. The appellate court concluded that the drugs were admissible as evidence even assuming arguendo the initial seizure of defendant was unlawful, because the seizure ended when defendant fled and the abandoned drugs were not obtained in violation of the Fourth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1110 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Price


No. 1-05-3782


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


375 Ill. App. 3d 684; 873 N.E.2d 453; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 821; 313 Ill. Dec. 829



July 27, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 18, 2007
Appeal denied by People v. Price, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1737 (Ill., Nov. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Thomas M. Davy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for aggravated unlawful use of a weapon. He was sentenced to 30 months' probation and assessed $ 729 in fines, fees, and costs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction on the basis that his status as an overnight guest at a residence put him outside the scope of the aggravated-unlawful-use-of-a-weapon statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6(a)(1), (a)(3)(A) (2002). He contended that the statute permitted a person who was in his or her "overnight living quarters" to lawfully possess a weapon. The appeals court found he was not outside the scope of the statute. By his own admission, he was never anything more than a guest at the residence, and did not claim to live there. The sentence was not erroneous as a matter of law; to the contrary, it was within the statutory guidelines. Defendant failed to file a motion to reconsider his sentence and, therefore, forfeited his right to challenge his sentence under a theory of abuse of discretion. Both a Vehicle Code fee (55 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-1101(a) (2004)) and a court systems fine (730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-9-1.10 (2004)) were improperly assessed. Defendant did not commit any offense enumerated in the Vehicle Code, and the aggravated-unlawful-use-of-a-weapon offense was not one of the offenses enumerated in the statute authorizing the court systems fine.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed. The imposition of the $ 10 mental health court charge and the $ 5 youth diversion/peer court charge were affirmed. The $ 100 Vehicle Code fee and the $ 5 court systems fine were vacated. Defendant also was entitled to a $ 10 credit for his time spent in custody against all fines imposed.

 

1111 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Smolley


No. 3-05-0793


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


375 Ill. App. 3d 167; 873 N.E.2d 8; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 816; 313 Ill. Dec. 713


February 6, 2007, Assigned; March 22, 2007, Submitted 
July 24, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 24, 2007.
Appeal denied by People v. Smolley, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1716 (Ill., Nov. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 04-CF-613. Honorable Scott Shore, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois) of two counts of felony murder (720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(a)(3) (2004)). He was also found guilty of unlawful possession of a firearm. Pursuant to § 5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii) of the Unified Code of Corrections (730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii) (2004)), he received a mandatory sentence of natural life in prison. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed § 5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii) was unconstitutional as applied to him. Specifically, he argued the sentence mandated by the Code violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970). The appeals court found that the natural life sentence imposed on defendant was neither cruel, degrading, nor so wholly disproportionate to the offense he committed as to shock the moral sense of the community. Therefore, we find that § 5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii) (730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii) (2004)) was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant. Prior to killing a woman and her daughter he committed multiple burglaries. While released and on juvenile probation after the first burglary, defendant committed the offenses of theft and criminal trespass to a building. After his probation for those offenses terminated, he committed his second burglary. Again, while released on juvenile probation, defendant violated that probation by committing a criminal trespass to a residence. Following a period of confinement and home electronic monitoring, defendant was again found in violation of his probation.


OUTCOME: the judgment of the circuit court of Peoria County is affirmed.

People v. Robinson


No. 1-04-2437


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


374 Ill. App. 3d 949; 872 N.E.2d 73; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 733; 313 Ill. Dec. 313



June 29, 2007, Decided 
June 29, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 9, 2007.
Rehearing denied by People v. Robinson, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 938 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 26, 2007)
Appeal granted by People v. Robinson, 226 Ill. 2d 602, 879 N.E.2d 937, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1788, 316 Ill. Dec. 549 (2007)
Affirmed by People v. Robinson, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1819 (Ill., Nov. 20, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 12422. The Honorable Preston L. Bowie, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with first degree murder and unlawful use of a weapon. Defendant was found guilty of involuntary manslaughter and unlawful use of a weapon, and was sentenced to 12 years for involuntary manslaughter and a concurrent 5 years for the weapon charge. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied defendant's motions to reconsider sentence and for a new trial, and his motion in arrest of judgment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's principal argument was that he was wrongly convicted of the uncharged offense of involuntary manslaughter of a household member because that offense was a separate and distinct offense from "simple" involuntary manslaughter, requiring proof of an "element" that the offense of first degree murder did not, that the victim was a household member. The appellate court disagreed, concluding that the victim's status as a household member was not an "element" of involuntary manslaughter. While 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3(f) (2000), required proof that the victim was a household member, that factor did not create a distinct offense, but rather enhanced the range of penalties for the offense. The appellate court further concluded that, inter alia, the charging instrument was not deficient, as it clearly identified the offense charged with sufficient specificity to allow defendant to prepare a defense and bar future prosecution arising out of the same conduct. Finally, the appellate court concluded that defendant's constitutional challenges to both 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3(f) (2000), and the compulsory extraction of his blood and storage of his DNA failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Duff


No. 1-05-2110


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


374 Ill. App. 3d 599; 872 N.E.2d 46; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 682; 313 Ill. Dec. 286



June 26, 2007, Decided 
June 26, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 9, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Nicholas Ford, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, and modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. The trial court found defendant to be Class X-eligible and sentenced him to six years' imprisonment. The trial court also assessed an Illinois Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund fine and a controlled substance assessment fine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer testified that he saw different people approach defendant. After each person handed money to defendant, defendant turned and signaled the accomplice. The accomplice then walked to a flower pot, picked up a brown vial, removed an object, and handed the object to the person who had approached defendant. Police officers recovered the brown vial, which contained plastic packets of cocaine. On appeal, the court found that (1) while the admission of the testimony of a witness regarding the accomplice's guilty plea violated the Confrontation Clause of the Sixth Amendment, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because, even without the testimony, the police officer's testimony was more than sufficient to support the conviction; (2) the trial court did not err by failing to allow defense counsel to elicit the reason for the accomplice's guilty plea during the redirect examination of the witness; (3) the trial court improperly assessed an Illinois Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund fine under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 240/10(c)(2) (2004) as other fines were imposed; and (4) defendant was entitled to credits under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/110-14(a) (2004).


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed in part as to the conviction, the judgment was vacated in part as to the Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund fine, and the judgment was modified in part as to the fees and costs order to reflect a credit towards defendant's drug assessment fine.

 

1115 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bailey


No. 1-05-2913


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


374 Ill. App. 3d 608; 872 N.E.2d 420; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 681; 313 Ill. Dec. 437



June 26, 2007, Decided 
June 26, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 9, 2007.
Appeal denied by People v. Bailey, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1710 (Ill., Nov. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable William G. Lacy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/401 (2002). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed an unknown person on a corner yelling the word "rocks" at passing cars and directing cars to an alley where defendant was standing. The officer observed defendant hand white items to car occupants who gave defendant money. Defendant ran from the police, threw a ziplock bag containing .1 gram of crack cocaine, and was found with $ 63 in his sock. On cross-examination, defense counsel asked the officer if he ever saw defendant speak with the unknown person on the corner. The officer said he saw the unknown person speak to defendant and accept money from defendant. Defense counsel continued questioning the officer about the interaction between defendant and the unknown person. The appellate court determined that there was sufficient evidence that defendant had an intent to deliver the drugs found in the ziplock bag. However, counsel was ineffective because counsel elicited damaging testimony not presented as part of the State's case. The evidence prejudiced defendant because (1) the testimony connected him to the man on the corner, (2) it explained why no money was found in his pockets, and (3) the trial court clearly relied on the evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded for a new trial.

 

1116 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Napleton v. Vill. of Hinsdale


No. 2-06-0390


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


374 Ill. App. 3d 1098; 872 N.E.2d 23; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 739; 313 Ill. Dec. 263



June 26, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 10, 2007.
Appeal granted by Napleton v. Vill. of Hinsdale, 226 Ill. 2d 588, 879 N.E.2d 932, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1777, 316 Ill. Dec. 544 (2007)
Affirmed by Napleton v. Vill. of Hinsdale, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 377 (Ill., June 5, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 05--CH--1058. Honorable Kenneth L. Popejoy, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trustee appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) dismissing with prejudice under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2--615 (2004) her first amended verified complaint, which challenged the facial validity of amendments to defendant city's zoning code that changed the permitted uses of a trust property.


OVERVIEW: After thorough study, the city amended its zoning code to increase tax revenues in certain business districts. The trustee alleged that amendments precluded the ground floor of the trust property from ever being sold or leased to a financial institution and raised a facial challenge to the amended code's validity, which the trial court dismissed for failure to state a cognizable claim. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly applied rational basis scrutiny, rather than intermediate scrutiny, in granting the dismissal. The proper level of scrutiny was determined, not by whether the trustee's challenge was facial or as-applied, but by the nature of the right at issue. Rational basis scrutiny was properly applied to challenges to legislative enactments to which extreme deference was owed, including zoning enactments such as the zoning code at issue that did not involve fundamental rights. The court refused to apply the substantial relationship test, i.e., the forerunner of the intermediate scrutiny standard, to the trustee's facial challenge. The city's amending the zoning code in order to promote its fiscal policy was a rationally based decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1117 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


O'Casek v. Childrens Home & Aid Soc'y


NO. 4-06-0344


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


374 Ill. App. 3d 507; 874 N.E.2d 150; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 687; 314 Ill. Dec. 240



June 25, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by O'Casek v. Children's Home & Aid Soc'y, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 5744 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., July 26, 2007)
Affirmed by O'Casek v. Children's Home & Aid Soc'y, 229 Ill. 2d 421, 892 N.E.2d 994, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 628, 323 Ill. Dec. 2 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 04L160. Honorable James E. Souk, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff special administratrix of a decedent's estate appealed after the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) dismissed with prejudice a medical malpractice action against defendants, a children's aid society, a hospital, and two doctors, based on plaintiff's failure to comply with the 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-622(a)(1) (2004) and denied plaintiff's motion for reconsideration. A previous complaint had been voluntarily dismissed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff had requested a 90-day extension of time to file her § 2-622 doctor's report when the case was refiled. At issue was whether a prohibition in the "civil reform" version of § 2-622 against such extensions of time where a case had previously been voluntarily dismissed applied to bar plaintiff's case. The appellate court, reexamining its Cargill decision, reversed. The language had been ruled unconstitutional in Best in 1997. However, the language remained in the statute when the legislature amended another portion of the statute in 1998. In Cargill, the court ruled that the amendment "resurrected" the unconstitutional language. Post-Cargill, however, the legislature again amended the statute. According to prefatory language in 2005 Ill. Laws 4964, the offending language disappeared with Best and was never reenacted. The legislature specifically rejected the civil-reform version of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-622 as a source for its 2005 amendments and instead "continued" the pre-1995 version of the statute. Thus, plaintiff's previous voluntary dismissal of the malpractice action had no bearing on her request for an extension of time.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Cummings


No. 1-05-2058


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 677

June 25, 2007, Opinion Filed

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by People v. Cummings, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 850 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 31, 2007)
Substituted opinion at People v. Cummings, 375 Ill. App. 3d 513, 873 N.E.2d 996, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 849, 314 Ill. Dec. 66 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 00 CR 26997-03. Honorable Joseph G. Kazmierski, Jr., Judge Presiding.
People v. Cummings, 351 Ill. App. 3d 343, 813 N.E.2d 1004, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 956, 286 Ill. Dec. 311 (Ill. App. Ct., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that summarily dismissed defendant's petition for post-conviction relief after defendant was sentenced to natural life imprisonment because he had been found guilty of armed robbery and he was eligible for sentencing as a habitual offender under the state's habitual offender law. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been previously convicted of murder in 1967 and armed robbery in 1984. Thereafter, he was charged with armed robbery in a case where he was accused of robbing a sandwich shop while armed with a baseball bat. Following a jury trial, he was found guilty of armed robbery. At sentencing, the trial court sentenced him to natural life imprisonment pursuant to Habitual Criminal Act, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33B-1 (2000). He appealed, and his conviction and sentence were affirmed. Defendant then filed a pro se petition for post-conviction relief. The trial court summarily dismissed his petition as frivolous and patently without merit. On appeal, defendant primarily argued that his sentence for armed robbery was unconstitutional because it violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. The appellate court found that his petition suffered from a number of procedural defects, but added that his biggest problem was that he was not sentenced for the armed robbery conviction, which he compared to another statute to make his argument, but, instead, was sentenced under the habitual offender statute.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Morgan v. Dep't of Fin. & Prof'l Regulation


No. 1-06-0266


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


374 Ill. App. 3d 275; 871 N.E.2d 178; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 645; 312 Ill. Dec. 778



June 15, 2007, Decided 
June 15, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 6, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Morgan v. Ill. Dep't Fin. & Prof'l Regulation, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 871 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 23, 2007)
Appeal denied by Morgan v. Ill. Dep't of Fin. & Prof'l Regulation, 226 Ill. 2d 588, 879 N.E.2d 932, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1802, 316 Ill. Dec. 544 (2007)
Related proceeding at Morgan v. Dep't of Fin. & Prof'l Regulation, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 57 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Feb. 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 05 CH 03127. Honorable Anthony Young, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee brought a complaint for administrative review challenging the summary suspension of his license as a clinical psychologist by appellee, the Illinois Department of Financial and Professional Regulation, and the Department's imposition of a suspension and indefinite probation. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) affirmed the Department and denied the licensee's subsequent motion for reconsideration. The licensee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department filed an administrative complaint, alleging that the licensee engaged in inappropriate sexual conduct with a female patient. The Director of the Department, after a telephone conversation with a Department investigator, summarily suspended the licensee's license. After an evidentiary hearing, an administrative law judge (ALJ) found that the licensee violated 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 15(7) (2004), and made recommendations. An administrative board recommended a suspension and probation. The Director adopted the recommendation. On appeal, the court found that (1) the Director did not abuse his discretion under 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 15/15.4 (2004) by denying a rehearing; (2) the ALJ did not make improper evidentiary and credibility determinations; (3) 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 15/21.6 (2002) was not unconstitutionally vague; (4) the summary suspension did not violate the licensee's due process rights; and (5) although the Illinois Clinical Psychologist Licensing Act, 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 15/1 et seq., itself, was not unconstitutional, the Department violated the licensee's right to due process by not promptly reaching a final determination after the hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1120 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Butler


No. 1-05-3288


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 637



June 13, 2007, Decided 
June 13, 2007, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Butler, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1187 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 26, 2007)
Opinion withdrawn by People v. Butler, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 852 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 26, 2007)
Substituted opinion at People v. Butler, 375 Ill. App. 3d 269, 873 N.E.2d 480, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 836, 313 Ill. Dec. 856 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 04 CR 25402. The Honorable Bertina E. Lampkin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of harassment of a witness, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/32-4a(a) (2004), and sentenced him, as a Class X offender, to eight years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the witness harassment statute was unconstitutionally overbroad because it criminalized constitutionally protected speech. The appellate court disagreed, noting that the elements of the statute containing speech were not constitutionally protected because the punishable speech was limited to situations where the specific intent element was satisfied, the communication was directed at a juror because of his or her verdict or a witness because of his or her testimony, and must ensure either mental anguish of emotional distress to convey a treat. Defendant also argued that the statute was vague on its face. The appellate court disagreed, noting the scope of punishable conduct was limited to a specified group, jurors or witnesses, and was further limited by the individual's specified intent to harass or annoy when communicating so as to inflict mental anguish or emotional distress or to convey a threat. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the State proved defendant guilty of witness harassment beyond a reasonable doubt, as the evidence showed defendant approached the victims with the intent to harass them and threaten their lives.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Mikolajczyk v. Ford Motor Co.


No. 1-05-3133


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


374 Ill. App. 3d 646; 870 N.E.2d 885; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 640; 312 Ill. Dec. 441; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P17,770



June 13, 2007, Decided 
June 13, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 6, 2007.
Appeal granted by Mikolajczyk v. Ford Motor Co., 225 Ill. 2d 637, 875 N.E.2d 1113, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1166, 314 Ill. Dec. 826 (2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by Mikolajczyk v. Ford Motor Co., 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1424 (Ill., Oct. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00L3342. The Honorable James P. Flannery, Jr., Judge Presiding.
Mikolajczyk v. Ford Motor Co., 369 Ill. App. 3d 78, 859 N.E.2d 201, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1057, 307 Ill. Dec. 201 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment against appellant car manufacturers after appellee estate representative sued them under a strict products liability theory for the alleged defective design of a car decedent was driving when he was fatally injured. After a jury apportioned damages between the car manufacturers and another defendant, and awarded damages including loss of society damages, the car manufacturers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The estate representative filed a suit alleging strict products liability for the defective design against the car manufacturers, and a negligence action against another defendant, after decedent was killed when the car he was driving was struck by a vehicle being driven by the other defendant. The estate representative contended that the seat that decedent was sitting in, known as a "yielding seat," flattened backwards, which caused decedent to sustain a fatal brain injury. Summary judgment was entered against the other defendant for negligence. The case was then tried to the jury on the strict products liability claim. The jury found the other defendant 60 percent liable and the car manufacturers 40 percent liable for the death of the decedent. The jury then awarded $ 2 million for loss of money, goods, and services and $ 25 million for loss of society. On appeal, the car manufacturers raised a number of issues, and primarily claimed that the jury had been improperly instructed and that the damages were excessive. The appellate court found that the jury could be instructed on the consumer expectations test and that the loss of society damage award was excessive.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed, except to the extent of the trial court's judgment awarding damages for loss of society which was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings including the trial court setting a remittitur of the loss of society award.

People v. Beachem


No. 1-05-0045


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


374 Ill. App. 3d 145; 871 N.E.2d 805; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 621; 313 Ill. Dec. 78



June 8, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 17, 2007.
Appeal granted by People v. Beachem, 225 Ill. 2d 641, 875 N.E.2d 1115, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1171, 314 Ill. Dec. 828 (2007)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable William G. Lacy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to six years in the Illinois state penitentiary and ordered defendant to pay a total $ 3,704 in fines and fees. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his conviction should have been reduced to simple possession of a controlled substance because the State did not prove he had the requisite intent to deliver. The appellate court concluded that, when viewed as a whole in the light most favorable to the State, a rational trier of fact could have concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant intended to deliver the narcotics in his possession. Among other things, defendant possessed 23.9 grams of cocaine and admitted to an officer that he sold drugs to take are of his family. In response to defendant's numerous sentencing issues, the appellate court concluded, inter alia, that defendant was entitled to credit, under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-7(b) (2004), for time spent in full custody prior to trial and between his guilty finding and his sentencing, and for actual time spent at the jail as a participant in the day reporting center program. Defendant was also entitled to credit against the controlled substance assessment for the same time periods, pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/110-14 (2004). Finally, the appellate court upheld the order for DNA extraction and storage as constitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. The order that defendant pay $ 5 to the Spinal Cord Injury Paralysis Cure Research Trust Fund was affirmed. The mittimus was amended to reflect 204 days' credit and to reflect a credit of $ 1,020 to be applied against the $ 3,000 controlled substance assessment. The order to pay a Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund penalty was reversed. The order regarding the extraction and storing of DNA was affirmed.

People v. Luczak

Appeal denied by People v. Luczak, 226 Ill. 2d 625, 882 N.E.2d 81, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 63, 317 Ill. Dec. 507 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Hon. John J. Mannion and The Hon. Marjorie C. Laws, Judges Presiding.

The trial court then denied that motion. On appeal, the appellate court found that res judicata barred defendant's DNA testing request, no prejudice resulted from the summary dismissal of his habeas corpus petition, and defendant's request for free transcripts was not timely filed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments were affirmed.

 

1125 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Alvarez v. Pappas


No. 1-06-0098


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


374 Ill. App. 3d 39; 870 N.E.2d 853; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 583; 312 Ill. Dec. 409



June 4, 2007, Decided 
June 4, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 17, 2007.
Appeal granted by Alvarez v. Pappas, 225 Ill. 2d 627, 875 N.E.2d 1109, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1179, 314 Ill. Dec. 822 (2007)
Affirmed by Alvarez v. Pappas, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 315 (Ill., Apr. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 05 CH 2822. Honorable Julia M. Nowicki, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed a complaint against defendant county treasurer in which they sought a return of duplicate real estate tax payments they had made over five years before the complaint was filed. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed the action as time-barred under 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/20-175 (2004). Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected plaintiffs' argument that their duplicate payments were not "tax payments" but mistaken payments of real estate tax assessments that had already been satisfied. First, plaintiffs had provided no authority for their proposition; thus, this argument was waived under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 341(h)(7). Second, the duplicate payments, even if made by mistake, amounted to "overpayments." A tax was overpaid when a taxpayer paid more than what was owed, for any reason. Thus, the payments were not tangible personal property, and the Illinois Uniform Disposition of Unclaimed Property Act, 765 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 1025/0.05 et seq. (2004) did not apply. Next, a request for a return of overpaid taxes was properly characterized as a claim for a refund. The language and the legislative history of 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 200/20-175 indicated that it applied to refund claims for duplicate payments such as those made here. Finally, because plaintiffs' tax bills had been paid when they tendered the duplicate payments, they had a right to a refund of those payments on the date that they were made, and the limitations period began at that time. Thus, the claims were time-barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1126 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bryant


NO. 4-05-1071


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1429



May 31, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Bryant, 231 Ill. 2d 638, 899 N.E.2d 1076, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 148, 326 Ill. Dec. 425 (2009)
Substituted opinion at, On reconsideration by People v. Bryant, 391 Ill. App. 3d 1072, 909 N.E.2d 391, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 543, 330 Ill. Dec. 678 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Coles County. NO.05CF141. Honorable Gary W. Jacobs, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court of Coles County (Illinois) convicted defendant of two counts of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court first held that defendant had forfeited his argument that the trial court erred in granting the State's motion to take the victim's testimony via closed-circuit television under 725 ILCS 5/106B-5(a)(2) (2004). At trial, defendant had objected to the testimony only on the ground of confrontation, not for failure to meet the statutory requirements. Furthermore, this situation was similar to another case in which the court had concluded that the trial court's ruling was adequate in context, although the trial court had not invoked the precise statutory language. Next, the victim was present for cross-examination and answered questions asked of her by defense counsel. Thus, she was not unavailable as a witness, and any prior statement of hers being offered at trial under 725 ILCS 5/115-10 (2004) was a nonevent for purposes of the Confrontation Clause of U.S. Const. amend. VI. Finally, although the trial court did not give the pattern jury instruction with regard to § 115-10 at the end of the trial, it did give that instruction orally after each of three witnesses testified about the victim's hearsay statements. Thus, there was no plain error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Fort


No. 1-04-1937


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


373 Ill. App. 3d 882; 869 N.E.2d 950; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 572; 311 Ill. Dec. 937



May 29, 2007, Decided 
May 29, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 17, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable William G. Lacy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A trial judge convicted defendant of possession of a controlled substance. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to 30 months' imprisonment, imposed a $ 500 drug assessment, ordered defendant to pay a $ 5 fee for deposit in the Spinal Cord Injury Paralysis Cure Research Trust, and ordered extraction of defenant's blood and perpetual storage of his DNA. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the $ 500 drug assessment was really a fine and should not have been imposed without a finding of defendant's ability to pay it as required by 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-9-1(d) (2002), and that he was entitled to a credit of $ 185 against the assessment for the 37 days spend in presentence incarceration. The appellate court agreed that the assessment was a fine, declining the State's invitation to reject the consistent line of appellate decision that allowed a sentence credit against the drug assessment. In addition, the appellate court found nothing in the Senate debates that indicated an intent that the drug assessment be anything other than a species of fine. Defendant also argued that his due process rights were violated by the imposition of a fee for deposit in the Spinal Cord Injury Paralysis Cure Research Trust, because it was an arbitrary and unreasonable exercise of police power. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the fee could properly be viewed as a criminal penalty. Finally, the appellate court held that the DNA extraction did not violate defendant's constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The costs and fees order was amended to reflect a credit of $ 185 against the $ 500 "Assessment Controlled Substance." The $ 5 fee for the Spinal Cord Trust was affirmed. The trial court's order that blood be extracted from defendant for storage of his DNA was affirmed.

Express Valet, Inc. v. City of Chicago

CASE SUMMARY:

People v. Carodine


No. 1-05-2775


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


374 Ill. App. 3d 16; 869 N.E.2d 869; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 543; 311 Ill. Dec. 856



May 21, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 17, 2007.
Rehearing denied by People v. Carodine, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 800 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 5, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 05 CR 12518. Honorable John P. Kirby, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of two counts of possession of a controlled substance following a bench trial.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court found that the trial court did not err under the Fourth Amendment and Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 (1970) by denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence recovered from a dryer vent because defendant did not have a reasonable expectation of privacy to the dryer vent. The State proved defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of possession of a controlled substance because it was highly unlikely that anyone tampered with the contents of the dryer vent between the time officers broke surveillance and the time the officers recovered the narcotics from the vent. Defendant was precluded from arguing insufficiency of the chain of custody because defendant stipulated that a proper chain of custody was maintained at all times, depriving the State of the opportunity to correct any deficiencies at the trial level. A $ 5 Spinal Cord Injury Paralysis Cure Research Trust Fund fine was proper, but a $ 20 Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund fine was improper because defendant was already properly fined $ 500 under the controlled substance assessment. Defendant was entitled to a $ 575 credit toward the $ 500 controlled substance assessment and a $ 100 trauma fund charge.


OUTCOME: Defendant was entitled to a $ 575 credit toward the $ 600 in fines, and the $ 20 penalty was improper. As modified the judgment was affirmed.

Ill. Hotel & Lodging Ass'n v. Ludwig


No. 1-06-2228


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


374 Ill. App. 3d 193; 869 N.E.2d 846; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 537; 311 Ill. Dec. 833; 12 Wage & Hour Cas. 2d (BNA) 1060; 154 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,408



May 18, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 17, 2007.
Appeal denied by Ill. Hotel & Lodging Ass'n v. Ludwig, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1494 (Ill., Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 05 CH 13796. Honorable James F. Henry, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hotel association filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant, the Director of the Illinois Department of Labor, in which plaintiff sought to have 3.1 of the One Day Rest in Seven Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 140/3.1 (Supp. 2005), declared unconstitutional. Defendant union intervened. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted defendants' motion for summary judgment. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Section 3.1 required employers to provide hotel room attendants with breaks, a meal period, and a break room. It applied only to hotels in Cook County. The court held that § 3.1 was not special legislation under Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 because it applied to Cook County. The legislature could have rationally concluded that the statute would protect hotel room attendants from overwork in the jurisdiction where the majority of such employees would be affected and in the one best positioned to absorb the costs of the new regulations. For the same reasons, the statute did not violate equal protection. Next, the statute was not preempted by the National Labor Relations Act (NLRA), 29 U.S.C.S. § 151 et seq. It did not regulate conduct governed by 29 U.S.C.S. § 157 or 29 U.S.C.S. § 158; rather, it set forth a minimum labor standard for individual attendants, whether they were unionized or nonunionized. Such standards were not preempted by the NLRA. 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 140/3.1 neither encouraged nor discouraged the collective bargaining processes. Furthermore, § 3.1 did not proscribe or support strikes, lockouts, use of replacement workers, or any other economic weapon of self-help.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

People v. Starnes


No. 1-04-2704


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


374 Ill. App. 3d 132; 869 N.E.2d 834; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 538; 311 Ill. Dec. 821



May 18, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 17, 2007.
Appeal denied by People v. Starnes, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1514 (Ill., Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Lawrence P. Fox, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; mittimus ordered corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted her following a jury trial of the first-degree murder of her infant son and sentencing her to 50 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court rejected defendant's argument that the prosecution's comments during rebuttal denied defendant a fair trial. When viewed in context of defense counsel's argument that the police had a "theory," the medical examiner was in on it, and the police "fed" defendant the statements she made, the prosecutor's response was proper. Moreover, any error would be harmless based on the strength of the evidence demonstrating defendant's guilt. The sentence was an appropriate exercise of discretion, and the 50-year term was not excessive, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(a) (2000). The trial court was informed of defendant's youth, her difficult background, her lack of a criminal history, and her potential for rehabilitation. She murdered her own defenseless, infant son. She did this, as reflected in a videotaped statement, because she wanted to attend a party with her boyfriend and felt the baby was holding her back. She was not prejudiced by any error relating to jury instructions regarding eligibility for an extended-term sentence. The record reflected that no enhanced sentence was imposed and no comment by the judge suggested an enhanced sentence was considered.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The clerk of the circuit court was ordered to correct the mittimus to reflect credit for 943 days defendant spent in custody prior to sentencing.

Poindexter v. State


NO. 4-05-0709


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


372 Ill. App. 3d 1021; 869 N.E.2d 139; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 562; 311 Ill. Dec. 465



May 17, 2007, Modified


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Poindexter v. State, 225 Ill. 2d 675, 875 N.E.2d 1123, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1173, 314 Ill. Dec. 836 (2007)
Affirmed by Poindexter v. State, 229 Ill. 2d 194, 890 N.E.2d 410, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 307, 321 Ill. Dec. 688 (Ill., Apr. 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court Sangamon County. No. 04MR305. Honorable Leo J. Zappa, Jr., Judge Presiding.
Poindexter v. State, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1146 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., Dec. 12, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sangamon County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment for plaintiff community spouses that enjoined defendants, a state family services agency and a state human services agency, from seeking any support from the income that the community spouses earned while their spouses, the institutionalized spouses, were in long-term care facilities and receiving Medicaid. The State, through those agencies, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered judgment for the community spouses, and enjoined the state family services agency and the state human services agency from seeking any support from the income the community spouses earned while the institutionalized spouses were receiving Medicaid. The State of Illinois, acting through those two state agencies, appealed and asserted that: (1) the community spouses did not exhaust administrative remedies, (2) the community spouses forfeited their claims by failing to raise them before the administrative agency, and (3) the court erred in finding the Medicare Catastrophic Coverage Act of 1988, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1396r-5, preempted the spousal-support provisions of 305 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/10-1 et seq. (2004). The appellate court found that the community spouses were not required to exhaust administrative remedies since the issue in the case, interpretation of a federal statute, was one purely of law and did not fall within an administrative agency's particular expertise. It also found that their claims, being constitutional, were outside an administrative agency's purview, and that the federal statute did not indicate an intent to preempt the state law.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

People v. Bell


No. 1-05-2493


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


373 Ill. App. 3d 811; 869 N.E.2d 807; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 521; 311 Ill. Dec. 794



May 14, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 17, 2007.
Appeal denied by People v. Bell, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1258 (Ill., Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 05 CR 7923. Honorable Joseph M. Claps, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver after a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) Defendant filed a motion for a new trial, which was denied, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court found the trial court did not violate the Fourth Amendment by limiting the cross-examination of an officer by allowing the State to invoke the surveillance location privilege, because the public interest in preserving the secrecy of a surveillance location used to monitor drug activity outweighed defendant's interest in disclosure to prepare a defense. The trial court also did not err by not appointing new counsel to investigate defendant's posttrial pro se motion of ineffective assistance, because defendant was not prejudiced by counsel's failure to secure the testimony of a coworker. The testimony would simply have established that defendant was in the same area where an officer testified he saw him selling narcotics. Nor did counsel's inability to locate the coworker fall below objective standards of reasonableness in discharging his duties to defendant. Counsel's efforts were indicative of due diligence in discharging his duties to defendant and not indicative of an abandonment of the case. The trial court did err by imposing a $ 20 fine for the Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund because the court properly imposed a controlled substance assessment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as modified.

Walliser v. Martin


No. 1-06-0408


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1434



May 11, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 05 CH 9631. Honorable Martin S. Agran, Judge Presiding.
Walliser v. Martin, 940 N.E.2d 307, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 2625 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2007)
Walliser v. Mineta, 33 Fed. Appx. 826, 2002 U.S. App. LEXIS 7503 (7th Cir. Ill., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that dismissed plaintiff property owner's complaint for administrative review that the property owner filed to challenge defendant state transportation agency's condemnation of his property in order to extend an interstate highway. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner approached the state transportation agency and requested that it purchase a parcel of property from him because the parcel was located directly in the right-of-way for a proposed federal interstate highway. Its representatives allegedly made certain promises to him. Eventually, he conveyed the parcel to the state transportation agency in return for a specified payment. However, he did not leave the property. The state transportation agency had to file forcible entry and detainer actions. He later vacated the parcel. He filed a complaint for administrative review to challenge the condemnation of the property. The trial court dismissed the complaint as having been untimely filed and as being barred by res judicata. The appellate court found that res judicata barred each of the claims that the property owner had raised. It so concluded because it found that over the many years that the condemnation action was litigated, there had been a final judgment on the merits of the claims that were rendered by a court of competent jurisdiction, that there had been an identity of the cause of action, and an identity of the parties or their privies.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Cazacu


No. 1-06-0376


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


373 Ill. App. 3d 465; 869 N.E.2d 381; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 484; 311 Ill. Dec. 707



May 10, 2007, Decided 
May 10, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 19, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Timothy Chambers, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after it found defendant guilty on two counts of possession of an altered card pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 250/15 (2004). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted on two counts of possession of an altered card pursuant to the Illinois Credit Card and Debit Card Act, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 250/15 (2004), and was sentenced to one year of probation. On appeal, defendant contended that: (1) the trial court erred in admitting business records into evidence despite the lack of proper foundation for them, (2) the trial court erred in denying his motion for a directed verdict, (3) the charging instrument lacked the necessary certainty, and (4) 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 250/15 (2004) contained an unconstitutional mandatory presumption. The appellate court found that the State did fail to lay a proper foundation for the records that the State's expert testified about, but no reversible error occurred because defendant stipulated to the testimony that the two true card holders would have given, defendant waived any error regarding the motion for directed finding by not renewing that motion at the close of the evidence, the charging instrument was sufficiently specific, and defendant's convictions could stand after the unconstitutional portion of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 250/15 (2004) was severed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments were affirmed.

City of Elgin v. All Nations Worship Ctr.


No. 2-06-0793


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


373 Ill. App. 3d 167; 868 N.E.2d 385; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 482; 311 Ill. Dec. 385



May 9, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 22, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 04--OV--1418. Honorable Michael J. Colwell, Judge, Presiding.
City of Elgin v. All Nations Worship Ctr., 369 Ill. App. 3d 664, 860 N.E.2d 853, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1239, 308 Ill. Dec. 9 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a worship center, appealed an order of Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) denying its petition for attorney fees from a city pursuant to the Illinois Religious Freedom Restoration Act, 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 35/20 (2004).


OVERVIEW: The city filed a complaint alleging that the worship center was violating a zoning ordinance by holding services in a zone which did not allow a church as either a permitted or conditional use. The city ultimately amended the ordinance to provide that a church could be a conditional use in. 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 35/20 (2004) stated that a party who prevailed in an action to enforce the Act against a government was entitled to recover its attorney fees and costs. The appellate court held that an agreed order entered by the trial court in which the city agreed to allow the center to occupy the property while the city considered whether to amend the ordinance was temporary and, ultimately, pyrrhic. Rather than an alteration of the legal relationship of the parties, the order appeared to be an agreement to preserve the status quo. The center's argument that it prevailed because the city voluntarily amended its ordinance also failed. The order provided only that the city would consider amending the ordinance, and the actual amendment was purely voluntary.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Moore


No. 1-05-0515


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


373 Ill. App. 3d 367; 869 N.E.2d 177; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 400; 311 Ill. Dec. 503



April 23, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 19, 2007.
Appeal denied by, Vacated by People v. Moore, 873 N.E.2d 941, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1347, 314 Ill. Dec. 11 (Ill., 2007)
Vacated by, in part People v. Moore, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1193 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Nov. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 82 C 12459, 82 C 12460. Honorable Paul P. Biebel, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his motion for deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) testing under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/116-3 (2004). He contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion because the identity at issue requirement was unconstitutional as applied to him; he also argued that his due process rights were violated because the trial court ruled on issues beyond the scope of the hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to robberies and rapes. He requested the testing, challenging the voluntariness of his guilty plea. Preliminarily, the state appellate court declined to consider his constitutionality argument because defendant failed to meet the chain of custody requirement of § 116-3(b)(2); he failed to allege with specificity if the proper authorities took DNA, when the DNA was received, or mention anything pertaining to its current condition. Nevertheless, the appellate court then addressed, and rejected, defendant's constitutionality arguments on both due process and equal protection grounds. Because § 116-3(b)(1) implicated neither a suspect classification nor a fundamental right, the appellate court applied the rational basis test, finding that the legislature could have included that subsection to restrict the availability of DNA testing to those who maintained their actual innocence. Further, while the appellate court was not prepared to hold that a guilty plea categorically divested a defendant of the opportunity to request DNA testing, it held that defendant could not satisfy the identity at issue requirement due to his guilty plea, which, it held, was voluntary.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for DNA testing.

People v. Smith


No. 1-04-1946


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


372 Ill. App. 3d 762; 866 N.E.2d 1192; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 374; 310 Ill. Dec. 590



April 19, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 30, 2007.
Appeal denied by People v. Smith, 225 Ill. 2d 669, 875 N.E.2d 1121, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1396, 314 Ill. Dec. 834 (2007)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Cause remanded by People v. Smith, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 374 (Ill., Apr. 2, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 99 CR 1111. Honorable Bertina Lampkin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; sentence modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder, armed robbery, and attempted armed robbery. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to 60 years' imprisonment for murder, a concurrent term of 20 years for armed robbery, and a consecutive term of 8 years for attempted armed robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's sole contention on appeal was that the trial court abused its discretion when it denied defendant's request for a separate jury verdict form for felony murder. Defendant argued that if the jury had returned a verdict of guilty for the count of felony murder based on the attempted armed robbery of the victim, defendant would not have received a consecutive eight-year sentence because the offense underlying the felony murder charge would not have supported a separate conviction and sentence. The appellate court held that when a defendant who is charged with intentional or knowing murder and felony murder requests a separate verdict form for felony murder and such a request has a basis in the evidence presented at trial, the separate verdict form must be given or consecutive sentences cannot be imposed based on the offense underlying the felony murder, pursuant to section 5-8-4(a) of the Unified Code of Corrections, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-4(a) (2004). Because a separate form was not given, eight years might have been added to defendant's sentence and thus, the appellate court concluded, modification was required.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was modified so that the attempted armed robbery sentence was to run concurrently with the other sentences. The judgment of the trial court was otherwise affirmed.

People v. McCombs


No. 3-04-0575 (Consolidated with Nos. 3-04-0576, 3-05-0417, 3-06-0320)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


372 Ill. App. 3d 967; 866 N.E.2d 1200; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 380; 310 Ill. Dec. 598


January 10, 2007, Submitted; November 22, 2006, Assigned  
April 19, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Released for Publication May 23, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Whiteside County, Illinois. Nos. 99--CF--379, 00--CF--74. Honorable Tim Slavin, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After separate bench trials, the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Whiteside County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of felony theft in each of two cases. Defendant appealed and the cases were consolidated for purposes of appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was entitled to a new trial on both charges because in each case defendant was tried in absentia without counsel. The appellate court agreed, finding, with respect to one charge, that defendant had not waived the right to counsel and thus, could not be tried in absentia without counsel present. As for the second charge, the appellate court noted that the legislature intended no exception based on a prior waiver of counsel. Therefore, conducting a trial of defendant in absentia without counsel present was reversible error regardless of whether there was a valid waiver of counsel. The appellate court further noted that there was nothing to prevent a trial court from issuing a warrant for defendant's arrest for failure to appear for trial and then, upon defendant's arrest, conducting a trial. If defendant could not be found, the court could appoint counsel, provide a reasonable time for counsel to prepare and then conduct the trial in absentia.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cases were remanded for new trials.

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 20, 2007. [***1] 
Rehearing denied by Bd. of Educ. v. Bd. of Educ., 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 713 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., June 20, 2007)
Appeal granted by Bd. of Educ. v. Bd. of Educ., 226 Ill. 2d 580, 879 N.E.2d 929, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1763, 316 Ill. Dec. 541 (2007)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by Bd. of Educ. v. Bd. of Educ., 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1423 (Ill., Oct. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County. No. 05 MR 225. Honorable Herman Haase, Judge, Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 12th Judicial Circuit Court, Will County (Illinois), entered a judgment that affirmed a decision of appellee state education board granting a petition to detach certain property from appellant one school district and annex it to appellee second school district pursuant to 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-2b (1998). In so doing, it made an independent finding titled "Constitutional Issues." The one school district appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellee property owners petitioned pursuant to 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-2b (1998) to detach property from the one school district and annex it to the second school district. The state education board could only address whether the detachment requirements under that statutory section had been met. The hearing officer found the property owners met those requirements. In so concluding, he found that the second school district's argument that the statute violated federal law to be outside the scope of the state education board's statutory and regulatory authority. The state superintendent then granted the petition. The trial court affirmed and made an independent finding that the state education board's actions did not create a constitutional impediment or violate federal law. On further review, the appellate court found that the state education board had jurisdiction to grant the petition, the state education board did not err in finding that the statutory requirements had been met, the trial court lacked both the jurisdiction and evidence to make the independent finding, and the statute was facially unconstitutional since it conflicted with federal law on the same subject.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated that portion of the trial court's judgment titled "Constitutional Issues," affirmed the findings of the state education board on those issues that it considered, and remanded the matter to the state education board for further proceedings.

People v. Johnson


No. 1-05-1050


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


372 Ill. App. 3d 772; 867 N.E.2d 49; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 315; 310 Ill. Dec. 736



March 30, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Released for Publication May 30, 2007.

Appeal denied by People v. Johnson, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1428 (Ill., Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Nicholas Ford, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following bench trial, defendant was convicted of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced him to 18 years in the Illinois Department of Correction and assessed a $ 20 penalty for the Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund, a $ 5 fee for deposit into the Spinal Cord Injury Paralysis Cure Research Trust Fund, and a $ 2,000 controlled substance assessment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court failed to properly inquire into his pro se claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the trial court reviewed defendant's motion and specifically gave him the opportunity to argue, explain, and support his allegations. In addition, the record did not reflect ineffective assistance of counsel but, rather, inter alia, trial strategy in the context of a choice not to litigate a motion to quash arrest and suppress evidence. Defendant also argued that the trial court's use of a presentence investigation (PSI) report to determine the existence of a prior conviction was unconstitutional. The appellate court disagreed, holding that such use of the PSI did not violate defendant's constitutional rights and that the PSI was an acceptable source for the trial judge to use when considering defendant's prior criminal background. Finally, as to the fines imposed, the appellate court concluded, inter alia, that defendant was entitled to credit against the controlled substance assessment for his 453 days of incarceration prior to his conviction and that the violent crimes assessment was improper.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, as was the charge for the Spinal Cord Fund. The $ 20 for the Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund. The fees and costs order was modified to reflect a credit of $ 2,265 toward the $ 2,000 drug assessment, thereby negating the drug assessment in its entirety. The mittimus and sentencing was ordered modified to reflect a conviction for possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, to wit: heroin.

Townsend v. Fassbinder


No. 2-06-0226


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois) denied the motions for directed verdict and judgment notwithstanding the verdict filed by defendants, a general contractor owner and general contractor, entered a judgment that found them negligent, and entered a judgment on a jury's verdict awarding damages to plaintiffs, a claimant and spouse. The general contractor owner and general contractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant and spouse sued, inter alia, the general contractor owner and general contractor for injuries the claimant sustained in a fall while he was working at the general contractor's house. The general contractor owner denied that the claimant was his employee and asserted that the claimant was responsible for his own injuries. The general contractor claimed that the claimant was its immediate employee and that he was barred from suing the general contractor because of the exclusivity remedy provision of the Workers' Compensation Act, 820 Ill. The trial court then denied their motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict. On appeal, the appellate court found that no error occurred in denying the motions for directed verdict and for judgment n.o.v., as the issue of who employed the claimant could not be decided as a matter of law.

People v. Lucas

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT

March 29, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Released for Publication May 2, 2007.
Appeal granted by People v. Lucas, 225 Ill. 2d 657, 875 N.E.2d 1119, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1183, 314 Ill. Dec. 832 (2007)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Cause remanded by People v. Lucas, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1419 (Ill., Oct. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit, Bureau County, Illinois, No. 05-CF-31. Honorable Scott A. Madson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of driving while his license was revoked (DWLR) under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-303(a), (d) (2004), unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.1(a) (2004), and armed violence under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33A-2(a) (2004). The Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit, Bureau County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to 30 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his conviction for armed violence should be vacated because a conviction for enhanced DWLR could not serve as a predicate felony for armed violence and if enhanced DWLR could be used as a predicate felony, it had to be proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court held that DWLR could be a predicate offense for armed violence because such use deterred individuals from carrying a weapon while committing the felony of driving while their license was revoked. The appellate court further found that the evidence demonstrated that defendant carried a weapon while driving a vehicle illegally and that when the officer attempted to stop him, defendant purposefully evaded the officer and attempted to hide in a nearby house. Defendant also claimed that his sentence should be vacated because it was unconstitutional, an abuse of the court's discretion and violated one-act, one-crime principles. The appellate court disagreed, concluding that the sentence did not contravene the proportionate penalties clause simply because the predicate felony offense fell into the lowest felony classification, nor was the sentence excessive in light of the nature of the offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Comp. Stat. Ann. 130/1 et seq. The landscape contractors association appealed.

Brdar v. Cottrell, Inc.


NO. 5-04-0415


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


372 Ill. App. 3d 690; 867 N.E.2d 1085; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 305; 311 Ill. Dec. 99



March 27, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Motion to Publish Granted March 27, 2007.
Appeal denied by Brdar v. Cottrell, Inc., 224 Ill. 2d 572, 871 N.E.2d 54, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1051, 312 Ill. Dec. 654 (Ill., May 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 00-L-181. Honorable A. A. Matoesian, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant cargo trailer manufacturer challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) in favor of plaintiffs, a truck driver and his wife, for injuries the driver sustained when a chain broke while he was attempting to tie down an automobile to a cargo trailer.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court found the trial court properly exercised its discretion in denying motions to exclude an expert's testimony on grounds of late and/or inadequate disclosure (Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 213). The manufacturer never sought an order to compel a more detailed disclosure, waiting instead until after the original trial setting had been continued, due to its own last-minute discovery of the chain, to seek to exclude the expert's testimony. The trial court also did not err in dismissing the manufacturer's third-party complaint on the ground that it did not file its complaint until after the statute of limitations for contribution claims, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-204(b) (2002), had expired. Although the manufacturer did not learn the specific identity of potential third-party defendants from plaintiffs' complaint, the complaint gave it notice that it might have a contribution claim against the manufacturer or distributor of the chain. The trial court applied the wrong standard in denying plaintiffs' request to submit punitive-damages claim to the jury, relying on a statute found to be unconstitutional. However, they were not automatically entitled to a new trial on the issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the cause was remanded for further proceedings, with directions for the court to make the determination required of it by 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-604.1 (2002). If the court concluded that there was a reasonable likelihood that plaintiffs would recover punitive damages, they would be entitled to a new trial limited to that issue.

Bigelow v. City of Rolling Meadows


No. 1-06-0292


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


372 Ill. App. 3d 60; 865 N.E.2d 221; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 243; 309 Ill. Dec. 858



March 19, 2007, Decided  
March 19, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected April 19, 2007. Released for Publication May 3, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 CH 04739. The Honorable Mary Anne Mason, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee beneficial owners filed an action against appellant city in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), for a declaratory judgment that they were the owners of a strip of property, and that the city had no interest in the property. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court granted summary judgment to the beneficial owners. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The subject property ran adjacent to lots owned by the beneficial owners. The city argued that the beneficial owners' action was time-barred, and that the subject property was dedicated to and accepted by the city for the benefit of the public. On appeal, the court found that the Illinois Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act's one-year statute of limitations under 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 10/8-101 (2002) did not bar the beneficial owners' action because, pursuant to 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 10/2-101 (2002), the beneficial owners did not seek damages. Additionally, although the subject property was designated as a named avenue, there were no marks or notations on the plat evidencing an intent to dedicate the property for use by the public. Accordingly, there was no statutory dedication under 765 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 205/3 (2002). Finally, because the city addressed only the statutory dedication of the subject property in the lower court, any argument concerning a common-law dedication was waived. Moreover, because there was no evidence of clear, unequivocal, and unambiguous donative intent, there was no common-law dedication.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
