People v. Smith


NO. 4-06-0274


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


371 Ill. App. 3d 817; 867 N.E.2d 1150; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 238; 311 Ill. Dec. 164



March 13, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal granted by People v. Smith, 224 Ill. 2d 589, 871 N.E.2d 60, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1032, 312 Ill. Dec. 660 (2007)
Remanded by People v. Smith, 228 Ill. 2d 95, 885 N.E.2d 1053, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 282, 319 Ill. Dec. 373 (2008)
Vacated by, On remand at People v. Smith, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 659 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., June 27, 2008)
Vacated by, On remand at People v. Smith, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1357 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., July 28, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 03CF2166. Honorable Thomas J. Difanis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to possession of a controlled substance with the intent to deliver. The Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) sentenced him to 10 years' imprisonment under the agreement. Later, the trial court denied defendant's motion to correct sentence and then sent a letter informing defendant's warden that the pleadings were frivolous and patently without merit under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3(d) (2003). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by finding that his "motion to correct sentence," in which he challenged his mandatory supervised release term, was a "lawsuit" as defined by 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3(d) (2003). The appellate court found that, although defendant titled his pleading as a "motion to correct sentence," the trial court treated the motion as a petition under the Postconviction Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 through 122-8 (2004), which was included in the definition of "lawsuit" in 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3(d) (2003). Because of defendant's direct appeal, the trial court did not have jurisdiction to entertain defendant's issue in a freestanding motion. Thus, defendant had to raise his claim in a statutory collateral proceeding. Defendant failed to set forth any statutory authority for the motion. Accordingly, the "motion to correct sentence" was not a cognizable action under Illinois law, and thus the Shellstrom procedures did not apply. Defendant did not suggest any other statutory collateral cause of action in which he could have raised his mandatory-supervised-release issue and not have been subjected to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3(d) (2003).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1149 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Doll


No. 2-05-0484


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


371 Ill. App. 3d 1131; 864 N.E.2d 916; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 231; 309 Ill. Dec. 675



March 12, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Released for Publication April 27, 2007.
Appeal denied by People v. Doll, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1653 (Ill., Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 04--CF--2514. Honorable Robert J. Anderson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of unlawful restraint under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/10-3(a) (2004), and sentenced to six years' imprisonment. Because defendant was convicted of unlawful restraint of a minor, the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) required defendant to register as a sex offender pursuant to the Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/2(B)(1.5), 3(a) (2004). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the State failed to prove him guilty of unlawful restraint beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court disagreed, noting that the State presented sufficient evidence through the victim's testimony to establish defendant's commission of the offense; among other things, the victim testified that defendant grabbed her, took her through a door, "jumped" her up, and grabbed her pants and pulled them down to her ankles. The State's failure to call the victim's family members did not give rise to an inference that their testimony would have harmed the State's case, as the defense could called them to testify the family members, who were equally available to the defense, to impeach the victim but chose not to. Defendant also contended that the Act was unconstitutional as applied to him, because his crime did not involve any sexual motivation or sexual component. The appellate court disagreed, concluding that the Act was rationally related to the protection of children and that it rationally applied to those convicted of unlawful restraint of children because those defendants might have a greater propensity to harm a child.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Addison


Nos. 1-03-0507 and 1-03-2541 (Consolidated)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


371 Ill. App. 3d 941; 864 N.E.2d 831; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 191; 309 Ill. Dec. 590



March 6, 2007, Decided  
March 6, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Released for Publication April 20, 2007.
Rehearing denied by People v. Addison, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 434 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Apr. 3, 2007)
Appeal denied by People v. Addison, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1568 (Ill., Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Marjorie C. Laws, Judge Presiding.
People v. Addison, 322 Ill. App. 3d 1042, 798 N.E.2d 423, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 2221, 278 Ill. Dec. 321 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of home invasion and armed robbery and sentenced to a 12-year prison term. The convictions and sentence were affirmed. Defendant filed a petition for relief from judgment under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 (2002) and a pro se postconviction petition. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) summarily denied defendant's petitions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court determined that the circuit court's dismissal of defendant's 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 petition was proper because (1) the circuit court had the authority to sua sponte dismiss a patently frivolous § 2-1401 petition under the Code of Civil Procedure, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1-100 et seq. (2002), and (2) defendant had previously and unsuccessfully raised the same issues on direct appeal. The circuit court erred in determining that defendant's 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-1401 petition was untimely, but this error was harmless in light of the finding that the petition was without merit. Also, the circuit court did not recharacterize the § 2-1401 petition as one brought under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act (Act), 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-1 et seq. (2002). The pro se postconviction petition was properly denied under the Act because (1) there were no affidavits or other supporting documentation attached to the petition, (2) each allegation of ineffective assistance of counsel had been raised twice previously, and (3) his allegation regarding the denial of a motion to suppress could have been raised on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

People v. Wear


NO. 4-06-0353


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


371 Ill. App. 3d 517; 867 N.E.2d 1027; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 37; 311 Ill. Dec. 41



January 19, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal granted by People v. Wear, 224 Ill. 2d 591, 871 N.E.2d 61, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 905, 312 Ill. Dec. 661 (2007)
Affirmed by People v. Wear, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 636 (Ill., July 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Greene County. No. 0DT1. Honorable James W. Day, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved for reconsideration of an order in which the Circuit Court of Greene County (Illinois) denied his motion to rescind the summary suspension of his driver's license and his motion to suppress evidence and quash his arrest for driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI), 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-501(a)(2) (2004). The court granted the motion for reconsideration. The State of Illinois appealed. Defendant moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The arresting police officer followed defendant to the home of defendant's girlfriend and entered the home to question defendant after observing defendants' erratic driving, defendant's failure to stop at the officer's directives, and the officer's smelling alcohol on defendant's breath. The officer served upon defendant a notice of the summary suspension of his driver's license for refusing to submit to a chemical test. On appeal, the court found that, because the State nol-prossed the DUI case after the granting of the motion for reconsideration, the portion of the appeal pertaining to the suppression of evidence and the quashing of the arrest (an interlocutory ruling that vanished with the criminal case) was to be dismissed. As for the rescission of the summary suspension, that ruling occurred in a civil proceeding separate and distinct from the DUI case; therefore, the nolle prosequi had no effect on that ruling, which was appealable as a final judgment. Moreover, the trial court's rescission of the summary suspension of defendant's driver license was improper because, pursuant to the doctrine of hot pursuit, there was no violation of defendant's Fourth Amendment rights.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed in part insomuch as it pertained to the suppression of evidence and quashing of the arrest. The trial court's rescission of the summary suspension of defendant's driver's license was reversed.

People v. Alexander


No. 3-04-0892


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


369 Ill. App. 3d 955; 862 N.E.2d 240; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 27; 308 Ill. Dec. 642



January 18, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 21, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12<th> Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois, No. 03-CF-364. Honorable Daniel J. Rozak, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of sexual exploitation of a child. Additionally, the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois, ordered defendant to pay a fee for the collection of his DNA. The issues on appeal were (1) whether the State proved that he possessed the requisite mens rea for sexual exploitation of a child, and (2) whether the trial court possessed the authority to impose a DNA collection fee.


OVERVIEW: The victims testified that defendant exposed himself to them, masturbated in front of them, and touched one child inappropriately. The appeals court found that even considering the other child's testimony that nothing came out of defendant's penis, it was not "inherently implausible" that a rational trier of fact, confronted with this evidence, could have found that there was sufficient proof that defendant's sexual gratification was proven beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant also argued that the trial court exceeded its statutory authority in ordering him to pay a fee for the collection of his DNA. The fee was not a cost authorized by statute. Thus, under the order, the fee was an unconstitutional infringement on the legislative power rather than a valid exercise of judicial power. Further, the chief judge's general administrative authority under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. Rule 21(b) could not appropriately encompass or purport to exercise a power so closely akin to the revenue raising power of the legislature. Therefore, the administrative order granting the trial judge specific authority to impose the $ 10 collection fee exceeded the powers granted to the chief judge under Rule 21(b).


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of two counts of sexual exploitation of a child was affirmed. The DNA collection fee was vacated.

People v. Allen


NO. 4-05-0683


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


371 Ill. App. 3d 279; 868 N.E.2d 297; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 30; 311 Ill. Dec. 297



January 16, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by People v. Allen, 223 Ill. 2d 639, 865 N.E.2d 970, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 746, 310 Ill. Dec. 250 (Ill., Mar. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 03CF2215. Honorable Heidi Ladd, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with unlawful delivery of a controlled substance for delivering 1 gram or more but less than 15 grams of heroin (720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/401(c)(1) (2002)). Defendant pleaded not guilty but was convicted after a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois). The trial court sentenced defendant to a 12-year prison term. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed he was denied his right to a fair trial by the State's misstatement of the law, which allowed the jury to convict him without finding that the State had proved his intent to promote or facilitate the commission of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt. The appeals court found that the prosecutor's use of the word "unwittingly," while perhaps misleading out of context, was not a misstatement of the law. Defendant argued that he was entitled to an additional day of credit for time served and an additional $ 5 credit toward his fines because the day of sentencing should be included in calculating the number of days he spent in custody. Defendant was remanded to the Department of Corrections (DOC) on the day of sentencing. Prior case law indicated that a defendant should not be given credit for the day he was remanded to the DOC. A $ 5 spinal-cord-injury fee was a fine and was unconstitutional. The State conceded, and the appeals court agreed, that the trial court had no statutory authority to impose a local anticrime fee when a defendant was sentenced to prison. The imposition of other fines was a judicial function beyond the authority of the clerk.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed, except the fines imposed by the clerk were vacated, and the case was remanded for proper imposition of the fines by the court.

People v. Martinez


1-04-2023


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


371 Ill. App. 3d 363; 862 N.E.2d 1022; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 15; 308 Ill. Dec. 819



January 12, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 22, 2007. As Corrected February 22, 2007.
Rehearing denied by People v. Martinez, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 265 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Mar. 6, 2007)
Appeal denied by People v. Martinez, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 540 (Ill., May 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CR 21122. Honorable Colleen McSweeney-Moore, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty on one count of reckless homicide. It then sentenced him to 14 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Despite the fact that defendant had several drinks, he drove his vehicle on to a highway. He was extremely intoxicated and drove it in the wrong direction. His vehicle collided with a motorcycle driven by the victim, killing the victim. Defendant was found guilty of reckless homicide and was sentenced to 14 years in prison. On appeal, he asserted that his sentence exceeded the maximum sentence permitted, that the crime was inadvertently referred to as "aggravated reckless homicide," that the State failed to produce photographs and measurements of the accident scene, that the State impermissibly allowed the jury to see certain photographic evidence, and that the 14-year sentence was excessive. The appellate court found his sentence was proper, as even though a new reckless homicide law had been enacted one year after his offense and one year before sentencing, the law made substantive changes to the offense, no plain error occurred regarding the inadvertent reference to "aggravated reckless homicide," the failure to produce the inadvertently-lost photos and measurements did not prejudice defendant, the photographic evidence was properly admitted, and the sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Mead Corp. v. Dep't of Revenue


No. 1-03-1160


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


371 Ill. App. 3d 108; 861 N.E.2d 1131; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 13; 308 Ill. Dec. 566



January 12, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 1, 2007.
Appeal denied by Mead Corp. v. Ill. Dep't of Revenue, 222 Ill. 2d 609, 862 N.E.2d 235, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 305, 308 Ill. Dec. 637 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by MeadWestvaco Corp. v. Ill. Dep't of Revenue, 128 S. Ct. 29, 168 L. Ed. 2d 806, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 9074 (U.S., 2007)
Vacated by, Remanded by Meadwestvaco Corp. v. Ill. Dep't of Revenue, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 3473 (U.S., Apr. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CH 7854. Honorable Alexander P. White, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sued appellees, the state revenue department and the state officials, in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), for injunctive and declaratory relief. The court found that the taxpayer and an electronic publisher were not unitary, the sale of the publisher by the taxpayer represented a liquidation in the business of electronic publishing, and the gain therefrom was apportionable business income. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a manufacturer of paper and packaging products, filed a combined unitary Illinois income tax return, which included the electronic publisher as a member of the taxpayer's unitary business group, and included in its Illinois combined apportionable business income the income earned by the publisher, but excluded the gain from the sale of the publisher. On appeal, the court found that the taxpayer did not establish that the finding of an operational purpose was against the manifest weight of the evidence, nor did it establish as clearly erroneous the conclusion that the gain was non-business income. Additionally, as the taxpayer reinvested the sale proceeds in its ongoing business, the gain satisfied the functional test and was properly identified as business income under 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1501(a)(1) (2002). Moreover, the taxpayer did not prove clearly and cogently that the apportionment of the gain was grossly disproportionate to its Illinois income or activities under 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/304(a) (2002). Finally, the taxpayer did not establish as clearly erroneous the trial court's conclusion that the gain from the sale was apportionable business income.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

People v. Brady


No. 2-04-1281


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


369 Ill. App. 3d 836; 861 N.E.2d 687; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 21; 308 Ill. Dec. 356



January 11, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 23, 2007.
Appeal denied by People v. Brady, 224 Ill. 2d 579, 871 N.E.2d 57, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 941, 312 Ill. Dec. 657 (Ill., May 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 03 CF 609. Honorable John R. Truitt, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) of drag racing, in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-504 (2002), and leaving the scene of a motor vehicle accident involving the death of a person, in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-401(b) (2002). He appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said it was not shown that he was "involved in a motor vehicle accident." The appellate court held participating in a drag race in which his opponent lost control and crashed showed defendant was implicated in the accident or connected with it in a substantial manner, which defined "involved in a motor vehicle accident." This language was not unconstitutionally vague as applied. It was definite enough to give a person of ordinary intelligence in defendant's position fair warning of his duties. 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-401 (2002) gave sufficiently definite standards for law enforcement and triers of fact so that its application did not depend on their private conceptions. Defendant showed no real or substantial risk of self-incrimination had he complied with statutory requirements to report the accident. He did not show an inference of causation would be reached from admitting involvement. Any inference resulting from his compliance would not have been testimonial or communicative and thus protected under the Fifth Amendment. His claim that danger of self-incrimination was heightened because the requisite information had to be reported in one hour was speculative.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

People v. Cole


NO. 4-05-0672


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


369 Ill. App. 3d 960; 874 N.E.2d 81; 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 8; 314 Ill. Dec. 171



January 9, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Cole, 223 Ill. 2d 644, 865 N.E.2d 971, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 802, 310 Ill. Dec. 251 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court of Adams County. No. 05CF64. Honorable Scott H. Walden, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's motion to suppress was denied. After a stipulated bench trial, defendant was found guilty of unlawful possession of 100 grams or more but less than 400 grams of cocaine, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/402(a)(2)(B) (2004). The Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to 12 years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress. Specifically, defendant claimed that the traffic stop was not justified because the officer believed that all suspended objects violated 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-503(c) (2004), and never testified that the beads materially obstructed defendant's view. Defendant further argued that even if the officer had testified that the beads materially obstructed defendant's view, that belief was unreasonable. The appellate court concluded that the officer acted under a mistake of law when the officer stopped defendant because something was suspended between defendant and the front windshield. The appellate court further concluded that a reasonable officer, correctly interpreting the law and considering the facts available at the time, would not have had reasonable suspicion to initiate the traffic stop. The officer did not testify that the quarter inch beads that were hanging from the mirror "materially obstructed" defendant's view, but only that they hindered defendant's view. The appellate court noted that § 12-503 was only violated by a "material obstruction."


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

City of Elgin v. All Nations Worship Ctr.


No. 2-06-0238


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


369 Ill. App. 3d 664; 860 N.E.2d 853; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1239; 308 Ill. Dec. 9



December 20, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 2, 2007.
Costs and fees proceeding at City of Elgin v. All Nations Worship Ctr., 373 Ill. App. 3d 167, 868 N.E.2d 385, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 482, 311 Ill. Dec. 385 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., May 9, 2007)
Appeal denied by City of Elgin v. All Nations Worship Ctr., 224 Ill. 2d 573, 871 N.E.2d 55, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 901, 312 Ill. Dec. 655 (Ill., May 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 04 OV 1418. Honorable Michael J. Cowell, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city filed a suit against defendant worship center in 2003, alleging violations of the city's zoning ordinance, Elgin, Ill., Mun. Code tit. 19. The center appealed after the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) dismissed its counterclaims, which challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance and asserted that it violated the Religious Land Use and Institutionalized Persons Act of 2000 (RLUIPA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000cc et seq.


OVERVIEW: In its counterclaim, the center contended that the zoning ordinance violated the U.S. Const. amend. XIV Equal Protection Clause and violated 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000cc(b)(1), (2), (3)(B), of the RLUIPA. The city dismissed its complaint after the counterclaim was filed, amended its zoning ordinance, and then moved to dismiss the counterclaim pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-619, on the ground that the amendments cured any defects in the ordinance. On appeal, the center did not dispute the amendments' curative effect. It argued that the former zoning ordinance was void ab initio and that it had acquired a vested right under the "common law" of zoning to use the property without obtaining a conditional use permit, as required by Elgin, Ill., Ordinance No. G65-05 (2005), which amended the ordinance. The court held that the appeal was not moot because it could grant relief to the center. The circuit court correctly rejected the center's claim that it acquired a vested right to continue operating. The void ab initio doctrine did not apply because the ordinance was not void on its face. Having failed to comply with it, the center did acquire vested rights arising from the former ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Miller v. Miller


No. 1-05-0243


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


369 Ill. App. 3d 46; 860 N.E.2d 519; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1140; 307 Ill. Dec. 865



December 12, 2006, Opinion Filed; December 12, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 24, 2007.
Appeal granted by Miller v. Miller, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 753 (Ill., Mar. 28, 2007)
Appeal granted by Miller v. Miller, 223 Ill. 2d 638, 865 N.E.2d 970, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 788, 310 Ill. Dec. 250 (2007)
Reversed by In re Miller, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1704 (Ill., Nov. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. 01 D5 30291. THE HONORABLE DANIEL RILEY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother filed a complaint against defendant employer seeking child support payments that the employer allegedly withheld from the father but failed to timely remit. After striking the employer's affirmative defense of laches, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered judgment against the employer for $1,172,100 in statutory penalties pursuant to 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 28/35 (2004). The employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found no error in the trial court's decision to strike the employer's affirmative defense of laches because the facts alleged by the employer di dnot support his contention that he was prejudiced in any way; the penalty imposed was not caused by the mother's delay in filing suit, but rather by the employer's knowing failure to remit child support withholdings in a timely manner. As for the employer's contention that 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 28/35 (2004) was unconstitutional as applied to the employer because the penalty imposed deprived the employer of his property without due process, the appellate court concluded that § 35 was unconstitutional as applied in this case because the $ 1,172,100 penalty imposed against the employer was approximately 47 times greater than the maximum criminal fine the legislature has found necessary to ensure a spouse's compliance with a child support obligation. The gross disparity between the penalty applied in this case and the maximum criminal fine demonstrated that the $ 1,172,100 penalty was wholly disproportionate to the employer's offense and obviously unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed and the case was remanded with directions to the circuit court that it hold a hearing to determine the appropriate penalty.

Poindexter v. State


NO. 4-05-0709


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1146



December 12, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified and rehearing denied by Poindexter v. People, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 562 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., May 17, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee community spouses sued the State of Illinois in the Circuit Court for Sangamon County (Illinois), for declaratory and injunctive relief, arguing that the State was illegally attempting to collect support from them for the support of their institutionalized spouses who were in long-term-care facilities and receiving Medicaid. The court enjoined the State from seeking support from the income of the community spouses. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Each of the complainants was a "community spouse" of an "institutionalized spouse" as those terms were defined in 42 U.S.C.S. § 1396r-5(h) (2000) of the Medicare Catastrophic Coverage Act of 1988 (MCCA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 1396r-5 (2000). The State, under authority found in Ill. Admin. Code tit. 89, § 103.10, sought spousal support from the community spouses' income for the amount that their income exceeded the minimum monthly maintenance needs allowance established by the MCCA in 42 U.S.C.S. § 1396r-5(d)(3) (2000). The community spouses argued that the State did not have the authority to do this pursuant to the MCCA. On appeal, the court found that Congress neither explicitly or impliedly preempted Illinois law, and Illinois law did not frustrate the execution of federal law. Therefore, the Illinois law regarding family responsibility was not preempted by the MCCA.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

People v. Luz M. (In re Janira T.)


No. 1-06-0111


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


368 Ill. App. 3d 883; 859 N.E.2d 1046; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1138; 307 Ill. Dec. 369



December 12, 2006, Decided  
December 12, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 18, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois Child Protective Division. No. 03 JA 01022. Honorable Kathleen M. Burke, Judge Presiding.
People v. Luz M. (In re Janira T.), 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 842 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 19, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois Child Protective Division termination the mother's parental rights to her minor daughter.


OVERVIEW: The mother contended that the State failed to show that the child was abused or neglected in the prior adjudicatory hearing, which was the predicate for the termination proceeding. The appellate court agreed with the State and the public guardian that the appellate court lacked jurisdiction to review the issue because the mother failed to appeal within 30 days of the entry of the dispositional order. The mother also contended that the State failed to prove by clear and convincing evidence that the mother was an unfit parent. The appellate court disagreed, noting that there was evidence that the mother failed to complete recommended services and was inconsistent with visitation. Next, the appellate court concluded that there was no error in the trial court's finding that termination of the mother's parental rights was in the child's best interest, as, inter alia, the child had bonded with her foster mother who wished to adopt the child and by whom the child wished to be adopted. Finally, the appellate court held that 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(b),(c), and (m) were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1162 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Luz M. (In re Janira T.)


No. 1-06-0111


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1258



December 12, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois Child Protective Division. No. 03 JA 01022. Honorable Kathleen M. Burke, Judge Presiding.
People v. Luz M. (In re Janira T.), 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 842 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 19, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, Child Protective Division terminating the mother's parental rights to her minor daughter.


OVERVIEW: The mother contended that the State failed to show that the child was abused or neglected in the prior adjudicatory hearing, which was the predicate for the termination proceeding. The appellate court agreed with the State and the public guardian that the appellate court lacked jurisdiction to review the issue because the mother failed to appeal within 30 days of the entry of the dispositional order. The mother also contended that the State failed to prove by clear and convincing evidence that the mother was an unfit parent. The appellate court disagreed, noting that there was evidence that the mother failed to complete recommended services and was inconsistent with visitation. Next, the appellate court concluded that there was no error in the trial court's finding that termination of the mother's parental rights was in the child's best interest, as, inter alia, the child had bonded with her foster mother who wished to adopt the child and by whom the child wished to be adopted. Finally, the appellate court held that 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(b),(c), and (m) were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Johnson


NO. 4-04-0460


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


368 Ill. App. 3d 1146; 859 N.E.2d 290; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1121; 307 Ill. Dec. 290



December 4, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 8, 2007.
Appeal denied by People v. Johnson, 223 Ill. 2d 656, 865 N.E.2d 973, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 639, 310 Ill. Dec. 253 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Johnson v. Illinois, 552 U.S. 897, 128 S. Ct. 216, 169 L. Ed. 2d 164, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 10053 (2007)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Johnson v. Hardy, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 53653 (C.D. Ill., June 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 02CF1373. Honorable Elizabeth A. Robb, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of two counts of attempt (first degree murder), under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/8-4, 9-1(a)(1) (2002) and home invasion under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(a)(5) (2002). The Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to two concurrent 60-year terms in prison for attempt and 85 years in prison for home invasion, and ordered the sentences be served consecutively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In upholding defendant's conviction, the appellate court concluded that there was no error in the admission of other-crimes evidence, as, inter alia, it was admissible under various exceptions including the continuing-narrative exception, the common scheme or design exception, the motive exception, and the intent exception. In addition, even if the trial court had decided not to admit such evidence during the State's case in chief, it would have been admissible to rebut defendant's alibi defense. Defendant's ineffective assistance claim also failed, as defendant failed to show that counsel's decision not to request a limiting instruction for the other-crimes evidence was not a tactical decision. Defendant also argued that the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he intended to kill the female victim. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the jury reasonably could have inferred intent from defendant's use of a deadly weapon and the character of the attack. Defendant's conviction for attempt as to the male victim and home invasion did not violate the one-act, one-crime rule as they were based on interrelated acts, not exactly the same physical act.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Gancarz


No. 2-04-0190


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


369 Ill. App. 3d 154; 859 N.E.2d 1127; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1104; 307 Ill. Dec. 450



November 30, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 19, 2007.
Appeal granted by People v. Gancarz, 223 Ill. 2d 649, 865 N.E.2d 972, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 800, 310 Ill. Dec. 252 (2007)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by People v. Gancarz, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 302 (Ill., Apr. 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 00--CF--1449. Honorable Robert J. Anderson, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Gancarz, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 579 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., June 30, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, defendant was found guilty of reckless homicide, aggravated driving under the influence (DUI), and driving with a suspended license. After noting that the reckless homicide count subsumed the DUI count, the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to a 14-year term for reckless homicide and a concurrent three-year term for driving with a suspended license. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erroneously admitted cannabis discovered in his bedroom and car because it was not relevant to the question of whether he was inebriated at the time of the accident, which occurred when defendant was driving a tractor-trailer. The appellate court agreed but found the error harmless because the evidence was cumulative of properly admitted evidence of cannabis discovered in the tractor-trailer. Next, the appellate court found that defendant's conviction for reckless homicide was amply supported by the staggering amount of THC that remained in defendant's system eight hours after the incident and defendant's decision to put other motorists in danger by driving the tractor-trailer at least 45 miles per hour into a busy intersection that displayed at best, a yellow light, and at worst, a red light. Finally, as to defendant's sentence, the appellate court concluded that defendant was prejudiced when the trial court did not admonish him of the opportunity to elect sentencing under the new, more favorable version of the reckless homicide statute because the State could not have charged defendant under the new aggravated DUI statute.


OUTCOME: The guilty findings of former reckless homicide and former aggravated DUI were affirmed. The sentence for former reckless homicide was vacated, and the cause was remanded for sentencing on the former aggravated DUI charge. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

No. 2-06-0573


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


369 Ill. App. 3d 328; 859 N.E.2d 1063; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1097; 307 Ill. Dec. 386



November 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 19, 2007.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee paternal grandmother filed a petition against appellant mother in the Circuit Court of Lee County (Illinois), for grandparent visitation pursuant to 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/607(a-5) (2005). The circuit court granted the petition, allowing the paternal grandmother unsupervised visitation, with certain restrictions. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that voluntary visits between the paternal grandmother and the child began shortly after the birth of the child. There was no indication of any problems during this period, and the mother, who never married the father of the child, sought to let a natural relationship develop. According to the maternal grandmother, things were fine until the father sought to establish his paternity. The mother then terminated the paternal grandmother's visitation. When the father was granted supervised visitation with the child, the paternal grandmother was allowed by the mother to attend with the father, but was prohibited from visiting without the father. Further, there was no error in the trial court's finding that the mother's denial of visitation was harmful to the child's mental, physical, or emotional health. Mikolajczyk v. Ford Motor Co.


No. 1-05-3133


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


369 Ill. App. 3d 78; 859 N.E.2d 201; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1057; 307 Ill. Dec. 201



November 22, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 5, 2007.
Vacated by, Appeal denied by Mikolajczyk v. Ford Motor Co., 223 Ill. 2d 638, 862 N.E.2d 1003, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 636, 308 Ill. Dec. 800 (2007)
Substituted opinion at, On reconsideration by, Remanded by Mikolajczyk v. Ford Motor Co., 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 640 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., June 13, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant motor companies appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment on a verdict in favor of plaintiff, the widow of a decedent and the administrator of the decedent's estate, in a suit alleging strict products liability for defective design. She alleged negligence against defendant, the driver of a car that struck the car in which the decedent was riding.


OVERVIEW: The decedent died when his car was hit from behind by the other driver's car. Summary judgment was entered against the other driver, and the case proceeded to a jury trial on the strict products liability claim. The jury found the other driver 60 percent responsible for causing the decedent's death and the motor companies 40 percent responsible. The jury awarded the widow $ 2 million for loss of money, goods and services and $ 25 million for loss of society. On appeal, the court held that the jury was properly instructed on consumer expectations law as it related to strict products liability. Further, the trial court did not err in denying the companies' suggested instructions regarding the risk-utility test when it allowed testimony about the risks and benefits of the vehicle's seat, which had collapsed on impact. Illinois courts allowed evidence of the risks and benefits of an allegedly defective product as evidence that it did not conform with consumer expectations. However, the court held that remittitur of the award for loss of society was appropriate under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 366(a)(5) because the award was arbitrary and excessive.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the award for loss of society and remanded that portion of the judgment for a determination of the appropriate amount of remittitur. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment.

Townsend v. Sears, Roebuck & Co.


No. 1-05-4045


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


368 Ill. App. 3d 902; 858 N.E.2d 552; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1005; 306 Ill. Dec. 755; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P17,645



November 8, 2006, Decided  
November 8, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 18, 2006.
Appeal granted by Townsend v. Sears, Roebuck and Co., 223 Ill. 2d 686, 865 N.E.2d 978, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 628, 310 Ill. Dec. 258 (2007)
Vacated by, Cause remanded by Townsend v. Sears, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1701 (Ill., Nov. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the circuit court of Cook County. No. 03 L 3520.Honorable Jennifer Duncan-Brice, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother, individually and on behalf of her minor son, filed a products liability action against defendant, a designer-manufacturer of lawn tractors that had its principal place of business and corporate headquarters in Illinois. Pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 308, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) certified a question for interlocutory appeal on a choice-of-law issue. The designer appealed on the certified question.


OVERVIEW: The mother alleged that her son was injured when his father backed over him with the lawn tractor. The family resided in Michigan, and the lawn tractor was purchased there. However, the design decision not to incorporate a "no-mow-in reverse" safety feature into the lawn tractor was made by the designer in Illinois. The question was whether Illinois or Michigan law applied to the case. Applying the "most significant relationship" test, the court ruled that Illinois law governed the issues of both liability and damages. Illinois law applied because 1) Illinois had a strong interest in applying its products liability law to regulate culpable conduct that occurred within its borders and to induce the design of safer products; 2) Illinois, as the designer's principal place of business and place where the alleged corporate misconduct occurred, had the most significant relationship to the issue of punitive damages; and 3) Illinois' public policy position that noneconomic damages could not be capped was a compelling interest that outweighed any interest Michigan might have on the issue of noneconomic damages, and thus, Illinois law also applied to the issue of compensatory damages.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question.

 

1168 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Sun Life Assur. Co. of Can. v. Manna


No. 1-05-1323


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


368 Ill. App. 3d 591; 858 N.E.2d 503; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 996; 306 Ill. Dec. 706



November 1, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 18, 2006.
Appeal granted by Sun Life Assur. Co. v. Manna, 223 Ill. 2d 686, 865 N.E.2d 978, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 498, 310 Ill. Dec. 258 (2007)
Affirmed by Sun Life Assur. Co. v. Manna, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1699 (Ill., Nov. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Anthony L. Young, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a Canadian life insurance company, filed a declaratory judgment action against defendants, the Director of Insurance and the Illinois Department of Financial and Professional Regulation, in which it challenged the constitutionality of 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/444(1) (2004). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted summary judgment to defendants and denied the company's motion for summary judgment. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The statute imposed a retaliatory tax on alien insurance companies. The court first held that the tax was valid under the Uniformity Clause, Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2. It had a legitimate purpose of promoting domestic industry by deterring other countries from enacting discriminatory or excessive taxes, and because the impact of the tax on foreign affairs was incidental, its imposition was not an unconstitutional intrusion into foreign affairs. Because the Uniformity Clause offered more stringent protection than the Federal Equal Protection Clause or Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, the tax did not violate equal protection either. The tax did not violate the Foreign Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. The United States Supreme Court had stated that the McCarran-Ferguson Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 1011 et seq., removed all Commerce Clause restrictions on a state's taxation of insurance. Even if the Act did not remove Foreign Commerce Clause restrictions from state taxation of alien insurers, the retaliatory tax was not discriminatory given its legitimate state purpose, and its impact on the federal government's ability to speak with one voice regarding foreign commerce was negligible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

People v. Stanley

Appeal denied by People v. Stanley, 223 Ill. 2d 674, 865 N.E.2d 976, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 792, 310 Ill. Dec. 256 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Stanley v. Ill., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 9812 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No.03 CR 28424. The Honorable Marcia B. Orr, Judge Presiding.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after it found defendant guilty of three counts of attempted aggravated criminal sexual assault and one count of aggravated unlawful restraint. He was then sentenced and assessed fines. Due to his attempted aggravated unlawful sexual assault conviction, he was informed that he would have to register as a "sexual predator" for the rest of his life. He appealed.

1170 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Brandon v. Bonell


No. 2-05-0802


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


368 Ill. App. 3d 492; 858 N.E.2d 465; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 963; 306 Ill. Dec. 668



October 23, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 15, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lee County. No. 99--L--42. Honorable David T. Fritts, Judge, Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmates filed an action against defendant Department of Corrections (DOC) employees after plaintiffs were injured while working in the prison kitchen. The Circuit Court of Lee County (Illinois), holding that sovereign immunity applied, dismissed the complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court stated that under 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/8(d) (2004), if defendants had sovereign immunity, exclusive jurisdiction rested in the Court of Claims. 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-7-3(a) (1996) imposed a duty of safety solely on the DOC, and thus any duty it imposed on DOC employees arose solely by virtue of their employment. Thus, the trial court properly found that the duty defendants allegedly breached arose solely from their employment. Because plaintiffs had not alleged any facts showing that defendants breached a duty to plaintiffs that arose independently of defendants' state employment, the action was considered one against the State; thus, the claims were barred by the State Lawsuit Immunity Act, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1 (2004). Next, even if the trial court had erred in failing to address plaintiffs' motion to amend, the error was harmless because the amended complaint would have also been barred by sovereign immunity. Defendants, as supervisors, not employers, did not have a duty to plaintiffs under the Health and Safety Act, 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 225/2 and 225/3 (2004), that was independent of their employment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

People v. Griffin


No. 1-04-2580


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


368 Ill. App. 3d 369; 857 N.E.2d 889; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 954; 306 Ill. Dec. 490



October 19, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 8, 2006.
Appeal denied by People v. Griffin, 222 Ill. 2d 614, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 332 (Ill., Jan. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Illinois No. 02 CR 11110 (01). Honorable Michael P. Toomin, Judge Presiding.
People v. Griffin, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 805 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 7, 2006)



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons, we affirm the decision of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of three counts of first degree murder based on an accountability theory (720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(a)(3), 5-2 (2004)). He was sentenced to natural life imprisonment on each count, with all counts running concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court found that the trial court's response to a question from the jury was a direct answer to the question posed. The trial court simply related the law of felony murder, residential burglary, and accountability. Furthermore, it did not apply that law to the evidence or instruct the jury on how to do so. It remained the jury's task to apply that law to the evidence and to determine defendant's guilt. Two comments made by the prosecutor during closing arguments did not deny defendant a fair trial. One reasonable interpretation of the prosecution's comment on reliability was that he was drawing an inference on the trial court's reason for admitting the statement, i.e., that it was reliable. It did not necessarily follow that the trial court found that the statement was reliable. In addition, when the second comment was placed in context, it was clear that the prosecutor was not suggesting that the trial court already deemed the statement proper. Even if there were an error, it would be harmless as the jury was instructed that closing arguments should be confined to the evidence and reasonable inferences to be drawn therefrom and that closing arguments were not evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1172 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Clifton R. (In re Clifton R.)


No. 1-05-2705


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


368 Ill. App. 3d 438; 857 N.E.2d 843; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 936; 306 Ill. Dec. 444



October 13, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 8, 2006.
Appeal denied by People v. Clifton R. (In re Clifton R.), 2008 Ill. LEXIS 701 (Ill., Mar. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Noreen Daly, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, a juvenile, appealed the portion of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) requiring respondent to submit buccal swab saliva specimens for genetic analysis under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2004) after respondent was found to be a juvenile delinquent based upon a finding that he committed the offense of possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Respondent argued that because he was a juvenile, the compulsory extraction of his saliva and perpetual storing of his DNA profile pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2004) violated his constitutional right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures. In an adult criminal proceeding, the state high court found that § 5-4-3 was facially constitutional. Although respondent asked the appellate court not to follow the high court case because he claimed it was wrongly decided, the appellate court declined, as it was bound to follow state high court decisions. The state high court also found that § 5-4-3 was constitutional as applied to juveniles. Respondent asked the appellate court to distinguish that holding on the ground that respondent did not commit a sexual offense. The high court held, however, that a defendant's status as a nonsexual offender did not so attenuate the vital linkage between his reduced privacy interests and the State's strong interest in deterring and solving crime. Thus, the trial court did not err in applying § 5-4-3 to respondent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Johnson v. Ill. Dep't of Corr.


NO. 4-05-0678


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sangamon County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that granted the motion to dismiss that defendants, the state corrections department, its director, and the state prisoner review board filed and which was directed against the complaint plaintiff inmate filed seeking the restoration of good-conduct credits, an award of meritorious good-conduct credits, and his immediate release from custody. He appealed.

On appeal, the appellate court found that the inmate had not shown entitlement to relief because he had not exhausted his administrative remedies, he had not shown an entitlement to immediate release, and the state corrections department was permitted to calculate his good-time credits in the way it did.

Sieron & Assocs. v. Dep't of Ins.


NO. 5-04-0571


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


368 Ill. App. 3d 181; 857 N.E.2d 805; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 939; 306 Ill. Dec. 406



September 28, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 12, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 03-MR-193. Honorable Richard A. Aguirre, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged the non-renewals of their insurance policies by appellee Illinois FAIR Plan Association to appellee, the Illinois Director of Insurance, who, after an administrative hearing, affirmed the FAIR Plan Association's nonrenewal of the policies. The owners then filed an administrative review action in the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois). The circuit court affirmed the order. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The FAIR Plan Association decided not to renew any of the owners' insurance policies because the owners' properties had an unusually high loss ratio. The owners argued that the Association's decision not to renew their insurance policies violated the Illinois FAIR Plan, 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/522 et seq. (2004). On appeal, the court found that (1) 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/524 (2004) did not apply because there were no conclusions of property inspectors at issue, and 5/524 said nothing about the renewal or nonrenewal of existing FAIR Plan policies; (2) the Association's decision not to renew the owners' policies complied with 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/525 (2004) and the approved underwriting standards; and (3) there was no deprivation of due process in either the notice of nonrenewal under 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/143.17(a) (2004), or in the appeal to the Director of Insurance under 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/143.23 (2004). However, the court clarified that if any contract buyer had any insurable interest in the owners' property, the buyer could not be denied FAIR Plan insurance coverage on the property upon reapplication simply because of the owners' claims history.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Carpenter


No. 1-05-0464


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


368 Ill. App. 3d 288; 856 N.E.2d 551; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 877; 305 Ill. Dec. 746



September 26, 2006, Decided  
September 26, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 20, 2006.
Appeal granted by People v. Carpenter, 222 Ill. 2d 611, 862 N.E.2d 235, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 391, 308 Ill. Dec. 637 (2007)
Affirmed by People v. Carpenter, 228 Ill. 2d 250, 888 N.E.2d 105, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 314, 320 Ill. Dec. 888 (Ill., Apr. 17, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of having a false or secret compartment in a motor vehicle under § 12-612 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, codified at 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-612 (2004), and sentenced to two years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-612 (2004) was unconstitutionally vague and that it swept too broadly and punished innocent conduct. The appellate court held that § 12-612 was not so vague that it violated due process of law under the facts of the case. However, the appellate court agreed with defendant that the statute required no criminal mental state and potentially punished innocent conduct. The appellate court noted that the statute was not violated unless a defendant intended and designed a compartment to conceal, hide, and prevent discovery of it or its contents by law enforcement officers. The statute did not require that contraband or the fruits or tools of crime be found in the compartment. The appellate court disagreed with the State that the plain language of the statute did not criminalize the concealment of legally possessed items in the compartment. Applying the rational basis test, the appellate court concluded that 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-612 (2004) violated the due process provisions of the United States and Illinois Constitutions.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed.

Hill v. PS Ill. Trust


No. 1-05-4000


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


368 Ill. App. 3d 310; 856 N.E.2d 560; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 876; 305 Ill. Dec. 755

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As corrected October 3, 2006. Released for Publication November 20, 2006.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) dismissed two counts of plaintiff customer's complaint against defendant storage facility after it sold the customer's property stored with it because of overdue rent payments. Count one alleged that the statutory storage facility act permitting the sale violated the state constitution's due process clause, and count two alleged violation of the state statutory consumer fraud act. The customer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The customer entered into a contract with the storage facility for the rental of a storage locker in order to store his personal property. He made his monthly payments for the first two months. He was unable to make the rental payments for the next two months. Thereafter, he called the storage facility and was told his belongings had been auctioned off. According to him, he never received notice of the auctioning off of his property in order to enforce the lien created under 770 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 95/3 (2004). He demanded the return of any balance remaining from the lien sale and received no response. He filed a complaint alleging the state storage act statute violated his state constitutional due process rights because it did not provide him adequate lien sale notice and that the storage facility's conduct violated the state's statutory consumer fraud act, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 505/2 (2004). Both claims were dismissed. On appeal, the appellate court found that dismissal of the due process contention was proper as the customer had not alleged the involvement of a state actor but also found that a violation of the state's statutory consumer fraud act had been adequately pled.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment dismissing the customer's state due process claim was affirmed. However, the trial court's judgment dismissing the customer's statutory consumer fraud act claim was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Galan


No. 1-04-2612


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


367 Ill. App. 3d 876; 856 N.E.2d 511; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 868; 305 Ill. Dec. 706



September 22, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 20, 2006.
Rehearing denied by People v. Galan, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1064 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Nov. 3, 2006)
Discretionary appeal allowed by People v. Galan, 222 Ill. 2d 613, 862 N.E.2d 236, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 207, 308 Ill. Dec. 638 (2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by People v. Galan, 229 Ill. 2d 484, 893 N.E.2d 597, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 639, 323 Ill. Dec. 325 (Ill., July 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 27205. Honorable Fred G. Suria, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted and charged in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), with both possession with intent to deliver more than 900 grams of cocaine and possession with intent to deliver more than 5,000 grams of cannabis. The circuit court, upon reconsideration, quashed defendant's arrest and suppressed the evidence obtained contemporaneous with and subsequent to defendant's unlawful arrest. The People of the State of Illinois appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parties agreed that, in compliance with Ind. Code Ann. § 35-33-3-1 (1998) of Indiana's fresh pursuit statute, the Chicago police were properly in fresh pursuit of defendant, whom the Chicago police believed had committed a felony in the State of Illinois. However, defendant contended that his arrest was unlawful in that the arrest occurred in the State of Indiana and the Chicago police officers who arrested defendant disregarded Ind. Code Ann. § 35-33-3-2 (1998), the portion of Indiana's fresh pursuit statute that required out-of-state police officers who effected an arrest inside the State of Indiana to bring the person arrested before an Indiana judge for a hearing regarding the lawfulness of the arrest. On appeal, the court found that the arrest was unlawful because the Chicago police officers acted in the absence of appropriate statutory authority when they disregarded Indiana's statutory directive that they present defendant to an Indiana judge for review of the lawfulness of the arrest in Indiana. In addition, the application of the exclusionary rule was necessary in that a contrary interpretation would have rendered empty the mandate of the Indiana fresh pursuit statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Woodard


No. 1-04-1981


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


367 Ill. App. 3d 304; 854 N.E.2d 674; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 846; 305 Ill. Dec. 82



September 20, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 5, 2006.
Appeal denied by People v. Woodard, 222 Ill. 2d 598, 861 N.E.2d 663, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 2089, 308 Ill. Dec. 332 (2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied United States ex rel. Porter v. Rednour, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 103391 (N.D. Ill., July 25, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 373. Honorable Dennis A. Dernbach, Judge Presiding.
People v. Woodard, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 671 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Aug. 3, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and solicitation to commit murder. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to consecutive terms of 45 years and 20 years in prison, and required defendant to register as a sex offender pursuant to the Sex Offender Registration Act and the Sex Offender and Child Murderer Community Notification Law. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that counsel was ineffective for failing to file a motion to suppress defendant's inculpatory statements to police. The appellate court disagreed, finding that defendant's statements were voluntary. The appellate court further noted that defendant's changing stories and dead-end leads only perpetuated her detention, as they necessitated further investigation. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury on second-degree murder because the evidence supported a finding that defendant's actions were the result of provocation. The appellate court disagreed, concluding that the 17 days that elapsed between the injury suffered by defendant at the hands of one of the persons defendant sought to murder was more than enough time for the voice of reason and humanity to be heard. The appellate court also upheld the solicitation conviction, noting that the intended victims of the solicitation differed from the actual murder victim. Finally, the appellate court upheld the sentence imposed for murder, after concluding that the trial judge considered the necessary factors, including defendant's lack of criminal history and lack of remorse.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Luz M. (In re Janira T.)


No. 1-06-0111


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.

Rehearing denied by In re J.T., 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1195 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 11, 2006)
Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Luz M. (In re Janira T.), 368 Ill. App. 3d 883, 859 N.E.2d 1046, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1138, 307 Ill. Dec. 369 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 12, 2006)
Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Luz M. (In re Janira T.), 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1258 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 12, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois Child Protective Division. No. 03 JA 01022. Honorable Kathleen M. Burke, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois Child Protective Division terminating the mother's parental rights to her minor daughter.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the trial court erred in finding the mother unfit because the State failed to provide sufficient evidence showing that the child was abused or neglected in the adjudicatory hearing which was the predicate for the termination proceeding. The appellate court lacked jurisdiction over the appeal from the adjudicatory order because the mother failed to file a notice of appeal. The mother also argued that the State failed to prove by clear and convincing evidence that the mother was an unfit parent. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the evidence showed, inter alia, that the mother did not complete any of the recommended services and did not visit the child in foster care on a regular basis. As for the mother's contention that the trial court erred in finding that the termination of the mother's parental rights was in the child's best interests, the appellate court noted that the child was in stable, appropriate, safe home, and had bonded with the foster mother, who wished to adopt the child. Finally, the appellate court concluded that 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(b), (D)(c), (D)(m) (2002), were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Griffin


No. 1-04-2580


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 805



September 7, 2006, Decided  
September 7, 2006, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by People v. Griffin, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 949 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Oct. 17, 2006)
Subsequent opinion on rehearing at People v. Griffin, 368 Ill. App. 3d 369, 857 N.E.2d 889, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 954, 306 Ill. Dec. 490 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Oct. 19, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 02 CR 11110 (01). Honorable Michael P. Toomin, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of three counts of first degree murder based on an accountability theory in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. An.. 5/9-1(a)(3), 5-2 (2004). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to natural life imprisonment on each count, with all counts running concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was denied his constitutional right to an impartial jury and fair trial when the trial judge improperly applied the law to the facts and essentially directed the jury to find defendant guilty. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the trial court's response was a direct answer to the question posed; the trial court did not apply the law to the evidence or instruct the jury on how to do so. Defendant also contended that two comments made by the prosecutor during closing arguments denied defendant a fair trial. Under the plain error test, the appellate court concluded that the alleged errors were not of such a magnitude that defendant was denied a fair and impartial trial. Among other things, the appellate court found the comments to be a fair response to several of defense counsel's remarks. Finally, defendant argued that the multiple-murder sentencing statute, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii) (2004), violated the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. The appellate court held that the sentence imposed was not disproportionate as, contrary to defendant's contention, he was not a passive participant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

McKee v. Bd. of Trs.


NO. 4-05-0943


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


367 Ill. App. 3d 538; 855 N.E.2d 571; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 822; 305 Ill. Dec. 404



September 7, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 24, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 03MR392. Honorable John R. Kennedy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Champaign County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that affirmed defendant city police pension board's decision that denied plaintiff claimant's application for disability benefits. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant, a police officer, and other officers attempted to place a combative suspect in a squad car. The next morning, he woke up with severe back pain. A few weeks later, he saw a doctor and underwent magnetic resonance imaging (MRI), which indicated a bulging disc and a nerve root problem. He applied for disability benefits. Eventually, a total of five physicians were selected, pursuant to 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-115 (1998), to determine whether he was disabled. Two physicians stated he was not disabled. Two others said he was disabled, but the injury was not severe. The city police pension board then denied his disability benefits application. On appeal, the trial court affirmed. On further review, the appellate court found that the city police pension board's decision was not against the manifest weight of the evidence, that the fact that three board-selected physicians may have indicated that he was disabled was not dispositive of the disability question pursuant to 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-115 (1998) since that statute allowed an administrative board to consider other evidence of disability, and that the physicians' certificates only told part of the story.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Felzak v. Hruby


No. 2-05-0848


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


367 Ill. App. 3d 695; 855 N.E.2d 202; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 812; 305 Ill. Dec. 311



September 5, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 10, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Felzak v. Hruby, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 957 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Oct. 10, 2006)
Appeal granted by Felzak v. Hruby, 222 Ill. 2d 606, 862 N.E.2d 233, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 372, 308 Ill. Dec. 635 (2007)
Vacated by, Remanded by Felzak v. Hruby, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1158 (Ill., Sept. 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 94-D-860. Honorable C. Stanley Austin, Judge, Presiding.
Felzak v. Hruby, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 665 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., July 28, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The DuPage County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered judgments that denied defendant parents' motion to dismiss plaintiff grandparent's petition to enforce an order that allowed the grandparent visitation with one of her granddaughters and held the parents in indirect civil contempt for not obeying that order. Part of the judgment also ordered them not to discuss the case with their daughter, who was the granddaughter. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: One of the parents was married to another person; those two people had three children. The other person then died. The remaining parent remarried. The children were then adopted by the new parent. Shortly thereafter, the deceased parent's mother, the grandparent, petitioned for grandparent visitation under 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/607(b) (1992). The parties entered into an agreed visitation order; visitation then occurred for the next decade. Visitation was then allegedly stopped. The grandparent petitioned to enforce the order. The parents moved to dismiss since the statute had been found unconstitutional; the trial court soon held them in civil contempt for not allowing visitation. The trial court also forbid the parents from discussing the case with the daughter. On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court did not lack subject matter jurisdiction over the case because the visitation was based on the order entered, not the statute, the parents could be found in contempt because the order was not void, and that part of the order forbidding them from discussing the case with the daughter violated their Fourteenth Amendment parental liberty interest rights.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment denying the parents' motion to dismiss and entering its judgment holding the parents in contempt was affirmed. However, its judgment directing the parents not to communicate with their daughter about the outcome of the case was vacated.

People v. Scott


No. 1-04-3295


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


367 Ill. App. 3d 283; 854 N.E.2d 795; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 782; 305 Ill. Dec. 203



August 30, 2006, Decided  
August 30, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 5, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 04 CR 529. Honorable Rickey Jones, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting defendant of possession of a controlled substance in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/402(a)(2)(A) (2002) and sentencing defendant to five years in prison.


OVERVIEW: The police officer twice saw the codefendant open a mailbox with a key, remove a golf-ball sized bag of cocaine, and hand it to defendant. After the second time and while defendant and the codefendant were in a nearby building, the officer approached the mailbox. Defendant and the codefendant exited the building and went to the mailbox. When defendant saw the officer approaching, he handed a golf-ball sized bag of cocaine to the codefendant, who placed it in the mailbox and walked away, leaving the key in the mailbox. The officer found two bags of cocaine in the mailbox, a golf-ball sized bag containing approximately 10 grams, and a larger one containing approximately 36 grams. The State failed to show that defendant had the capability to maintain control and dominion over the larger bag of cocaine found in the mailbox. Defendant never possessed or had access to the key needed to open the mailbox where the larger bag was found. Defendant conceded that he possessed the smaller bag of cocaine. Thus, the appellate court found that he was guilty of a lesser-included offense of possession of cocaine under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/402(c) (2002).


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed as modified to a lesser included offense. The case was remanded for resentencing on the lesser included offense.
