People v. Turner


No. 2-06-0060


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


367 Ill. App. 3d 490; 854 N.E.2d 1139; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 740; 305 Ill. Dec. 229



August 22, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 13, 2006.
Post-conviction proceeding at People v. Turner, 231 Ill. 2d 684, 904 N.E.2d 985, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 833, 328 Ill. Dec. 475 (2009)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Turner, 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 499, 2012 IL App (2d) 100819 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 05--CF--3717. Honorable Victoria A. Rossetti, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted on three counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse and was in jail awaiting trial when the State obtained a search warrant to photograph defendant's penis. The State appealed after the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) entered an order that barred the State from presenting evidence of the photographs or testimony from those individuals involved in taking the photographs.


OVERVIEW: The warrant had not been obtained from the presiding judge, and defense counsel was neither informed of the warrant nor present during the photographing session. The presiding judge barred the evidence as a sanction for violating Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 413(b). The presiding judge thereafter denied the State's Rule 413 motion for photos. The court affirmed, holding first that it had jurisdiction to consider the appeal under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(a)(1). Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 413 rather than 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/108-4 (2004) governed the obtaining of the photographs. The State violated Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 413 by not providing notice to defense counsel. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in suppressing the evidence as a sanction for the discovery misconduct. Not all evidence regarding defendant's alleged circumcision had been excluded, and presentation of the excluded evidence would not provide meaningful corroboration for the victim's underlying claims. Finally, the State's contention that the trial court erred in denying its subsequent Rule 413 motion was not a matter that could be reviewed as the denial did not result in a suppression of evidence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Russell v. Blagojevich


NO. 4-05-0765


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


367 Ill. App. 3d 530; 853 N.E.2d 920; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 710; 304 Ill. Dec. 843



August 9, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 13, 2006.
Appeal denied by Russell v. Blagojevich, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1921 (Ill., Nov. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 04MR514. Honorable John W. Belz, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sangamon County Circuit Court (Illinois) dismissed plaintiff former state's attorney's petition for a writ of mandamus that he filed in an attempt to obtain a cost-of-living adjustment and back salary he believed he had been improperly denied while working as a state's attorney, based on a public law that was passed to prevent state officials from receiving cost of living increases. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The former state's attorney filed a petition for writ of mandamus against defendants, a governor, a revenue director, an economic development director, and a comptroller to obtain a cost-of-living adjustment and back salary that he believed he had been denied as the result of the passage of a public act aimed at preventing state officials from obtaining cost of living increases. The public act had been enacted while he was working as a state's attorney. The petition was filed because he had requested that various officials see to it that he get the amount he believed he was entitled to and they had either not responded or had informed him that they were not authorized to pay to him the requested amount. The trial court dismissed the petition and found that even though the state supreme court had found the public act unconstitutional in Jorgensen, the unconstitutional part pertained only to judicial salaries, which could not be diminished due to Ill. Const. VI, § 14. On appeal, the appellate court found that Ill. Const. art. VI, § 19, regarding state's attorneys, did not contain a similar provision and, thus, the public act used to deny his COLA was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Woodard


No. 1-04-1981


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 671



August 3, 2006, Decided  
August 3, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1]
Rehearing denied by People v. Woodward, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 916 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 15, 2006)
Substituted opinion at, Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Woodard, 367 Ill. App. 3d 304, 854 N.E.2d 674, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 846, 305 Ill. Dec. 82 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 373. Honorable Dennis A. Dernbach, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and solicitation to commit murder. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to consecutive terms of 45 years and 20 years in prison and ordered defendant to register as a sex offender pursuant to the Sex Offender Registration Act and the Sex Offender and Child Murderer Community Notification Law. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held, inter alia, that defense counsel was not ineffective for failing to file a motion to suppress defendant's inculpatory statement to police because the statement was voluntary; defendant did not suffer any mental or physical affliction, was informed of her Miranda rights, and was provided with food, drink, and the use of a restroom. The appellate court also concluded that defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on second degree murder where there was no evidence of provocation. Next, the appellate court upheld defendant's conviction for solicitation, noting that it was based on defendant's orchestration of the death of a victim separate from the victim murdered and thus, was not supported by the same evidence as defendant's murder conviction. The trial court was not remiss in failing to sua sponte conduct an inquiry into defendant's fitness to stand trial as there was no evidence defendant was anything other than interested, rational, and appropriate. Defendant's sentence, within the statutory guidelines, was upheld. Finally, the appellate court concluded that there was no error in the order requiring defendant to register as a sex offender.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Faircloth v. Sternes


No. 2-05-0736


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


367 Ill. App. 3d 123; 853 N.E.2d 878; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 666; 304 Ill. Dec. 801



August 1, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 15, 2006.
Appeal denied by Faircloth v. Sternes, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 340 (Ill., Jan. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lee County. No. 03-MR-17. Honorable David T. Fritts, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Faircloth, 234 Ill. App. 3d 386, 599 N.E.2d 1356, 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1477, 175 Ill. Dec. 342 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lee County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that denied defendant's petition for habeas corpus relief in a case where he was convicted of, inter alia, drug-induced homicide for giving the victim cocaine, the adverse effects of which caused her death. Defendant appealed the denial of his petition for habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted of, inter alia, drug-induced homicide, now 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3.3(a) (2004) after defendant gave the victim cocaine and she died from the cocaine's adverse effects on her. Defendant was sentenced to 30 years in prison for the drug-induced homicide. The appellate court also found that defendant's 30-year prison sentence was not disproportionate to the seriousness of the offense, which involved the death of a person.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

In re Marriage of Gambla


No. 2-05-0971


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


367 Ill. App. 3d 441; 853 N.E.2d 847; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 667; 304 Ill. Dec. 770



July 31, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 15, 2006.
Appeal denied by Gambla v. Woodson, 222 Ill. 2d 571, 861 N.E.2d 654, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1920, 308 Ill. Dec. 323 (2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gambla v. Woodson, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 10286 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 03-D-1116. Honorable C. Stanley Austin, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner husband appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) dissolving his marriage to respondent wife.


OVERVIEW: The father was Caucasian while the mother was African-American. They had a child in 2002. In deciding the issue of custody, the trial court considered the factors enumerated in 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/602(a) (2004). The trial court found that the child had a close relationship with both parents. The child had no difficulty in either her father's home or her mother's home. Neither parent suffered from mental or physical maladies that would have precluded them from parenting the child. Based on the § 602(a) factors, the trial court found that the father and the mother were equally qualified to care for the child. Because the parties were equal on these factors, the trial court looked to other relevant factors. One factor was that the child was African-American and Caucasian and that, as an African-American woman, the mother was able to provide the child with the support she would need in a world that was potentially hostile to biracial individuals. This factor tipped the scales slightly in favor of the mother. It was permissible for race to be considered as long as it was not the sole factor. The trial court carefully weighed the eight statutory factors along with race.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1189 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Felzak v. Hruby


No. 2-05-0848


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 665



July 28, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Substituted opinion at Felzak v. Hruby, 367 Ill. App. 3d 695, 855 N.E.2d 202, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 812, 305 Ill. Dec. 311 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Sept. 5, 2006)
Opinion withdrawn by Felzak v. Hruby, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 847 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Sept. 5, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 94-D-860. Honorable C. Stanley Austin, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a biological father and a stepmother (parents), challenged an August 22, 2005, order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) holding them in indirect civil contempt of court for failing to obey a June 15, 1995, order providing for grandparent visitation and from a June 8, 2005, order denying their motion to dismiss plaintiff maternal grandmother's petition to enforce the June 15, 1995, order.


OVERVIEW: The grandmother filed a petition for grandparent visitation with the parents' children pursuant to § 607(b) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/607(b) (1992). The parents claimed the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because § 607(b) was held unconstitutional. The appeals court found that because the provisions of § 607(b) allowing for grandparent visitation were inoperative, they conferred no subject matter jurisdiction to hear the grandmother's petition. However, despite invoking § 607(b), her petition framed a case for grandparent visitation, and because the court had subject matter jurisdiction over cases concerning grandparent visitation pursuant to the common law, the court had subject matter jurisdiction over the grandmother's petition. Because the grandmother had a legal right to pursue her contract claims and asserted this right in good faith, the forbearance of her claims under a previous agreement provided valid consideration for the parties' June 15, 1995, agreement. Because the June 15, 1995, agreed order was not void for lack of subject matter jurisdiction or lack of consideration, it remained in effect.


OUTCOME: The trial court did not err when it entered its June 8, 2005, order denying the parents' motion to dismiss or when it entered its August 22, 2005, order holding them in contempt. The June 15, 1995, order was not void. The portion of the August 22, 2005, order directing the parents not to communicate with their daughter about the outcome of the case was vacated.

 

1190 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. McAfee


No. 3-05-0003


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


366 Ill. App. 3d 726; 853 N.E.2d 107; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 647; 304 Ill. Dec. 575



July 27, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 28, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. No. 04-CF-220. Honorable Richard Schoendstedt, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County (Illinois), of unlawful possession of a controlled substance. Pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2004), defendant was required to submit a DNA sample. Pursuant to § 5-4-3(j), he was also required to a $ 200 genetic marker analysis fee. A $ 10 DNA collection fee was also imposed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the compulsory extraction of his blood and the storing of his DNA profile violated his right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures, that the trial court lacked authority to impose the DNA collection fee, and that he was entitled to a $20 credit against his fine. The court affirmed in part. Defendant's constitutional argument was rejected based on a prior state supreme court holding that § 5-4-3 did not violate the fourth amendment. The court agreed, however, that the trial court lacked authority to impose the collection fee. The fee was not authorized under § 5-4-3. It was also not a "fine" or "court cost" that could be imposed as a condition of probation under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-6-3(b)(2) (2004) because, while it was not unreasonable, the fee did not relate to defendant's offense or to his rehabilitation. Defendant was already required to pay the analysis fee and a portion of that fee was allocated to the circuit court clerk to offset administrative cost. Finally, as the State conceded the point, defendant was entitled to a $20 credit toward his street value fine.


OUTCOME: The court rejected defendant's constitutional challenge and affirmed the DNA order. The court vacated the DNA collection fee imposed by the trial court. The case was remanded for entry of a $20 credit toward defendant's fined.

Barbara's Sales, Inc. v. Intel Corp.


NO. 5-05-0078


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


367 Ill. App. 3d 1013; 857 N.E.2d 717; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 650; 306 Ill. Dec. 318



July 25, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal granted by Barbara's Sales, Inc. v. Intel Corp., 222 Ill. 2d 567, 861 N.E.2d 653, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1683, 308 Ill. Dec. 322 (2006)
Reversed by, Cause remanded by Barbara's Sales, Inc. v. Intel Corp., 227 Ill. 2d 45, 879 N.E.2d 910, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 1698, 316 Ill. Dec. 522 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 02-L-788. Honorable Ralph J. Mendelsohn, Judge, presiding.
Paul v. Intel Corp. (In re Intel Corp.), 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 36716 (D. Del., May 22, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered; order vacated; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purchasers and defendant manufacturer appealed an order by the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois); questions were certified as to whether the circuit court erred in certifying a class of Illinois consumers under Illinois law rather than certifying a nationwide or Illinois class under California law, and whether it erred in holding that the action should not proceed as a nationwide class action.


OVERVIEW: The purchasers, residents of Illinois and Missouri, alleged that the manufacturer, a California corporation, engaged in unfair business practices through the omission, suppression, and concealment from the public of the material fact that its microprocessor did not perform to the expectations of a reasonable consumer. The circuit court determined, inter alia, that Illinois did not have a legitimate interest in applying California law to adjudicate the dispute because California did not have the most significant relationship with the action. The circuit court denied class certification for the counts that were based upon California statutes. The appellate court found that the injury to the purchasers occurred throughout the country by virtue of the nationwide sales of computers containing the manufacturer's microprocessors. California was clearly the only state where conduct relevant to all the potential class members occurred. The circuit court erred by not first considering which state had the most significant relationship to the occurrence.


OUTCOME: The certified questions were answered; the order was vacated regarding class certification, and the matter was remanded with directions for the circuit court to apply California substantive law and to reconsider its class certification order in light of the applicability of California law.

Emerald Casino, Inc. v. Ill. Gaming Bd.


No. 1-05-3142


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


366 Ill. App. 3d 622; 852 N.E.2d 512; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 569; 304 Ill. Dec. 262



June 30, 2006, Decided  
June 30, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 27, 2006. Released for Publication August 17, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Hon. Thomas P. Quinn, Judge Presiding.
Emerald Casino, Inc. v. Ill. Gaming Bd., 366 Ill. App. 3d 113, 851 N.E.2d 843, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 503, 303 Ill. Dec. 656 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Illinois Gaming Board filed a disciplinary action against plaintiff casino. An administrative law judge upheld the constitutionality of the Board's administrative rules. The casino's complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief against the Board challenging certain of the Board's rules was dismissed by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). The casino's motion for a preliminary injunction was denied. The casino appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the appeal was pending, the Board revoked the casino's license. The casino appealed the Board's decision in the Illinois Appellate Court, Fourth District. The appellate court held that the casino sought review of a "final order of the Board" as that term was used in § 17.1(a) (230 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 10/17.1(a) (2004)) of the Illinois Riverboat Gambling Act (RGA), 230 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 10/1 et seq. (1992). The petition in the Fourth District was a global attack on the revocation order, claiming due process violations and challenging certain administrative rules. The casino made the same facial attack on the Board's rules in the appeal. There was no reason that the issues raised in the appeal could not be resolved by the Fourth District. The cases cited by the casino did not support its claim that it could attack the Board's rules in the appeal while it was pursuing the same arguments in the Fourth District. The Fourth District was the proper place for the casino to pursue its broad-scale attack on the Board's order. The RGA created the only permissible avenue for the attack on the revocation order and authorized jurisdiction and venue only in the Fourth District.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

1193 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gancarz


No. 2-04-0190


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 579



June 30, 2006, Decided  
June 30, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Corrected by, Superseded by People v. Gancarz, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 1104 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Nov. 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 00--CF--1449. Honorable Robert J. Anderson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, defendant was found guilty of reckless homicide, aggravated driving under the influence (DUI), and driving with a suspended license. The reckless homicide count subsumed the aggravated DUI count, and the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to a 14-year prison term for reckless homicide and a concurrent three-year term for driving with a suspended license. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erroneously admitted cannabis discoveries into evidence because they were irrelevant and prejudicial. The appellate court agreed that the evidence as more prejudicial than probative to the central issue of defendant's impairment at the time of the accident but concluded that the error was harmless because defendant was not unfairly prejudiced by the admission of the evidence. Defendant also argued that he was not proved guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of reckless homicide. The appellate court disagreed, concluding that any rational trier of fact could have found defendant reckless beyond a reasonable doubt. The finding of recklessness was amply supported by, inter alia, the scientific evidence of the staggering amount of THC that remained in defendant's system eight hours after the incident. Finally, the appellate court agreed that the trial court violated defendant's right to due process by failing to advise him of the option of receiving a sentence under a newer, more favorable version of the reckless homicide statute. Remand for sentencing on the aggravated DUI conviction was permissible even though it was unsentenced and unappealed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for former reckless homicide and former aggravated DUI were affirmed. Defendant's sentence for former reckless homicide was vacated, and the case was remanded for sentencing on the former aggravated DUI charge. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

Smith v. Boudreau


No. 1-04-3175


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


366 Ill. App. 3d 958; 852 N.E.2d 433; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 557; 304 Ill. Dec. 183



June 29, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 17, 2006.
Appeal denied by Smith v. Boudreau, 223 Ill. 2d 686, 865 N.E.2d 977, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 596, 310 Ill. Dec. 257 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Smith v. Boudreau, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 11484 (U.S., Oct. 15, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Kathy M. Flanagan, Judge Presiding.
People v. Smith, 287 Ill. App. 3d 1116, 710 N.E.2d 571, 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 5286, 237 Ill. Dec. 941 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that dismissed plaintiff claimant's amended complaint against defendant, several police detectives and a city, that alleged state and federal violations of the claimant's civil rights. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant sued several police detectives and a city for alleged violations of his state and federal civil rights for allegedly using excessive force or allowing it to be used during an October 1992 interrogation. The trial court in the state and federal civil rights case dismissed his amended complaint, which originally had been filed in July 2003. On appeal, the claimant contended that his state-law claims alleging excessive force were not time barred, that his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims were not time barred, that the city was collaterally estopped from asserting his claims were untimely, and that his claims were timely under the doctrine of equitable tolling. The appellate court found that his excessive force claim did not necessarily undermine the validity of his murder convictions, and, thus, his civil rights claims began to accrue as soon as the alleged use of excessive force occurred; since they were filed 10 years later, they were barred under the applicable two-year limitations period in 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-202 (2004) governing personal injury actions, he was collaterally estopped from relitigating his claims, and equitable tolling did not apply.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1195 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Steele


No. 2-04-0930


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


366 Ill. App. 3d 220; 851 N.E.2d 920; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 553; 303 Ill. Dec. 733



June 28, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Steele, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1756 (Ill., Nov. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. Nos. 03--DT--789, 03--TR--32245, 03--TR--32246, 03--TR--32247. Honorable Gerald M. Zopp, Jr., Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), of numerous traffic offenses, including operating an uninsured vehicle, a violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-707 (2002). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that § 3-707, which defined the offense, contained an unconstitutional mandatory presumption. Specifically, he asserted that language in § 3-707 that stated that a person, such as defendant, who produced in court satisfactory evidence that the vehicle he was operating was insured at the time of his arrest could not be convicted of violating the statute, shifted the burden to defendant to produce evidence of his innocence. The court disagreed, finding § 3-707 to be constitutionally sound. The statutory offense was for the failure to produce evidence of insurance and the only proof necessary was that defendant did not produce such evidence when asked for it. Violation of the statute did not create a presumption that defendant did not have insurance. The saving provision did not shift the burden to defendant to disprove he failed to produce evidence of insurance. Rather, it provided defendant with a way to avoid conviction, a legislative "gift" best described as an act of grace. The procedure allowed by the statute did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

People v. Gariano


No. 1-03-2485


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


366 Ill. App. 3d 379; 852 N.E.2d 344; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 537; 304 Ill. Dec. 94



June 23, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 1, 2006. Released for Publication August 17, 2006. As Corrected September 20, 2006.
Rehearing denied by People v. Gariano, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 771 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Aug. 7, 2006)
Appeal denied by People v. Gariano, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1942 (Ill., Nov. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 25349. Honorable Kenneth J. Wadas, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of five counts of indecent solicitation of a child to commit aggravated criminal sexual abuse. The trial court sentenced defendant to two years of felony probation, sex offender counseling, DNA testing, HIV testing, and sex offender registration. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police investigator, who was monitoring Internet chat rooms, posed as a teenage boy. Defendant contacted the investigator in an Internet chat room through instant messaging. The investigator, without obtaining defendant's consent or obtaining a search warrant, retained transcriptions of defendant's instant messages. The parties agreed by instant message to meet at a bus stop and then go to defendant's apartment to engage in sex. Defendant was arrested when he appeared at the bus stop. Defendant contended that the trial court erred when it denied his motion to suppress the transcriptions of the instant messages. On appeal, the court found that defendant's constitutional protections against the invasion of privacy under U.S. Const. amend IV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 were not offended. Further, the investigator did not intend that his communications with defendant would remain private. Therefore, there was no electronic communication as defined by 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/14-1(e) (2000). Thus, there was no violation of the eavesdropping statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/14-2(a)(1) (2000). Accordingly, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Jones


No. 1-05-0020


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


366 Ill. App. 3d 666; 852 N.E.2d 364; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 531; 304 Ill. Dec. 114



June 23, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 17, 2006.
Appeal denied by, Vacated by People v. Jones, 2007 Ill. LEXIS 534 (Ill., Mar. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Rickey Jones, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to five years' imprisonment and ordered defendant to pay $ 1,224. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the fines and fees imposed by the trial court and contended that the extraction of his blood and perpetual storing of his DNA violated the Fourth Amendment right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures. Among other things, the appellate court concluded that the Spinal Cord Fund fee violated defendant's due process rights because the fee was not reasonably related to the offense for which defendant was convicted. In addition, the Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund penalty was stricken because, under the plain language of 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 240/10(c) (2004), the penalty could only be ordered if no other fine was imposed, and the trial court imposed other fines. Defendant was not, however, entitled to credit toward the fee he was ordered to pay the Trauma Center Fund, as 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 105/27.6(c) (2002) expressly indicated that the fee was not be considered a part of a fine for purposes of any reduction. The appellate court also upheld the order for extraction of defendant's blood and storage of defendant's DNA, finding that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2004) was constitutional as applied to defendant and on its face.


OUTCOME: The Spinal Cord Fund fee and Violent Crime Victims Assistance Fund penalty were stricken. The costs and fees order was amended to reflect a credit of $ 504 for the $ 500 controlled substance assessment and the $ 4 traffic and criminal conviction surcharge. The trial court's order that the $ 5-per-day credit could not be applied to the $ 100 Trauma Center Fund penalty and order regarding the extraction and storing of defendant's DNA were affirmed.

People v. Andrews


No. 3-04-0442


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


365 Ill. App. 3d 696; 850 N.E.2d 888; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 527; 303 Ill. Dec. 83



June 20, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 20, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 9th Judicial Circuit, Knox County, Illinois. 00-CF-462. Honorable Stephen G. Evans Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Sentencing order modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for the 9th Judicial Circuit, Knox County, Illinois, which denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The postconviction motion asserted ineffective assistance of counsel. However, on appeal, the inmate's sole contention was that he should be given one additional day of sentence credit because he was in custody before he was convicted on a charge of aggravated battery for 113 days, not the 112 days he was credited. The State argued that the issue was waived because it was not presented in the original postconviction motion. The court disagreed. 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-3 (2000) stated that any claim of substantial denial of constitutional rights not raised in the original petition was waived. Further, decisions by the Illinois Supreme Court prohibited appellate courts from excusing the failure to raise such issues in an original petition. However, the issue of sentence credit was a statutory right, not a substantial constitutional issue. Thus the prohibition in § 122-3 and the case law did not apply. As it was mandatory under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-7(b) (2000) that credit be given for presentence incarceration, and as the State conceded that the inmate was entitled to the 113 day credit, the court modified the trial court's order to reflect the correct credit.


OUTCOME: The trial court's sentencing order was modified to give the inmate 113 days of presentence credit.

 

1199 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Weger v. Weger (In re T.W.)


NO. 5-06-0019


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


365 Ill. App. 3d 1075; 851 N.E.2d 881; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 526; 303 Ill. Dec. 694



June 19, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected, September 20, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Crawford County. No. 05-MR-4. Honorable Mark L. Shaner, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Crawford County (Illinois), which granted custody of the minor child to petitioner maternal grandparents under the custody provisions of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act (Marriage Act), 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/601 et seq. (2004).


OVERVIEW: The mother of the child had surrendered physical custody of the child to the grandparents in November 2002 when the child was almost four years old. At the time that the grandparents petitioned for custody, the child had not been in the physical custody for either parent for more than two years. The father responded to the petition and also filed a counterpetition for a change of custody. After a bench trial, the trial court awarded custody to the grandparents, finding that they had met their burden of showing good cause to overcome the superior rights of the father. On appeal, the court rejected the father's assertion that In re R.L.S., which addressed procedural and standing requirements under the Probate Act of 1975, 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-5(b) (2004), needed to be incorporated into the Marriage Act in order to protect the rights of the natural parent. The Marriage Act adequately afforded due process protections to natural parents. The court found that there was sufficient evidence to support the award of custody to the grandparents based upon evidence that the child had developed a very close relationship with the grandparents and that the child was well adjusted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1200 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kizer


NO. 4-04-0653


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


365 Ill. App. 3d 949; 851 N.E.2d 266; 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 524; 303 Ill. Dec. 368



June 16, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 25, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Vermilion County. No. 01CF193. Honorable Michael D. Clary, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of driving under the influence of alcohol under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-501(a)(2) (1998), and driving under the influence of alcohol with a blood alcohol content of .08 grams per deciliter or more under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-501(a)(1) (1998). The Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to 18 months' probation and 75 hours' community service. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought dismissal of the charges because the State failed to bring him to trial within 160 days after defendant filed a demand for a speedy trial in a traffic case that had been initiated prior to the instant action. The appellate court concluded that defendant's demand for a speedy trial in the traffic case had no force in the present case because statutory law did not require the State to join the felonies in the instant action with the misdemeanor charged by uniform citation and complaint in the traffic case. Defendant also argued that he was deprived of his constitutional right to due process when the State destroyed blood samples before defendant had the opportunity to have an independent examination made. The appellate court found no error, as defendant failed to prove that the State destroyed the blood samples in bad faith. The admission of evidence of the death of the passenger was not error, but was an indispensable part of a narrative the jury had to hear to determine who was the driver. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol was affirmed, but the conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol with a blood alcohol content of .08 grams per deciliter or more was vacated under the one act, one crime rule.
